Husband's Self-Accusation After Li'an: Hadd and Remarriage
Ruling on consequences if husband admits falsehood after li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband admits falsehood after li'an and explain the proof from Quran 24:4.

Core Idea
Admitting falsehood after li'an triggers the hadd of qadhf and permits remarriage.

Li'an dissolves a marriage when a husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses. But what happens if the husband later confesses he lied? The Hanafi school rules that he must receive eighty lashes (hadd al-qadhf) for his false accusation, and after that, it becomes permissible for him to remarry his former wife. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the Quran, and the conditions that trigger the hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and its ruling
The husband performed li'an with his wife (accused her of zina, swore oaths, and the marriage was dissolved). Later, he admits he was lying. According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling regarding punishment and remarriage?
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites Quran 24:4. Read the verse and understand that it prescribes eighty lashes for anyone who accuses a chaste person of zina without producing four witnesses. How does this apply to the husband after li'an?
The verse is general, but the husband's li'an takes the place of the four witnesses. If he admits falsehood, he effectively fails to produce witnesses, so the hadd applies.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
The imperative 'fajliduhum' (flog them) indicates obligation (wujub). The specified punishment is eighty lashes. Once the husband admits falsehood, he is no longer protected by li'an, so the general rule of qadhf applies.
4
Identify the consequence for remarriage
After receiving the hadd, the husband may remarry his ex-wife because the separation caused by li'an is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce. His admission of falsehood does not automatically restore the marriage, but it removes the prohibition on remarriage.
This contrasts with the case where the husband does not admit falsehood – then the marriage is permanently dissolved and remarriage is not allowed.
5
Compare with cases of other accusations
The passage also mentions that if the husband accused another woman and received hadd for lack of witnesses, he is similarly permitted to remarry his li'an wife. This shows consistency: the hadd removes the legal barrier to remarriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۰۷۰] (۱۲) اگر شوہر لوٹ کر اپنے آپ کی تکذیب کرے تو قاضی اس کو حد لگائے اور اس کے لئے حلال ہے کہ اس عورت سے شادی کرے۔ اسی طرح اگر دوسرے کو تہمت لگائی اور اس کی وجہ سے شوہر کو حد لگ گئی یا عورت نے زنا کروایا اور اس کو حد لگ گئی۔ شوہر نے بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی جس کی وجہ سے لعان کیا اور دونوں کے درمیان تفریق ہوگئی۔ بعد میں شوہر نے اپنے آپ کو جھٹلایا تو قاضی اس کو حد قذف اسی کوڑے لگائے۔ اب اس کے لئے حلال ہے کہ اس بیوی سے شادی کرے۔ اسی طرح اس مرد نے کسی اور عورت کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی اور چار گواہوں سے ثابت نہ کر سکا جس کی وجہ سے اس کو حد قذف لگ گئی تو حد لگنے کے بعد اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ اس بیوی سے دوبارہ شادی کرے جس سے لعان کیا تھا۔
او پر گزر چکا ہے کہ زنا کی تہمت لگانے کے بعد اگر اجمیہ کو بہت لگائی ہے تو اس پر چار گواہ لائیں ورنہ حد قذف لگ جائے گی ۔ اور میاں بیوی لعان کریں۔ یہ لعان چار گواہوں کے درجے میں ہے اسی لئے لعان میں چار مرتبہ قسم کھاتے ہیں۔ اور لعان نہیں کیا یا اپنے آپ کو جھٹلایا تو دونوں صورتوں میں مرد پر حد قذف لگے گی (۲) اس آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ والذين يرمون المحصنات ثم لم يأتوا باربعة شهداء فاجلدوهم ثمانين جلدة ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة ابدا (ب) ( آیت ۴ سورۃ النور ۲۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ تہمت لگانے کے بعد چار گواہ نہ لا سکے تو اس پر اسی کوڑے حد لگے گی (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ ان قبيصة بن ذوء يب كان يحدث عن عمر ابن الخطاب
[2070] (12) If the husband returns and falsifies himself, the qadi imposes hadd on him, and it becomes permissible for him to marry that woman. Similarly, if he accuses another and receives hadd because of it, or if the woman commits zina and receives hadd. The husband accused his wife of zina, which led to li'an, and separation occurred. Later, the husband denied himself, so the qadi imposes the hadd of qadhf (eighty lashes). Now it is permissible for him to marry this wife. Similarly, if this man accused another woman of zina and could not bring four witnesses, thereby receiving hadd of qadhf, then after the hadd, it is permissible for him to remarry the wife with whom he performed li'an.
It has passed earlier that after accusing zina, if he has accused a married woman, he must bring four witnesses, otherwise hadd of qadhf applies. And the spouses perform li'an. Li'an takes the place of four witnesses, which is why they swear four oaths. And if they do not perform li'an or if the husband falsifies himself, in both cases the husband receives hadd of qadhf. (2) There is proof in this verse: And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony. (Quran 24:4) This verse states that if one accuses without four witnesses, he receives eighty lashes. (3) There is an athar that Qubaysa ibn Dhu'ayb narrated from Umar ibn al-Khattab... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage covers the consequence when a husband, after li'an, admits that his accusation was false. He is punished with the hadd of qadhf (eighty lashes) for false accusation, and then it becomes lawful for him to remarry his ex-wife (since the separation was a ba'in divorce). The same applies if he was punished for accusing another woman. The proof is Quran 24:4, which mandates flogging for false accusers. The passage also explains that li'an itself replaces the four witnesses, so if the husband later admits falsehood or avoids li'an, he is liable for hadd. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
حد قذف (hadd al-qadhf): Eighty lashes for false accusation of zina against a chaste person.
تكذيب النفس (takdhib al-nafs): The husband's admission that his li'an accusation was false.
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when husband accuses wife of zina without witnesses; involves oaths and results in permanent separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true according to the Hanafi ruling on a husband who admits falsehood after li'an?
A) He is exempt from punishment because li'an already settled the matter.
B) He receives eighty lashes and can remarry his ex-wife.
C) He must divorce her again before remarrying.
D) He is permanently prohibited from remarrying her.

Key Takeaway
A husband who admits falsehood after li'an must receive the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes), after which he may remarry his former wife.

Li'an and Hadd Waived for Accusing a Minor or Insane Wife
Ruling that accusing a minor or insane wife does not trigger li'an or hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband accuses his minor or insane wife of zina, and explain why li'an and hadd are replaced with ta'zir.

Core Idea
Accusing a minor or insane wife of zina does not trigger li'an or hadd but warrants ta'zir.

The general rule in Islamic law is that a husband who accuses his wife of zina must either produce four witnesses or undergo li'an, and if the accusation is false, he receives the hadd of qadhf. However, this passage from al-Sharh al-Saghir presents an important exception: when the wife is a minor or insane, these fixed procedures and punishments are suspended. The reason is that the wife lacks legal capacity to participate in li'an, and the conditions for qadhf are not met. Instead, the husband is given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) determined by the judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Read the passage to determine what the husband does and what the legal consequence is.
The act is accusing the wife of zina. The ruling: no li'an, no hadd, but ta'zir.
2
Identify the Conditions That Nullify Li'an and Hadd
Find the characteristics of the wife mentioned in the text that trigger the exception.
The wife is a minor (underage) or insane (mentally incapacitated).
3
Understand Why Li'an Is Not Applicable
Li'an requires both spouses to be legally capable of swearing oaths and facing consequences. A minor or insane person lacks such capacity.
Li'an is a mutual oath-taking process; the wife must be able to participate meaningfully.
4
Understand Why Hadd Is Not Applicable
The hadd of qadhf (eighty lashes) requires the accused to be a muhsana (chaste, free, adult, Muslim). A minor or insane wife does not meet this condition.
If the wife is not muhsana, the fixed punishment is not imposed; instead, the judge may apply ta'zir.
5
Determine the Alternative Punishment
The passage states that ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is applied. Note that ta'zir is less severe than hadd and depends on the judge's discretion.
Ta'zir serves as a deterrent while respecting the wife's legal incapacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قذف امرأته وهي صغيرة او مجنونة فلا لعان بينهما ولا حد [۲۰۷۱] (۱۳) اور اگر اپنی بیوی کو تہمت لگائی اس حال میں کہ وہ چھوٹی ہے یا مجنونہ ہے تو ان دونوں کے درمیان لعان نہیں ہے اور نہ حد ہے۔ شوہر نے بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی وہ چھوٹی نابالغہ تھی یا مجنونہ تھی تو اس تہمت کی وجہ سے نہ تو لعان ہوگا اور نہ شوہر کو حد لگے گی البتہ تعزیر ہوگی۔
And if he accuses his wife while she is a minor or insane, then there is no li'an between them and no hadd. [2071] (13) And if he accused his wife while she is a minor or insane, then there is no li'an between them and no hadd. The husband accused his wife of zina while she was a minor (underage) or insane, then due to that accusation neither li'an will occur nor will the husband be given hadd; however, there will be ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that outlines an exception to the rules of li'an and hadd. According to the Hanafi school, if a husband accuses his wife of adultery but she is either a minor (under the age of puberty) or insane (mentally incapacitated), then the procedure of li'an does not apply. The reason is that li'an requires the wife to be a legal subject capable of swearing oaths and facing consequences; a minor or insane person lacks such capacity. Additionally, the hadd of qadhf (eighty lashes) is not imposed on the husband in this case because the accusation is not legally considered as a full qadhf; the wife is not a 'muhsana' (chaste, free, adult, Muslim) which is a condition for qadhf. Instead, the husband is given ta'zir, a discretionary punishment determined by the qadi, which is lighter than hadd and can vary based on the circumstances.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses not covered by fixed hadd or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the punishment for a husband who accuses his minor wife of zina?
A) Hadd of qadhf (80 lashes)
B) Li'an is required
C) Ta'zir (discretionary punishment)
D) No punishment at all

Key Takeaway
Accusing a minor or insane wife of zina exempts the husband from li'an and hadd; he receives ta'zir instead.

Qasamah: Hanafi Ruling, Procedure, and Shafi'i Dispute
Hanafi ruling on qasamah with evidence and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasamah, identify the procedure (who swears, number of oaths, and consequence), and distinguish the Shafi'i position on guardians' oaths.

Core Idea
In unwitnessed homicide, the locality's fifty oaths clear them but incur diyah; the guardian never swears.

Qasamah is a unique institution in Hanafi criminal law where the burden of proof shifts to the community when a body is found with no known killer. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, its proofs from the Sunnah, the procedural details (including refusal and incomplete numbers), and the Shafi'i disagreement about whether the victim's guardians can also swear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is qasamah (القسامة)? It is a set of oaths taken in a case of unwitnessed homicide. The Hanafi ruling is that the people of the locality (أهل المحلة) must swear fifty oaths denying involvement. Their oath is wajib (obligatory) – refusal leads to imprisonment.
The ruling is based on collective responsibility for security.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites several hadith: the Prophet's dealings with the Jews (he made them swear fifty oaths and imposed diyah) and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Sahl. These demonstrate the practice of making the locality swear.
The key hadith: 'فكتبوا يحلفون بالله خمسين يمينا ما قتلناه وما علمنا قاتلا' – they wrote that they swear fifty oaths.
3
Trace the procedure
Fifty men from the locality swear: 'By Allah, we did not kill him, nor do we know his killer.' If they swear, diyah is imposed on the locality. If fewer than fifty, the oaths are repeated until fifty are completed (athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i). If any one refuses, he is imprisoned until he swears.
The guardian (ولي) of the victim is NOT made to swear, nor is a ruling passed against the locality based on the guardian's oath.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if there is any indication (علامة) that the locality killed, the victim's guardians swear fifty oaths against the locality, after which diyah is imposed. The Hanafi school rejects this and requires the locality's own oaths.
The dispute centers on who bears the burden of the oath: the accused locality (Hanafi) or the accuser guardians (Shafi'i).
5
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i dalil
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith of Abdullah ibn Sahl (where the Prophet asked the heirs to swear) as a preliminary inquiry. When the heirs declined, the Prophet did not compel them; instead, he made the locality swear. The default rule is that the locality swears because they are responsible for protection.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on the weight of evidence and the principle of maintaining public order.
6
Examine the rulings on refusal and incomplete numbers
If one person from the locality refuses to swear, he is imprisoned until he complies. If fifty men are not available, the oaths are repeated upon the available men until the count of fifty is reached. These rules ensure the procedure is completed.
These rulings are derived from hadith and athar (statement of Ibrahim).

Source Text

گا۔
محلہ میں قتل ہونے کی وجہ سے مقتول کے وارثین کا حق ہو گیا کہ اہل محلہ کو تم کھلائے ۔ اس لئے اگر وہ قسم نہیں کھاتا ہے تو اس کو قید کیا جائے

So he said to them: 'Do you swear fifty oaths that you will become entitled to your companion?' (a) (Muslim, Book of Qasamah, p. 55, no. 669; and Bukhari, Book of Qasamah, p. 1018, no. 6898). [2408] (2) He swears thus: 'By Allah, we did not kill him, nor do we know his killer.' In a hadith: That the Messenger of Allah sent to the Jews that a slain person has been found among you, so pay his blood-money. So they wrote that they swear by Allah fifty oaths: 'We did not kill him, nor do we know his killer.' He said: 'Then the Messenger of Allah paid the blood-money from his own side, one hundred camels.' (b) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Abandoning Retaliation by Qasamah, p. 274, no. 4525). From this hadith it is understood that the people of the locality, fifty men, swear that neither we killed him nor do we know the killer. Imam Shafi'i's opinion is that if there is any indication that the people of the locality killed him, then the guardian of the slain himself swears fifty times that the people of the locality killed him. Then the blood-money will be imposed on the locality. In the hadith of Abdullah ibn Sahl ibn Zaid, it is similar: The Prophet asked his brothers: 'Do you swear that the Jews killed him?' Upon which they said: 'We do not know for certain that they killed him, so how can we swear?' Then he said: 'Then the Jews will swear and be cleared of the killing.' Again consider the words of the hadith: They mentioned to the Messenger of Allah the killing of Abdullah ibn Sahl. He said to them: 'Will you swear fifty oaths so that you become entitled to your companion or your killer?' They said: 'How can we swear when we did not witness?' (c) (Muslim, Book of Qasamah, p. 55, no. 1669; Abu Dawud, Book of Qasamah, p. 273, no. 4520). From this hadith it is understood that the heirs of the slain themselves swear fifty oaths and impose blood-money on the locality. [2409] (3) So when they swear, the decision of blood-money is made against the people of the locality. From men of the Ansar: The Prophet said to the Jews, starting with them: 'Let fifty men from you swear.' They refused. So he said to the Ansar: 'Become entitled.' They said: 'Should we swear about the unseen, O Messenger of Allah?' So the Messenger of Allah placed the blood-money on the Jews because the slain was found among them. (w) (Footnote (a): He said to them: Can you swear fifty oaths so that you become entitled to your slain? (b) He made the Jews swear: A slain person was found among you, so pay his ransom. So the Jews wrote that they swear fifty men that we did not kill him nor know his killer. Then the Prophet paid one hundred camels from his own side. (c) People mentioned the killing of Abdullah ibn Sahl to the Prophet, so he said to them: Will you swear fifty times to become entitled to the slain or the killer? They said: How can we swear when we were not present at the time of killing? (1) The Prophet said to the Jews, starting with them: Let fifty men from you swear. They refused. So he said to the Ansar: You become entitled by swearing. They said: O Messenger of Allah! Should we swear about the unseen? From this hadith it is understood that blood-money is imposed on the people of the locality because the corpse was found among them. Therefore, apparently they are the criminals because they did not protect the locality. (2) If blood-money is not imposed on anyone, the people of the locality will not protect against killing and blood will go in vain. (3) In a hadith: Ibn Abbas said: A man of the Ansar was found slain in a date-palm garden of some Jews. The Messenger of Allah sent to them and took from them fifty of their best men and made them swear: 'By Allah, we did not kill nor do we know the killer.' And he imposed blood-money on them. They said: 'He judged with what our Prophet Moses used to judge among us.' (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Book of Qasamah, vol. 8, p. 213, no. 16447). From this hadith it is understood that the people of the locality are made to swear, then blood-money is imposed on them. 2410] (4) And the guardian is not made to swear, nor is a ruling of injury passed against him even if he swears. A hadith has passed that the oath is taken from the people of the locality. Therefore, with us, the oath is not taken from the guardian of the slain. And even if he swears, the ruling of injury is not passed against the locality until fifty men of the locality swear. It has passed earlier that if there is an indication of killing among the locality, then the guardians of the slain swear fifty times, then blood-money is decided on the locality. This is the school of Imam Shafi'i. [2411] (5) If one of the people of the locality refuses to swear, he is imprisoned until he swears. If anyone from the locality refuses to swear, he is imprisoned until he swears. Because of the killing in the locality, the heirs of the slain have a right to make the locality swear. So if he does not swear, he is imprisoned. [2412] (6) If fifty are not complete from the people of the locality, then oaths are repeated upon them until fifty oaths are completed. In an athar: Ibrahim said: 'If they do not complete fifty, the oaths are repeated upon them.' (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Book of Qasamah, vol. 10, p. 411, no. 18285; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 167, Chapter on Qasamah, vol. 5, p. 440, no. 27803). From this athar it is understood that fifty... Footnote (a): Ibn Abbas narrates that a man of the Ansar was found slain in a date-palm garden of some Jews. The Prophet sent to them, took fifty of their good men, and made them swear: 'By Allah, we did not kill nor do we know the killer.' And he imposed blood-money on them. They said: 'This is the same judgement that our Prophet Moses used to make among us.' (b) Ibrahim said: 'If they do not complete fifty, oaths are repeated upon them.'
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri presents the Hanafi doctrine of qasamah (oaths in unwitnessed homicide) and contrasts it with the Shafi'i school. The passage is a legal exposition (sharh) that cites multiple hadith and a statement from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i to establish the rulings. The Hanafi position, based on the hadith of the Prophet's dealings with the Jews and the Ansar, is that when a corpse is found in a locality with no known killer, the people of that locality (ahl al-mahallah) must swear fifty oaths that they did not kill the victim and do not know the killer. This oath is taken from fifty men of the locality if available; if less, the oaths are repeated until fifty are completed (a ruling from Ibrahim). The purpose is to avoid bloodshed and ensure protection of the locality. Once they swear, blood-money (diyah) is imposed on them. The guardian (wali) of the victim is NOT made to swear, and even if he swears, no liability is fixed on the locality until fifty of the locality swear. The author then mentions Imam Shafi'i's view: if there is circumstantial evidence (indication) that the locality killed, then the victim's guardians swear fifty oaths against the locality, after which blood-money is imposed. The Hanafi school rejects this and requires the locality's own oaths, as per the practice of the Prophet. The passage also rules that if any one of the locality refuses to swear, he is imprisoned until he complies. This is because the heirs have a right to clear the locality of suspicion. The overall ruling is part of the Hanafi criminal law system, emphasizing collective responsibility for security within a locality.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasamah): Oaths taken in a case of unwitnessed homicide, where the locality swears to deny involvement, leading to payment of diyah.
ولي (wali): The guardian or heir of the victim who has the right to pursue blood-money or retaliation.
دية (diyah): Blood-money, a financial compensation paid to the victim's heirs in homicide cases where retaliation is not applicable or is waived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what happens if one of the fifty men from the locality refuses to swear in a qasamah case?
A) The case is dismissed
B) The victim's family receives diyah directly
C) The refusing individual is imprisoned until he swears
D) The judge appoints a substitute

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qasamah, the burden of proof is on the locality to swear innocence; their oath imposes diyah on them, and refusal leads to imprisonment.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Minimum Amount the 'Aqila Must Bear
Ruling on minimum diyah amount the 'aqila must pay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum diyah amount the 'aqila must bear in Hanafi fiqh and identify the proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
The 'aqila only pays diyah if the amount is at least 1/20 (500 dirhams); anything less is on the offender.

The 'aqila (clan/helpers) is responsible for diyah in accidental killing, but only above a minimum threshold. This lesson establishes that threshold as half of one-tenth (nisf 'ushr) of the full diyah, i.e., 500 dirhams or 5 camels. The proofs come from the well-known hadith of the two women of Hudhayl and the athar of Ibrahim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the 'aqila bearing diyah. The ruling: wajib when the diyah is 1/20 or more.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith of Abu Hurairah about two women of Hudhayl, and the athar of Ibrahim from Musannaf Abdurrazzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet imposed a ghurrah (slave) worth 500 dirhams on the 'aqila. 500 dirhams is exactly 1/20 of the full diyah (10,000 dirhams).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This is a settled Hanafi position; some schools may have different thresholds, but the Hanafi proof is strong.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
If the diyah is less than 500 dirhams, the offender pays from his own wealth; the 'aqila is not liable.

الا الله قال الغرة خمس مائة يعني درهما، قال ابو داؤد قال ربيعة الغرة خمسون دينارا (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب دیته الجنین ص ۱۴۸ نمبر۰ ۴۵۸ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام کی قیمت پانچ سو درہم ہو۔ پانچ سو درہم پوری دیت دس ہزار درہم کا بیسواں حصہ ہوا اور یہ رقم اوپر کی حدیث میں عاقلہ پر لازم کی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عاقلہ بیسواں حصہ یا اس سے زیادہ کی رقم برداشت کریں گے اس سے کم کی رقم نہیں (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عـن ابـراهيـم قال لا تعقل العاقلة في ادنى من الموضحة قال محمد و به ناخذ (ب) کتاب الآثار الامام محمد ، باب دیۃ الخطاء وما تعقل العاقلة ص ۱۲۴ نمبر ۵۷۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ موضحہ زخم سے کم کی دیت عاقلہ برداشت نہیں کریں گے۔ اور موضحہ کی قیمت پوری دیت کا بیسواں حصہ پانچ اونٹ ہیں۔ وفی الموضحة خمس (ج) ( نسائی شریف، ذکر حدیث عمر بن حزم ص ۶۶۹ نمبر ۴۸۶۰) نصف عشر : پوری دیت کا دسواں حصہ اور اس حصے کا بھی آدھا تو پوری دیت کا بیسواں حصہ ہوا۔
And the 'aqila does not bear less than half of one-tenth of the diyah, and bears half of one-tenth and above, and what is less than that is from the wealth of the offender. Because the mawla al-muwalah becomes his tribe and family. Therefore the mawla al-muwalah and his tribe will pay the diyah. (2) In an athar: From Ibrahim regarding a man who enters into wala' with a man and then accepts Islam at his hands, he said: He pays the 'aql for him and inherits from him. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq) This athar shows that the mawla al-muwalah and his tribe pay the diyah, and if there is no dhu rahim mahram, they also inherit. (2) Also in hadith: From Tamim al-Dari marfu': He is the most entitled to the person in his life and after his death. (Bukhari) This hadith also shows that the mawla al-muwalah accompanies him in grief and joy in life and after death, meaning if he has no one from his own family, they pay the diyah. [2439] (9) The 'aqila does not bear less than one-twentieth of the diyah, and bears one-twentieth or more, and what is less than that is from the wealth of the offender. The full diyah for accidental killing etc. is ten thousand dirhams; its one-twentieth is five hundred dirhams. If the amount due is five hundred dirhams or more, the 'aqila can bear it. But if the accidental killing involves a diyah less than five hundred dirhams, the 'aqila does not bear it; the offender himself must pay. There is a repeated report in hadith about the woman of Banu Lihyan who was struck on her belly causing her unborn child to die; the Prophet (peace be upon him) imposed a ghurrah (a slave) for the child. In Abu Dawud, the value of that ghurrah is five hundred dirhams, which is one-twentieth of the full diyah of ten thousand dirhams. And in Bukhari's hadith, it is stated that this was accidental killing, so this diyah is borne by the 'aqila of the woman who struck. From this it is known that the 'aqila bears one-twentieth (five hundred dirhams) or more, but not less, because there is no evidence for less. The proof that a slave was imposed for the child and its diyah was on the 'asaba is the hadith of Abu Hurairah: Two women of Hudhayl fought, one struck the other with a stone killing her and what was in her womb; they brought the case to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he judged that the diyah for the fetus is a male or female slave, and the diyah for the woman is on her 'aqila. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, the value of the slave was made liable on the 'aqila and 'asaba of the woman who struck, and the value of the slave is five hundred dirhams, as confirmed in Abu Dawud: from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The ghurrah is five hundred dirhams.' And Abu Dawud also narrated that Rabi'ah said the ghurrah is fifty dinars. This athar shows that the value of the slave is five hundred dirhams, which is one-twentieth of the full diyah, and this amount was made liable on the 'aqila in the above hadith, establishing that the 'aqila bears one-twentieth or more, not less. (3) In an athar: From Ibrahim: 'The 'aqila does not bear for less than a mawdihah (wound that exposes bone).' Muhammad said: 'And we adopt this.' (Kitab al-Athar) This athar shows that the 'aqila does not bear diyah for less than a mawdihah, and the diyah for a mawdihah is five camels, which is one-twentieth of the full diyah. Also: 'And for the mawdihah, five (camels).' (Nasa'i) Half of one-tenth: one-tenth of the full diyah, and half of that is one-twentieth.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from hadith and athar regarding the minimum amount of diyah that the 'aqila (the clan/helpers) must bear in cases of accidental killing (qatl al-khata'). The ruling: The 'aqila is only liable for an amount equal to or greater than half of one-tenth (nisf 'ushr) of the full diyah, i.e., 1/20 = 500 dirhams (or 5 camels). If the diyah is less than that, it falls on the offender's own wealth. The proof comes from the incident of two women from Hudhayl and the Prophet's verdict that the diyah for a fetus (ghurrah) is a slave worth 500 dirhams, and that the 'aqila of the woman who struck bore that. Also the athar from Ibrahim that the 'aqila does not bear for less than a mawdihah (a wound that lays bare the bone), whose diyah is also 500 dirhams/5 camels. Thus the Hanafi position is firmly established: the 'aqila's liability begins at this threshold.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('Aqila): The clan, tribe, or helpers (asabah) who are obliged to pay diyah on behalf of a member who commits accidental killing.
دية (Diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide or bodily harm.
نصف عشر (Nisf 'Ushr): Half of one-tenth; i.e., one-twentieth (1/20) of the diyah, which is 500 dirhams or 5 camels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount of diyah that the 'aqila must bear in Hanafi fiqh?
A) One-twentieth of the full diyah (500 dirhams)
B) One-tenth of the full diyah (1000 dirhams)
C) One-fourth of the full diyah (2500 dirhams)
D) Any amount, regardless of size

Key Takeaway
The 'aqila's liability for diyah in accidental killing starts at one-twentieth (500 dirhams/5 camels); smaller amounts are the offender's personal responsibility.

Zina is Proven by Four Witnesses or Four Confessions
Ruling with proof: zina is proven by bayyinah (four witnesses) or iqrar (four confessions).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods by which zina is proven in Hanafi law and explain the Islamic legal proofs for the requirement of four witnesses and four confessions.

Core Idea
Zina is proven only by four male witnesses or four confessions; anything less is insufficient for the hadd punishment.

Zina is one of the most serious offenses in Islamic law, carrying severe punishments. However, the law does not allow these punishments to be applied lightly. This lesson examines the strict evidentiary requirements established by the Quran and Sunnah: either four male eyewitnesses or four separate confessions from the accused. Understanding these conditions is essential to ensure that the hadd is applied only when the proof is unequivocal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods of proof
The text states that zina is proven by 'bayyinah' (evidence) and 'iqrar' (confession). Bayyinah here specifically means four male witnesses. Iqrar means the accused's confession, which must be made four times in court.
Other schools may accept fewer confessions, but Hanafi strictly requires four.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence for four witnesses
The author quotes three verses: (1) al-Nur:2 commands flogging for zina, (2) al-Nur:4 prescribes flogging for false accusation unless four witnesses are produced, and (3) al-Nisa:15 requires four witnesses for lewdness. These verses collectively establish that zina cannot be proven without four witnesses.
The imperative 'fajlidū' (flog) and the condition of four witnesses in al-Nur:4 are key.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence for four confessions
The hadith of Ma'iz (from Abu Hurairah) shows that the Prophet turned away from the man until he confessed four times. Only after the fourth confession did the Prophet order stoning. This demonstrates the requirement of four separate confessions.
The hadith also checks for insanity and muhsan status, showing additional safeguards.
4
Note the conditions for witnesses and effect of confession
The commentary mentions that witnesses must be male and must meet certain conditions. If they testify, the hadd is applied. If the accused confesses four times, hadd is also applied. The footnote clarifies that for a muhsan (married, free adult), the punishment is stoning.
The conditions for witnesses include being 'adl (upright) and directly observing the act.

From Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, volume 3, p. 364. Book of Hudud. 2444 (1) Zina is proven by evidence (bayyinah) and confession (iqrar). (Book of Hudud) Necessary note: Hud means prevention; because when the hadd is applied, a person refrains from sins, hence it is called hadd. This is the chapter of the hadd of zina. Therefore, for its proof, it is necessary that the person himself confess to committing zina four times, or four men testify that so-and-so committed zina. The proof is: 'The fornicatress and the fornicator, flog each one of them a hundred stripes, and let not pity for them overtake you in the religion of Allah' (Surah al-Nur:2). 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses, flog them eighty stripes and never accept their testimony' (Surah al-Nur:4). From this verse it is understood that four witnesses are required for proof. 'And those who commit lewdness from among your women, call four witnesses from among you; if they testify, then confine them in their houses until death overtakes them or Allah makes a way for them' (Surah al-Nisa:15). From this verse also it is understood that four witnesses are required for proof of zina. And the hadith proves this: from Abu Hurairah: A man came to the Messenger of Allah while he was in the mosque and called out, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina.' The Prophet turned away from him until he repeated it four times. When he testified against himself four times, the Prophet called him and said, 'Are you insane?' He said, 'No.' He said, 'Are you muhsan (married)?' He said, 'Yes.' Then the Prophet said, 'Take him away and stone him.' (Bukhari, chapter: Do not stone the insane, hadith no. 2815; Muslim, chapter: On the one who confesses to zina, p. 66, no. 1992). From this hadith, knowledge of zina and its rulings is obtained. [2444] (1) Zina is proven by testimony and confession. If someone committed zina, and the fornicator himself does not confess, but four men testify that he committed zina with a certain woman, then zina is established and the hadd will be applied to the man. However, there are several conditions for these witnesses that must be fulfilled. The second scenario is that the fornicator himself confesses, saying 'I committed zina,' and he confesses four times, then the hadd will be applied to him. If he is muhsan, then he will be stoned. Footnote: (a) The fornicator man and fornicatress woman, each flog a hundred stripes and let not pity overtake you in the religion of Allah. (b) Those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses, flog them eighty stripes and never accept their testimony. (c) As for your women who commit lewdness, call four witnesses from among you; if they testify, then confine them in their houses until death overtakes them or Allah makes a way for them. Note: Later the way of li'an was made. (d) A man came to the Prophet, while he was in the mosque, and called out: O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina. The Prophet turned away from him until he returned it four times. When he testified against himself four times, the Prophet called him and asked: Are you insane? He said: No. He asked: Are you muhsan? He said: Yes. The Prophet said: Take him away and stone him.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hudud with the ruling that zina is proven by bayyinah (four witnesses) or iqrar (four confessions). The author first provides a necessary note explaining the meaning of hadd as prevention. Then he quotes three Quranic verses (al-Nur:2, al-Nur:4, al-Nisa:15) to establish that four witnesses are required. The hadith of Ma'iz shows that four confessions are required. The ruling is then elaborated: if four witnesses testify, the hadd is applied; if the person confesses four times, the hadd is applied. The note at the end mentions that if the person is muhsan (free, married, adult Muslim), the punishment is stoning. The passage carefully follows the sequential reasoning from Quran and Sunnah to the ruling.

Key Terms
الزنا (al-zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other and where there is no legal impediment.
البينة (al-bayyinah): In this context, it refers to four male witnesses who directly testify to having seen the act of penetration.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession of the accused; for zina, it must be made four separate times in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, zina is proven only through four male witnesses or four confessions, as established by clear Quranic verses and the practice of the Prophet.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Proof of Zina: Evidence and Confession
States the two methods of proving zina in Hanafi law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of proving zina in Hanafi law and explain why four witnesses or four confessions are required.

Core Idea
Zina is proven exclusively by four male witnesses or four confessions — neither alone suffices without repetition.

In Hanafi criminal law, the punishment for zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) is severe, but so are the evidentiary requirements to protect against false accusations. This passage from Al-Sameri establishes the two exclusive modes of proof: bayyinah (four male witnesses) and iqrar (four separate confessions). Understanding these strict standards is essential because they safeguard the integrity of the hudud penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of proof
Recognize that zina is proven only through bayyinah (four witnesses) or iqrar (four confessions). This is a foundational principle in Hanafi hudud.
No other methods, such as forensic evidence, are accepted for hadd.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence for bayyinah
Analyze verses from Surah An-Nur (24:2, 24:4) and Surah An-Nisa (4:15). The imperative 'fajlidu' indicates obligation, and the requirement of four witnesses is explicit in verse 4:15.
The verses also warn against false accusations.
3
Understand the hadith on iqrar
Study the hadith of Ma'iz: the Prophet turned away until the fourth confession. This establishes the requirement of four separate confessions.
The Prophet also checked sanity and muhsan status before ordering punishment.
4
Apply the distinction between muhsan and ghayr muhsan
Note that the punishment differs: stoning (rajm) for muhsan (married, free, had consummated marriage) and 100 lashes for non-muhsan.
The passage ends by mentioning this distinction for the confession case.
5
Compare with other schools
Be aware that Shafi'is accept a single confession. Understand why Hanafis insist on four based on the explicit sunnah of the Prophet.
This is a key point of ikhtilaf.

كتاب الحدود 

۲۴۴۴ (۱) الزنا يثبت بالبيئة والاقرار.

ضروری نوٹ حد کے معنی ہیں روکنا ، حد لگنے سے آدمی گناہوں سے رکھتا ہے اس لئے اس کو حد کہتے ہیں۔ یہ باب حد زنا کا ہے اس لئے اس کے ثبوت کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ خود چار مرتبہ زنا کرنے کا اقرار کرے یا چار آدمی گواہی دے کہ فلاں نے زنا کیا ہے۔ ثبوت یہ ہے۔ الزانية والزاني فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة ولا تأخذكم بهما رأفة فى دين الله (الف) (آیت ۲ سورۃ النور (۲۴) (۲) والذين يرمون المحصنات ثم لم يأتوا باربعة شهداء فاجلدوهم ثمانين جلدة ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة ابدا (ب)( آيت ۴ سورۃ النور ۲۴) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ ثبوت کے لئے چار گواہ چاہئے ۔ والتي يأتين الفاحشة من نسائكم فاستشهدوا عليهن اربعة منكم فان شهدوا فامسكوهن في البيوت حتى يتوفهن الموت او يجعل الله لهن سبيلا (ج) ( آیت ۵ اسورة النساء۴) اس آیت سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ زنا کے ثبوت کے لئے چار گواہ چاہئے۔
اور اس حدیث سے اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرۃ قال اتى رجل رسول الله الا الله وهو في المسجد فناداه فقال يا رسول الله اني زنیت فاعرض عنه حتى ردد عليه اربع مرات فلما شهد على نفسه اربع شهادات دعاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال ایک جنون؟ قال لا! قال فهل احصنت؟ قال نعم ! فقال النبي عل له اذهبوا به فارجموه (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب لا یر حجم الجون الجهوری ۲۰۰۶ نمبر ۲۸۱۵ مسلم شریف، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۹۹۲) اس حدیث سے زنا اور اس کے احکام کا علم ہوا۔
[۲۴۴۴] (۱) زنا ثابت ہوتا ہے گواہی سے اور اقرار ہے۔ کسی نے زنا کیا، خود زنا کرنے والا اقرار نہیں کرتا لیکن چار آدمیوں نے گواہی دی کہ اس نے فلاں عورت کے ساتھ زنا کیا ہے تو زنا ثابت ہو جائے گا اور مرد پر حد لگے گی۔ لیکن ان گواہوں کے لئے بھی کئی شرطیں ہیں جن کا پورا کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ زنا کرنے والا خود اقرار کرے کہ میں نے زنا کیا ہے۔ اور چار مرتبہ اقرار کرے تب جا کر اس پر حد جاری ہوگی۔ اگر وہ محصن ہے تو رحیم ہوگا اور
The book of prescribed punishments. 2444 (1) Zina is proven by evidence and confession. Essential note: The meaning of 'hadd' is prevention; by prescribing a punishment, a person is restrained from sins, hence it is called 'hadd'. This chapter is on the punishment for zina. Therefore, for its establishment, it is essential that the person himself confesses to committing zina four times, or four men give testimony that so-and-so committed zina. Its proof is: 'The fornicator and the fornicatress, flog each of them with a hundred lashes, and let not compassion for them take hold of you in the religion of Allah' (Surah An-Nur 24:2). 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes and never accept their testimony forever' (Surah An-Nur 24:4). From this verse it is learned that for proof, four witnesses are required. 'And those who commit immoral acts from among your women, call to witness against them four of you. So if they bear witness, then confine them to houses until death takes them or Allah makes for them a way' (Surah An-Nisa 4:15). From this verse also it is learned that for the proof of zina, four witnesses are required. And its proof is from this hadith: From Abu Huraira who said: A man came to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, while he was in the mosque and called out to him: 'O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina.' So the Prophet turned away from him until he repeated it four times. When he bore witness against himself four times, the Prophet called him and asked: 'Do you have madness?' He said: 'No.' He asked: 'Are you muhsan?' He said: 'Yes.' Then the Prophet said: 'Take him away and stone him.' (Bukhari and Muslim). From this hadith, knowledge of zina and its rulings is gained. [2444] (1) Zina is established by testimony and confession. If a person commits zina and he himself does not confess, but four men testify that he committed zina with a certain woman, then zina will be established and the punishment will be applied to the man. However, there are several conditions for these witnesses that must be fulfilled. The second scenario is that the person who committed zina himself confesses that he committed zina, and he confesses four times, then only will the punishment be inflicted on him. If he is muhsan, then he will be stoned, and
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, opening the chapter on hudud (prescribed punishments) for zina. The author begins by defining 'hadd' as a deterrent punishment (literally 'prevention') that protects the community from sin. The main ruling is that zina—unlawful sexual intercourse—is proven through two means only: (1) bayyinah, meaning the testimony of four male witnesses, and (2) iqrar, meaning the confession of the accused repeated four times. The proof is drawn from Surah An-Nur verse 2, which mandates flogging for fornicators, and verses 4 and 15 of Surah An-Nur and Surah An-Nisa respectively, which require four witnesses for any accusation of zina. Additionally, the hadith of the man (known as Ma'iz) who confessed four times to the Prophet is cited: the Prophet initially turned away, and only after the fourth confession did he establish the conditions of sanity and muhsan status (i.e., the offender being married free and having had lawful sexual relations) before ordering stoning. The commentary emphasizes that the witnesses themselves have conditions (like being male, free, just, and seeing the act of penetration directly) and that a confession must be explicit and repeated four times without retraction. The ruling distinguishes between muhsan (married, free, and had consummated marriage) offenders who are stoned to death and non-muhsan offenders who receive 100 lashes.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed, prescribed punishment for crimes against public order and morals, such as zina, theft, and drinking wine.
بيئة (bayyinah): In this context, it specifically means the testimony of four male witnesses confirming the act of zina.
اقرار (iqrar): A confession by the accused, which must be made on four separate occasions and with explicit details.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, zina is only proven by four male witnesses or four separate confessions, reflecting a strict evidentiary standard to protect against false accusations.

Four Male Witnesses for Zina: Proofs and Requirements
Explains the requirement of four male witnesses and their qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and hadith evidence for requiring four male witnesses in zina cases and explain why the gender requirement is derived from the pronoun 'minkum'.

Core Idea
Zina requires four male eyewitnesses — the Quranic 'arba'ah minkum' sets both the number and the gender.

The hadd punishment for zina is severe, so Islamic law demands an exceptionally high standard of proof. This passage examines the requirement of four male witnesses, citing direct Quranic and prophetic texts. Understanding this condition is essential for correctly applying hudud law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The passage discusses the evidence (bayyinah) required to prove zina, not the act itself. The ruling is that zina can only be proven by the testimony of four witnesses.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: Quran 4:15 and the hadith of Sa'id ibn 'Ubada. Identify the specific texts and their sources.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove the requirement? The phrase 'arba'ah minkum' (four from among you) explicitly mandates four witnesses. The masculine pronoun 'minkum' indicates male witnesses.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Are there other opinions? Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) accept female witnesses in some cases. The Hanafi school rejects this based on the masculine pronoun.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and is based on the clear text of the Quran.

Source Text

[ ۲۴۴۵) (۲) پس بعینہ کی شکل یہ ہے کہ گواہی دیں چار گواہ مرد پر یا عورت پر زنا کی ۔ چار گواہ کسی مرد یا عورت پر گواہی دیں کہ انہوں نے زنا کیا ہے تو زنا ثابت ہوگا۔
زنا میں چار گواہوں کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے کہ اس کی جان جائے گی۔ اور قرآن میں بھی ہے کہ ثبوت کے لئے چار گواہ چاہئے (۲)

[2445] (2) So the evidence is that four witnesses testify against a man and a woman for zina. [2445] (2) So the form of the evidence is that four witnesses give testimony against a man or a woman for zina. Four witnesses testify against some man or woman that they committed zina, then zina will be established. The need for four witnesses in zina is because the punishment involves loss of life. So if they bear witness, then confine them to houses' (Surah An-Nisa 4:15). From this verse it is learned that four witnesses are required. And in the hadith: Sa'id ibn 'Ubada said: O Messenger of Allah, if I find a man with my wife, should I wait until I bring four witnesses? He said: Yes. (Muslim). From this verse and hadith it is learned that to prove zina, four witnesses are required. And in the verse, since the pronoun 'minkum' is masculine, all four witnesses must be men.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage expands on the requirement of bayyinah (evidence) for proving zina. The author specifies that the evidence must consist of four witnesses (shuhud) who testify against a specific man and woman. The Urdu commentary clarifies that four witnesses must testify that they saw the act of zina. The rationale given is that the punishment (stoning or flogging) is severe, involving potential loss of life, so strict proof is required. Two proofs are cited: first, Surah An-Nisa 4:15, which requires four witnesses for any accusation of illegal sexual intercourse (fahishah); second, the hadith of Sa'id ibn 'Ubada, where the Prophet confirmed that even if one finds a man with his wife, he must produce four witnesses before any legal action. A key point derived from the verse is the masculine pronoun 'minkum' (from among you), which indicates that all four witnesses must be male. This distinguishes the Hanafi position from schools that might allow female witnesses in some cases. The passage thus establishes that both the number and gender of witnesses are fixed: four male witnesses of upright character (adl) who saw the act of penetration directly.

Key Terms
شاهد (shahid): A witness in a zina case; must be a male adult, free, just, and testifying to the specific act of penetration.
بيئة (bayyinah): In this passage, bayyinah refers specifically to the testimony of four male witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic command for four male witnesses in zina is a strict condition for proving the crime, ensuring that severe punishments are not applied lightly.

The Imam's Interrogation to Avert Hadd
Ruling with proof on judicial interrogation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the imam must thoroughly interrogate witnesses in a zina case and apply the principle of dar' al-hudud to identify when the hadd is averted.

Core Idea
The imam's investigation prioritizes averting punishment over applying it.

When witnesses testify to zina, the Hanafi school requires the imam to go beyond a simple acceptance of testimony. He must actively interrogate the witnesses about the nature, time, place, and partner of the alleged act. This interrogation serves not just to confirm the truth but also to uncover any doubt that would block the hadd penalty. This lesson unpacks the procedure and the underlying principle from a key hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that the imam must ask the witnesses detailed questions about the zina. This is an obligation (wajib) on the judge.
The ruling is procedural, not about the act of zina itself.
2
Understand the purpose
Two reasons are given: to discover the truth and to find grounds to avert the hadd. The second is paramount.
Averting hadd is a core Hanafi principle.
3
Examine the proof
The hadith from Aisha commands: 'Avert the prescribed punishments as much as you can...' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is ahad but relied upon for this ruling.
4
Apply the principle of dar' al-hudud
The interrogation can reveal shubhah, which then blocks the hadd. The judge is instructed to err on the side of pardon.
This reflects the maxim: 'Hadd is averted by doubts.'
5
Note the practical consequence
If any inconsistency or lack of clarity arises from the witnesses, the hadd is not applied. The imam must actively seek such ambiguity.
Cross-madhhab: Some schools may not require such extensive questioning.

[ ۲۴۴۶] (۳) امام گواہوں سے پوچھیں گے زنا کے بارے میں کہ زنا کیا ہے؟ کس طرح ہوتا ہے؟ زنا کہاں کیا ہے؟ کب کیا ہے؟ کس کے ساتھ کیا ہے؟
تشریح گواہ زنا کی گواہی دیدے تو امام گواہوں سے پوری تحقیق کریں گے تا کہ حقیقت ظاہر ہو جائے کہ واقعی زنا ہوا ہے یا نہیں۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ جہاں تک ہو سکے حد کو ساقط کی جائے ۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الا الله ادرئوا الحدود عن المسلمين ما استطعتم فان كان له مخرج فخلوا سبيله فان الامام ان يخطئ في العفو خير من ان يخطئ في العقوبة (ج) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی درء الحدود ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۱۴۲۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں تک ہو سکے حدود کو شبہ کی بنا پر ساقط کی جائے۔ گواہوں سے زنا کے بارے میں پوچھے کہ زنا کیا ہے؟ یعنی جو کام اپنی بیوی سے حلال کے طور پر کرتا ہے وہی کام اجتنبیہ عورت سے حرام کے طور پر کرنے کو کہتے ہیں ۔ گواہ اس حقیقت کو جانتا ہو۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ انه سمع أبا هريرة يقول جاء الاسلمى الى نبى الله الله فشهد على نفسه انه اصاب امرأة حراما اربع مرات كل ذلك يعرض عنه النبي الا الله فاقبل في الخامسة فقال انكتها ؟ قال نعم قال حتى غاب ذلك
[2446] (3) Then the imam asks the witnesses about zina: what is it, how is it, where did the zina take place, when did the zina happen, and with whom did the zina occur? [2446] (3) The imam will ask the witnesses about zina: what is zina? How does it occur? Where did the zina take place? When did it take place? With whom did it take place? Explanation: When the witnesses give testimony of zina, the imam will thoroughly investigate the witnesses so that the truth becomes apparent as to whether zina actually occurred or not. The second reason is that the hadd punishment should be averted as much as possible. From Aisha who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Avert the prescribed punishments from the Muslims as much as you can. If there is any way out, let him go free, for the imam making a mistake in pardoning is better than making a mistake in punishing.' (Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is learned that as much as possible, the prescribed punishments should be averted due to doubt. Ask the witnesses about zina: what is zina? That is, the act that one does with his wife lawfully, doing the same with a forbidden woman unlawfully is called zina. The witness must know this reality. In a hadith: He heard Abu Huraira say: The Aslami came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and testified against himself four times that he had committed an unlawful act with a woman. Each time the Prophet turned away from him. Then on the fifth time he came forward and asked: 'Did you have intercourse with her?' He said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Until that [private part] disappeared...'
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage outlines the procedure the imam (judge) must follow when witnesses testify to zina. The imam is required to interrogate the witnesses in detail, asking about the definition of zina, the manner, the location, the time, and the identity of the partner. The commentary explains that this thorough questioning serves two purposes: first, to uncover the truth and confirm that the act indeed occurred; second, to find any grounds for doubt (shubha) that would allow the hadd punishment to be averted. This is based on the famous hadith narrated by Aisha: 'Avert the prescribed punishments as much as you can; if there is any way out, let him go free, for the imam making a mistake in pardoning is better than making a mistake in punishing.' This reflects the general Hanafi principle of dar' al-hudud (averting hadd punishments) in cases of doubt. The commentary further defines zina as the act of intercourse that is halal with one's wife but becomes haram with a woman who is not permissible. The witness must understand this definition clearly. The passage also begins a hadith about a man from Aslam who confessed repeatedly, but the text is incomplete at the end of the page. The key takeaway is that the imam's role includes active scrutiny to minimize punishment, not merely to apply it mechanically.

Key Terms
درء الحدود (dar' al-hudud): The principle of averting hadd punishments in cases of doubt or ambiguity.
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary purpose of the imam's detailed questioning of witnesses in a zina case?
A) To confirm the witnesses' integrity
B) To find grounds to avert the hadd punishment
C) To intimidate the witnesses
D) To document the crime for public record

Key Takeaway
The imam must actively seek doubt through interrogation to avoid applying hadd punishment unjustly.

Proof of Zina through Four Male Witnesses
Procedure for proving zina through four male witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for proving zina through witness testimony, including the number of witnesses, their gender, the explicit description required, and the imam's role in cross-examination.

Core Idea
Four male witnesses, explicit testimony, and thorough questioning: the Hanafi path to proving zina, with every ambiguity averting the punishment.

This lesson explains the strict rules for establishing zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) through witness testimony in Hanafi law. Drawing from the Quranic verse (4:15) and prophetic hadiths, the Hanafi school requires four male witnesses who must describe the act in explicit detail. The imam (judge) must cross-examine them to eliminate any doubt, as the principle of dar' al-hudud (averting punishments) demands that penalties be dropped if uncertainty remains.

Guided Path
1
State the requirement for witnesses
From the Quran (4:15) and hadith, identify that four male witnesses are needed. Note the masculine pronoun 'minkum' indicates males.
2
Understand the role of the imam
The imam must ask the witnesses about the nature, location, time, and person involved. This cross-examination ensures truth and finds doubts that avert punishment.
3
Define explicit testimony
Witnesses must describe the act explicitly using clear language, e.g., 'like the pencil entering the kohl container.' Allusions are not accepted.
4
Apply the principle of dar' al-hudud
If any discrepancy arises—such as disagreement on location—the punishment is averted. This reflects the Hanafi preference for mercy in hudud cases.

[2445] (2) فالبينة ان تشهد اربعة من الشهود على رجل وامرأة بالزنا [2446] (3) فسألهم الامام عن الزنا ماهو وكيف هو و این زنی ومتى زنى و بمن زنی محسن نہیں ہے تو سو کوڑے حد لگے گی۔

[2445] (2) پس بعینہ کی شکل یہ ہے کہ گواہی دیں چار گواہ مرد پر یا عورت پر زنا کی ۔ چار گواہ کسی مرد یا عورت پر گواہی دیں کہ انہوں نے زنا کیا ہے تو زنا ثابت ہوگا۔ زنا میں چار گواہوں کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے کہ اس کی جان جائے گی۔ اور قرآن میں بھی ہے کہ ثبوت کے لئے چار گواہ چاہئے (2) والتى يأتين الفاحشة من نسائكم فستشهدوا عليهن اربعة منكم فان شهدوا فامسكوهن في البيوت (الف) ( آیت 15 سورۃ النساء 4) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ چار گواہ چاہئے (2) حدیث میں ہے۔ ان سعید بن عبادة قال يا رسول الله الله ان وجدت مع امرأتي رجلا امهله حتى اتى باربعة شهداء ؟ قال نعم (ب) ( مسلم شريف، کتاب اللعان ص 288 نمبر 1498) اس آیت سے اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زنا ثابت کرنے کے لئے چار گواہ چاہئے ۔ اور آیت میں منکم چونکہ مذکر کی ضمیر ہے اس لئے چاروں گواہ مرد ہوں۔

[2446] (3) امام گواہوں سے پوچھیں گے زنا کے بارے میں کہ زنا کیا ہے؟ کس طرح ہوتا ہے؟ زنا کہاں کیا ہے؟ کب کیا ہے؟ کس کے ساتھ کیا ہے؟ تشریح گواہ زنا کی گواہی دیدے تو امام گواہوں سے پوری تحقیق کریں گے تا کہ حقیقت ظاہر ہو جائے کہ واقعی زنا ہوا ہے یا نہیں۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ جہاں تک ہو سکے حد کو ساقط کی جائے ۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الا الله ادرئوا الحدود عن المسلمين ما استطعتم فان كان له مخرج فخلوا سبيله فان الامام ان يخطئ في العفو خير من ان يخطئ في العقوبة (ج) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی درء الحدود ص 263 نمبر 1424) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں تک ہو سکے حدود کو شبہ کی بنا پر ساقط کی جائے۔ گواہوں سے زنا کے بارے میں پوچھے کہ زنا کیا ہے؟ یعنی جو کام اپنی بیوی سے حلال کے طور پر کرتا ہے وہی کام اجتنبیہ عورت سے حرام کے طور پر کرنے کو کہتے ہیں ۔ گواہ اس حقیقت کو جانتا ہو۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ انه سمع أبا هريرة يقول جاء الاسلمى الى نبى الله الله فشهد على نفسه انه اصاب امرأة حراما اربع مرات كل ذلك يعرض عنه النبي الا الله فاقبل في الخامسة فقال انكتها ؟ قال نعم قال حتى غاب ذلك حاشیہ : تمہاری عورتوں میں سے جو زنا کرائے ان پر تمہارے لوگوں میں سے چار گواہ لاؤ۔ پس اگر گواہی دے دیں تو ان کو گھروں میں قید رکھو (ب) سعد بن عبادہ نے فرمایا یا رسول اللہ ! میں نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ ایک آدمی پایا۔ کیا اس کو چھوڑ کر چار گواہ بلانے جاؤں؟ آپ نے فرمایا ہاں؟ (ج) آپ نے فرمایا جب تک ہو سکے مسلمانوں سے حدود دفع کیا کرو ۔ پس اگر اس کے لئے کوئی راستہ نکلے تو اس کو چھوڑ دو ۔ اس لئے کہ امام معاف کرنے میں غلطی کرے یہ زیادہ بہتر ہے اس سے کہ سزا دینے میں غلطی کرے۔

[2447] (4) فاذا بينوا ذلك وقالوا رأيناه وطأها في فرجها كالميل في المكحلة. منک فى ذلك منها ؟ قال نعم قال كما يغيب المرود فى المكحلة والرشاء في البئر ؟ قال نعم قال هل تدرى ما الزنا؟ قال نعم اتيت منها حراما ما يأتى الرجل من امرأته حلالا قال فما تريد بهذا المقول ؟ قال اريد ان تطهر نی فامر به فرجم (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب رجم ما عز بن مالک ص 20 نمبر 4428 ، بخاری شریف ، باب لامير جم الجحون والجو بيص 1006 نمبر 6815) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زنا کیا ہے گواہوں سے اور اقرار کرنے والے سے پوری طرح اس کی تحقیق کریں گے۔ اور کس کے ساتھ زنا کیا یہ بھی پوچھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ حـدثـنـي يزيد بن نعيم بن هزال عن ابيه ... فقال النبي الله انک قد قلتها اربع مرات فيمن ؟ قال بفلانة قال هل ضاجعتها ؟ قال نعم قال هل باشرتها؟ قال نعم قال هل جامعتها ؟ قال نعم قال فامر به ان يرجم (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب رجم ما عز بن مالک ص 260 نمبر 4419 ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بھی پوچھے کہ کس سے زنا کیا تا کہ ایسا نہ ہو کہ اس کے لئے حلال عورت ہو اور زنا کی گواہی دے رہا ہو۔ اور زنا کی جگہ اس لئے پوچھے کہ اگر گواہوں کے درمیان جگہ کے بارے میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم في اربعة شهدوا على امرأة بالزنا ثم اختلفوا في الموضع فقال بعضهم بالكوفة وقال بعضهم بالبصرة قال يدرأ عنهم جميعا (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شہادة اربعة على امرأة بالزنا واختلافهم في الموضع ج سابع ص 334 نمبر 1338) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ زنا کی جگہ میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے جگہ کے بارے میں بھی گواہوں سے پوچھے ۔

[2447] (4) پس جب اس کو بیان کر دے اور وہ کہیں میں نے اس کو وطی کرتے دیکھا ہے اس کے فرج میں جیسے سلائی سرمہ دانی میں ۔ ار گواہ نے اشارہ کنایہ سے زنا کی گواہی دی تو مقبول نہیں ہے بلکہ پوری وضاحت سے کہنا ہوگا کہ جیسے سلائی سرمہ دانی میں ڈالی جاتی ہے ایسا میں نے کرتے ہوئے دیکھا تب زنا کا ثبوت ہوگا۔
[2445] (2) The evidence is that four witnesses testify against a man and a woman for zina. [2446] (3) So the imam asks them about zina: what it is, how it is, where he committed zina, when he committed zina, and with whom he committed zina. If he is not muhsan, then the punishment is one hundred lashes. ... [2445] (2) So the form of testimony is that four witnesses testify against a man or a woman for zina. Four witnesses testify against a man or a woman that they committed zina, then zina is proven. The need for four witnesses in zina is because life will be taken. And in the Quran there is that for proof four witnesses are required: 'And those who commit immorality among your women - bring four witnesses among you. If they testify, then confine them to their houses.' (Surah An-Nisa 4:15) This verse indicates that four witnesses are required. And in the hadith: 'Sa'id ibn 'Ubadah said: O Messenger of Allah, if I find a man with my wife, should I leave him until I bring four witnesses? He said: Yes.' (Muslim, Kitab al-Li'an, p. 288, no. 1498) From this verse and hadith it is learned that to prove zina, four witnesses are needed. And in the verse the pronoun 'minkum' is masculine, so all four witnesses must be men. ... [2446] (3) The imam will ask the witnesses about zina: what is zina? How does it happen? Where was zina committed? When was it committed? With whom was it committed? Explanation: If a witness gives testimony of zina, the imam will thoroughly investigate until the truth becomes apparent whether zina actually occurred or not. The second reason is that as much as possible the punishment should be dropped. 'A'ishah reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Avert the punishments from the Muslims as much as you can. If there is a way out, let the person go. For the imam to err in pardoning is better than to err in punishing.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Dar' al-Hudud, p. 263, no. 1424) From this hadith it is learned that punishments should be dropped as much as possible due to doubt. He asks the witnesses about zina: what is zina? That is, the act that a man does with his wife lawfully, doing the same act with a strange woman unlawfully is called zina. The witness should know this reality. There is a hadith: 'Abu Hurairah said that al-Aslami came to the Prophet of Allah and testified against himself four times that he had unlawful intercourse with a woman. Each time the Prophet turned away from him. Then on the fifth time he said: Did you marry her? He said: No. He said: Until it disappeared inside her? He said: Yes. He said: As the pencil disappears into the kohl container and the rope into the well? He said: Yes. He said: Do you know what zina is? He said: Yes. I did with her unlawfully what a man does with his wife lawfully. He said: What do you want with this saying? He said: I want to purify me. So he ordered that he be stoned.' (Abu Dawud, Bab Rajm Ma'iz ibn Malik, p. 20, no. 4428; Bukhari, Bab, no. 6815) From this hadith it is learned what zina is. They will thoroughly investigate from the witnesses and the one who confesses. And he also asks with whom zina was committed. For this there is a hadith: 'Yazid ibn Nu'aym ibn Hazzal from his father ... The Prophet said: You have said it four times. With whom? He said: With so-and-so woman. He said: Did you lie with her? He said: Yes. He said: Did you have direct contact? He said: Yes. He said: Did you have intercourse? He said: Yes. So he ordered that he be stoned.' (Abu Dawud, Bab Rajm Ma'iz ibn Malik, p. 260, no. 4419) From this hadith it is learned that he also asks with whom zina was committed so that it may not be that the woman is lawful for him and he is testifying to zina. And the place of zina is asked because if the witnesses differ about the place, the punishment is dropped. There is an athar: 'Ibrahim said about four who testified against a woman for zina then differed about the location: some said in Kufa, some said in Basra. He said: It is averted from all of them.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Shahadat Arba'ah 'ala Imra'ah bil Zina wa Ikhtilafihim fi al-Mawdi', vol. 7, p. 334, no. 1338) From this athar it is learned that if they differ about the location of zina, the punishment is dropped. So he asks about the place as well. [2447] (4) Then when they explain that and say: We saw him having intercourse with her in her vagina like the pencil in the kohl container. If a witness testifies to zina through allusion or metaphor, it is not accepted. Rather, he must state with full clarity that he saw him insert like the pencil into the kohl container; then zina is proven.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Hudud explains the procedure for proving the crime of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) through witness testimony, as per the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating the primary requirement: four male witnesses must testify against a man or a woman for zina. This is derived from the Quranic verse (4:15) which commands bringing four witnesses against women who commit immorality, and from a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) confirms that four witnesses are needed even if a man finds someone with his wife. The author notes that the pronoun 'minkum' (from among you) is masculine, indicating that all four witnesses must be men.

Next, the passage describes the role of the imam (judge) in cross-examining the witnesses. The imam must ask about the nature of zina, how it was committed, where, when, and with whom. The purpose of this detailed inquiry is twofold: first, to ascertain the truth, and second, to find any doubt that may cause the punishment to be dropped. The author cites a hadith: 'Avert the punishments from the Muslims as much as you can, for the imam to err in pardoning is better than to err in punishing.' This reflects the Hanafi principle of dar' al-hudud (averting punishments) by removing any uncertainty.

The passage then clarifies that witnesses must explicitly describe the act of penetration using clear language, such as 'like the pencil entering the kohl container.' Allusive or metaphorical statements are not accepted. The author supports this with the story of Ma'iz and the woman (or al-Aslami) where the Prophet asked detailed questions about the act before ordering stoning. Similarly, the imam must ask with whom the act was committed, to ensure that the woman is not lawful for the man (e.g., his wife). If witnesses disagree about the location of the act, the punishment is averted, as shown by an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Overall, the Hanafi position is that zina is proven by the testimony of four male witnesses who must describe the act explicitly. The imam must thoroughly question them, and any discrepancy—especially regarding location—can nullify the testimony and avert the punishment.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony given by witnesses in a legal case; for zina, it must be from four male witnesses who explicitly describe the act.
زنا (zinā): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other, involving penetration of the vagina by the penis.
إمام (imām): The judge or ruler who presides over legal proceedings and ensures the proper conduct of testimony and punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The witnesses are punished for false testimony

Key Takeaway
Zina is proven only by four male witnesses who explicitly describe penetration; any doubt, especially about location, averts the punishment.

Explicit Testimony for Zina and Location Disagreement
Requirement for explicit description of zina act by witnesses and confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement for explicit testimony in zina cases and explain why disagreement on location nullifies the hadd punishment.

Core Idea
For hadd, testimony must explicitly describe penetration; location disagreement drops the punishment.

The hudud punishments demand the highest evidentiary standards. This passage from Sharh al-Thamiri explains two key rules: witnesses must describe the act with explicit clarity, and if they differ on the location, the hadd is averted. Let's examine the proof and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two evidentiary rules
Recognize that the passage establishes two distinct requirements: (1) testimony must explicitly describe penetration using a clear analogy, and (2) if witnesses disagree on the location, the hadd is dropped.
The first rule is based on the hadith of Ma'iz; the second on an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
2
Analyze the hadith proof for explicit testimony
The Prophet (peace be upon him) repeatedly asked Ma'iz for clarification until he described the act as 'like a kohl stick entering a kohl container.' This insistence shows that vague or implicit statements are insufficient for hadd.
The hadith is ahad in transmission but its meaning is clear and definitive (dalala qat'i).
3
Analyze the athar for location disagreement
The athar from Ibrahim states that if four witnesses differ on the location (e.g., Kufa vs. Basra), the hadd is averted from all. This prevents punishment when the testimony is inconsistent on a key detail.
The location is considered a material detail that must be consistent to establish the offense.
4
Understand the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi school holds these requirements as necessary to uphold the strict evidentiary standards for hudud, protecting against false accusations and erroneous punishment.
Other schools may accept less explicit testimony, but Hanafi adheres to the explicit analogy from the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود
[۲۴۴۷] (۴) فاذا بينوا ذلك وقالوا رأيناه وطأها في فرجها كالميل في المكحلة. ... اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زنا کیا ہے گواہوں سے اور اقرار کرنے والے سے پوری طرح اس کی تحقیق کریں گے۔ اور کس کے ساتھ زنا کیا یہ بھی پوچھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ اس طرح بیان کریں کہ میں نے سلائی کو سرمہ دانی میں جس طرح ڈالتے ہیں اس طرح کرتے دیکھا ہے۔ میل : سرمہ کی سلائی، مکحلہ : کحل سے مشتق ہے سرمہ رکھنے کی چیز، سرمہ دانی۔
اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ بھی پوچھے کہ کس سے زنا کیا تا کہ ایسا نہ ہو کہ اس کے لئے حلال عورت ہو اور زنا کی گواہی دے رہا ہو۔ اور زنا کی جگہ اس لئے پوچھے کہ اگر گواہوں کے درمیان جگہ کے بارے میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم في اربعة شهدوا على امرأة بالزنا ثم اختلفوا في الموضع فقال بعضهم بالكوفة وقال بعضهم بالبصرة قال يدرأ عنهم جميعا (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شہادة اربعة على امرأة بالزنا واختلافهم في الموضع ج سابع ص ۳۳۴ نمبر ۰ ۱۳۳۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ زنا کی جگہ میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے جگہ کے بارے میں بھی گواہوں سے پوچھے ۔
Book of Hudud. [2447] (4) So when they clarify that and say: We saw him having intercourse with her in her vagina like the kohl stick in the kohl container. ... From this hadith it is understood what zina is: the witnesses and the one confessing will be thoroughly investigated. And also ask with whom zina was committed; for this there is this hadith. In the hadith it is that they describe it as: I saw him inserting like one inserts the kohl stick into the kohl container. 'Mil' means kohl stick, 'mukhlah' is derived from kuhl, meaning the container for kohl. From this hadith it is also understood that he should also ask with whom he committed zina, so that it may not happen that the woman was lawful for him and he is testifying to zina. And he asks about the place of zina because if the witnesses differ about the place, the hadd is dropped. There is an athar: From Ibrahim concerning four who testified against a woman for zina then differed about the place: some said in Kufa, some said in Basra. He said: The hadd is averted from all of them. (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on four testifying against a woman for zina and their disagreement on the place, vol. 7, p. 334, no. 13318). From this athar it is understood that if there is disagreement about the place of zina, the hadd is dropped. Therefore, the witnesses should also be asked about the place.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh al-Thamiri discusses the evidentiary requirements for proving zina. The ruling is that witnesses must give explicit testimony describing the act of penetration using a clear analogy, like a kohl stick entering a kohl container. Mere hints or allusions are insufficient. The text bases this on the hadith of Ma'iz where the Prophet (peace be upon him) repeatedly asked for clarification until Ma'iz described the act explicitly. Additionally, the judge must inquire about the identity of the partner to ensure it is not a lawful relationship. Furthermore, if witnesses disagree on the location of the act, the hadd punishment is averted entirely, as shown in the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. This prevents ambiguity in establishing the offense.

Key Terms
الميل في المكحلة (al-mil fi al-mukhlah): The kohl stick in the kohl container; used as an analogy for full penetration in zina testimony.
الحد (al-hadd): Fixed punishment for certain crimes (e.g., zina) prescribed by Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The hadd is still applied because the act itself is confirmed.
B) The hadd is averted from all witnesses and the accused.
C) The judge chooses the testimony of the majority.
D) The witnesses must repeat their testimony until they agree.

Key Takeaway
Explicit description of penetration and agreement on location are mandatory for hadd; any ambiguity drops the punishment.

Judge's Investigation of Witnesses' Character (Tazkiyah)
Requirement for judge to verify witnesses' uprightness both secretly and publicly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for tazkiyah (verification of witnesses' integrity) and apply it to determine when a judge may accept testimony in a hudud case.

Core Idea
The judge must verify witnesses' uprightness both secretly and publicly before ruling on hudud penalties.

This passage from Sharh al-Thamiri explains the obligation of the judge to investigate the character of witnesses before accepting their testimony in a zina case. The Hanafi school requires tazkiyah (attestation of integrity) covering both outward reputation and inward conduct, as demonstrated by the Quranic command to verify news and the practice of the Prophet and Caliph Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the ruling: it is wajib (obligatory) for the judge to conduct tazkiyah, i.e., investigate the moral character of witnesses, both secretly and publicly, before accepting their testimony in hudud cases such as zina.
The passage specifies the context of zina, but the principle applies generally to hudud.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse cited: Surah al-Hujurat 49:6. The command to verify news (fatas bi-ahmili al-nafs) indicates that verification of witnesses' integrity is required.
The verse uses 'fasiq' (wicked person), so the principle applies when news comes from a fasiq; by qiyas, verification is required even more for witnesses.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fatabayyanu' (verify) indicates obligation (wujub). Applying this to witnesses means the judge must actively investigate their 'adalah (uprightness) before relying on their testimony.
The Hanafi usul rule: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Examine the supplementary proofs
The passage also cites hadith of Ma'iz (Prophet inquired about his sanity) and athar of Umar (detailed questioning about neighborliness and travel). These illustrate the practical scope of tazkiyah: secret and public aspects, including travel and close association.
Umar's questioning shows that superficial knowledge is insufficient; deep acquaintance is needed.
