[2448] (5) And the judge asked about them, and they (the witnesses) were declared upright in secret and in public, so he ruled according to their testimony. ... After the witnesses testify, the judge should inquire about their moral condition secretly and publicly. People should testify to their goodness and piety both outwardly and inwardly, which is called tazkiyah (attestation of integrity). Then the judge may rule on zina based on their testimony. The evidence for investigation is this verse: 'O you who believe, if a wicked person comes to you with news, verify it, lest you harm people out of ignorance and become regretful over what you have done.' (Surah al-Hujurat, 49:6). From this verse it is understood that when any news comes, it should be investigated. It also indicates that witnesses must be verified (ta'dil). (2) The Prophet (peace be upon him) asked about Ma'iz al-Aslami's people: 'Is he mad?' They said: 'There is nothing wrong with him.' (c) (Abu Dawud, chapter on Rajm of Ma'iz bin Malik, p. 260 no. 4421; Muslim, chapter on those who confess to zina, p. 66 no. 4432/1995). In this hadith, the Prophet verified Ma'iz's mental state. (3) Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) asked about witnesses. From Khirash bin al-Hurr: Two witnesses testified before Umar, so he said to them: 'I do not know you, but it does not harm you that I do not know you. Bring someone who knows you.' A man came, and Umar asked: 'How do you know them?' He said: 'They are righteous and trustworthy.' Umar asked: 'Were you their neighbor?' He said: 'No.' He asked: 'Did you travel with them on a journey that reveals the character of men?' He said: 'No.' Umar said: 'You do not know them. Bring someone who knows you.' (d) (I'la al-Sunan no. 4966, chapter on asking about witnesses, vol. 15 p. 173). From this athar it is understood that one should investigate about witnesses; then if they are found to be upright, one may rule based on them.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh al-Thamiri explains the requirement for the judge to conduct a background check on witnesses before accepting their testimony in a zina case. The Hanafi position is that tazkiyah (verification of integrity) is necessary both secretly and publicly, meaning the judge must inquire about the witnesses' character from reliable people, considering both their public reputation and private conduct. The proof is the Quranic verse commanding verification when receiving news, coupled with the Prophet's practice of investigating Ma'iz's sanity before proceeding. Also, the practice of Umar shows detailed questioning: he asked about the witnesses' neighborliness and travel companionship because these reveal true character. Only when the witnesses are declared 'adil (upright) does the judge proceed to rule based on their testimony.

Key Terms
تعديل / تزكية (ta'dil / tazkiyah): The act of attesting to a witness's uprightness ('adalah) by reputable individuals, covering both outward and inward conduct.

Key Takeaway
Investigating witnesses' character both secretly and publicly is obligatory (wajib) before accepting their testimony in hudud cases.

The Judge's Duty to Verify Witnesses in Hudud Cases
Explains the judge's duty to investigate witnesses' character before accepting testimony for zina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tadil (verification of witnesses) in hudud cases and explain its evidentiary basis from the Quran, Sunnah, and practice of the Sahaba.

Core Idea
A judge must investigate witnesses' character before accepting testimony in hudud — certainty is required.

The burden of proof in hudud cases, especially zina, is extremely high. The Hanafi school requires the judge to actively verify the uprightness (adalah) of witnesses before relying on their testimony. This lesson unpacks that requirement and the three proofs that establish it: a Quranic command to verify news, the Prophet's precaution with Ma'iz, and Umar's rigorous questioning of witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
Recognize that the passage imposes a duty on the judge to conduct tadil (verification of witnesses' integrity) before accepting their testimony in a zina case. This is a wajib (obligatory) step for the judge.
The ruling applies specifically to hudud, where the threshold for proof is highest.
2
Understand the process of tadil
The judge must inquire both secretly (sirran) and openly (alaniyatan) about the witnesses' moral character. Community members attest to their righteousness (salah) and piety (taqwa). Only after this collective affirmation can the judge rule based on their testimony.
This dual verification prevents reliance on superficial impressions.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof (49:6)
The verse commands 'fatabayyanu' (verify) when a sinful person brings news. The Hanafi position is that this imperative indicates wujub (obligation), and by analogy, witnesses' reports require verification of their integrity.
The comparison: a fasiq's news → witnesses' testimony; both need verification to avoid injustice.
4
Analyze the Sunnah proof (hadith of Ma'iz)
The Prophet did not immediately accept Ma'iz's confession but asked his people about his mental state. This demonstrates the principle of verifying the capacity (and by extension, integrity) of the one offering testimony or confession.
Although Ma'iz confessed, the principle of inquiry is extended to witnesses.
5
Analyze the Sahaba proof (practice of Umar)
Umar refused to accept testimony until witnesses brought someone who knew them well, such as neighbors or travel companions. This shows the need for concrete, reliable sources of character verification, not just casual acquaintance.
Umar's method sets a precedent for proper judicial inquiry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۴۸] (۵) قاضی نے سوال کیا گواہوں کے بارے میں تو ان کو عادل بتایا خفیہ اور علانیہ تو فیصلہ کر دے ان کی شہادت کے مطابق۔ اف گواہوں کی گواہی کے بعد قاضی خفیہ اور علانیہ طور پر گواہوں کی اخلاقی حالت کے بارے میں پوچھ تاچھ کرے۔ ظاہری طور پر اور باطنی طور پر دونوں طرح لوگ ان کے صلاح اور تقوی کی گواہی دیں جس کو تعدیل کہتے ہیں تو قاضی ان کی گواہی پر زنا کا فیصلہ کر دے۔ تحقیق و تفتیش کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ۔ یا ایها الذين آمنوا ان جائكم فاسق بنبأ فتبينوا ان تصيبوا قوما بجهالة فتصبحوا على ما فعلتم نادمين (ب) ( آیت ۶ سورة الحجرات (۴۹) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی خبر آئے تو اس کی تحقیق کرنی چاہئے ۔ اس میں یہ بھی معلوم ہوئی کہ گواہی دینے والوں کی بھی تعدیل کرنی چاہئے (۲) حضور حضرت ماعز اسلمی کے بارے میں ان کی قوم سے پوچھا تھا کہ یہ کیسے ہیں۔ عن ابن عباس ان ماعز بن مالک اتی النبی الله الله فقال انه زنی فاعرض عنه فاعاد عليه مرارا فاعرض عنه فسأل قومه امجنون هو ؟ قالوا ليس به بأس (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب رحم ما عز بن مالک ص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۱۴۴۲۱ مسلم شریف ، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۴۴۳۲/۱۹۹۵) اس حدیث میں حضور نے حضرت ماعر کی دماغی حالت کے بارے میں تعدیل کی ہے (۳) حضرت عمرؓ نے گواہوں کے بارے میں پوچھا ہے۔ عن خرشة بن الحر قال ان شاهدين شهداعند عمر فقال لهما اني لا اعـرفـكـمـا ولا يضر كما ان لا اعرفكما انتيا بمن يعرفكما فاتاه رجل فقال بم تعرفها ؟ قال بالصلاح والامانة قال كنت جارا لهما ؟ قال لا ! قال صحبتهما في السفر الذي يسفر عن اخلاق الرجال؟ قال لا قال فانت لاتعرفهما انتيا بمن يعرفكما (د) (اعلاء السنن نمبر ۴۹۶۶، باب السؤال عن الشهود، ج الخامس عشر ص ۱۷۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہوں کے بارے میں تحقیق کرے پھر صحیح معلوم ہو تو فیصلہ کرے۔
[2448] (5) The judge asked about the witnesses, they were declared upright secretly and openly, so he judged according to their testimony. So after the witnesses testify, the judge should inquire secretly and openly about the moral state of the witnesses. Both outwardly and inwardly, people should testify to their righteousness and piety, which is called tazkiya. Then the judge should decide the case of zina based on their testimony. The evidence for investigation and scrutiny is this verse: 'O you who have believed, if a sinful person comes to you with information, verify it, lest you harm a people out of ignorance and become regretful over what you have done.' (Surah al-Hujurat 49:6). From this verse it is learned that when news comes, it must be investigated. And it also indicates that the character of those giving testimony must be verified. (2) The Prophet asked about the people of Ma'iz al-Aslami (may Allah be pleased with him) how he was. From Ibn Abbas: Ma'iz ibn Malik came to the Prophet and said he had committed zina. The Prophet turned away from him. He repeated it several times but the Prophet turned away. Then he asked his people, 'Is he insane?' They said, 'There is nothing wrong with him.' (Abu Dawud #4421, Muslim #1695/1995). In this hadith, the Prophet verified Ma'iz's mental state. (3) Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) asked about witnesses. From Kharsha ibn al-Hurr: Two witnesses testified before Umar. He told them, 'I do not know you, and it does not harm you that I do not know you. Bring someone who knows you.' A man came and asked, 'How do you know them?' He said, 'By their righteousness and trustworthiness.' He asked, 'Were you their neighbor?' He said, 'No.' He asked, 'Did you travel with them in a journey that reveals a man's character?' He said, 'No.' He said, 'Then you do not know them. Bring someone who knows you.' (I'la al-Sunan #4966, Bab al-Su'al 'an al-Shuhud, vol. 15 p. 173). From this effect it is learned that one should investigate witnesses and then judge when they are found upright.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm wa dalil) from the Hanafi text explaining the procedure for accepting testimony in zina cases. The author states that after witnesses come forward, the judge must conduct an investigation into their character—both secretly and openly—to ensure they are 'adil (upright) in both outward and inward conduct. This process is called tadil (declaring witnesses' integrity). Only when community members affirm their righteousness and piety should the judge accept the testimony and issue the hadd punishment for zina. Three proofs are cited: (1) Quran 49:6, which commands verification (tabayyun) when a sinful person brings news, understood analogically to require verification of witnesses' credibility. (2) The hadith of Ma'iz ibn Malik, where the Prophet did not immediately accept his confession but asked his people about his mental state, showing the need to verify the confessor's capacity. (3) The practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who refused to accept the testimony of two witnesses until their character was verified through proper inquiry—neighbors or travel companions. This demonstrates that even testimonies in court must undergo scrutiny. The Hanafi position emphasizes that tadil is a necessary condition (shart) for the judge to rule based on testimony, especially in hudud cases where the burden of proof is highest.

Key Terms
تعديل (tadil): The process of declaring witnesses upright (adil) after investigation by the judge or community.
تزكية (tazkiya): The act of attesting to a witness's integrity, equivalent to tadil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only ask witnesses if they are Muslim.
C) Investigate the witnesses' character both secretly and openly (tadil).
D) Require the witnesses to bring four other witnesses to support them.

Key Takeaway
In hudud, the judge must verify witnesses' integrity through thorough investigation before accepting testimony; this is wajib and based on Quran, Sunnah, and Sahaba practice.

The Requirement of Four Confessions for Zina: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Evidence
Ruling on the requirement of four confessions for zina with evidence and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires four confessions for zina and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of Ma'iz and the woman.

Core Idea
Confession of zina requires four separate sessions — like four witnesses, each confession is a piece of testimony.

This passage delves into the procedural requirements for a confession of zina to be legally effective under Hanafi law. The key issue is how many times a person must confess, and the Hanafi school insists on four distinct confessions in four separate sessions, drawing an analogy to the four witnesses needed for proof. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing a case where one confession led to stoning. This lesson will walk you through the evidence and the reasoning that resolves the conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school require for a confession of zina to establish the hadd? Quote the passage: four confessions in four separate sessions, with the judge rejecting each time.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one confession is sufficient. What is his evidence from the hadith of the woman?
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school uses the hadith of Ma'iz to show that the Prophet turned him away after two confessions, and only after four did he act. How does this prove the requirement?
Also note the analogy to the four witnesses in zina.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school respond to the Shafi'i evidence of the woman who confessed once? The passage suggests an interpretation: the woman may have confessed multiple times, or it is an exception.
The key is that the strongest evidence aligns with the four-confession rule.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? In a Hanafi court, a person confessing once cannot be stoned; in a Shafi'i court, one confession suffices.
This affects real-life application of hudud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۴۹] (٦) والاقرار ان يقر البالغ العاقل على نفسه بالزنا اربع مرات في اربعة مجالس من مجالس المقر كلما اقر ردَّه القاضى تعدیل کرنا، گواہوں کے بارے میں پوچھنا کہ یہ اچھے لوگ ہیں یا اچھے لوگ نہیں ہیں۔ [۲۴۴۹] (۶) اور اقرار کی شکل یہ ہے کہ اقرار کرے بالغ عاقل آدمی اپنی ذات پر زنا کا چار مرتبہ چار مجلسوں میں اقرار کرنے والے کی مجلسوں میں۔ جب جب اقرار کرے قاضی اس کو رد کر دے۔ اوپر چار گواہوں کے ذریعہ زنا کے ثبوت کا طریقہ تھا۔ اب یہ طریقہ بیان کیا جا رہا ہے کہ اقرار کرنے والا خود اپنی ذات پر زنا کا اقرار کر رہا ہے۔ تو اس کے لئے بھی ضروری ہے کہ چار مرتبہ اقرار کرے اور ہر بار اقرار کرنے والے کی مجلس بدل جائے ۔ یعنی چار مرتبہ چار الگ الگ مجلسوں میں اقرار کرے۔ اور قاضی ہر بار اس کے اقرار کور د کر دے کہ شاید تم نے دیکھا ہوگا یا بھینچا ہوگا۔
حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ماعر نے چار مرتبہ اقرار کیا اور چار مجلسوں میں کیا۔ ان ابا هريرة قال اتى رسول الله لا رجل من الناس وهو في المسجد فناداه يا رسول الله ! انی زنیت یرید نفسه فاعرض عنه النبي عل الله فتنحى لشق وجهه الذي اعرض عنه فقال يا رسول الله ! انى زنيت فاعرض عنه فجاء لشق وجه النبى الله الذى اعرض عنه فلما شهد على نفسه اربع شهادات دعاه النبی الله الله فقال ایک جنون ؟ (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب سوال الامام المقر هل احصنت ص ۱۰۰۸ نمبر ۶۸۲۵ ر مسلم شریف ، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۶۹۵/۱۶۹۲) اس حدیث میں چار مرتبہ چار جانب سے حضرت ماعز آئے جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ چار مجلسوں میں چار مرتبہ اقرار کرے تب فیصلہ کریں گے (۲) یہ اقرار بھی گواہ کی طرح ہے۔ اور اوپر آیت گزری کہ چار گواہ چاہئے۔ اسی طرح زنا کے اقرار کے لئے بھی چار مرتبہ اقرار کرنا چاہئے۔ اور ہر بار رد کرنے کی دلیل بھی حدیث میں گزرگئی۔ ابو داؤد شریف کی حدیث میں یہ لفظ بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال جاء ماعز بن مالك الى النبي له فاعترف بالزنا مرتين فطرده (ب) ( ابو داؤد شریف ، باب رحم ما عز بن مالک ص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۴۴۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے دو مرتبہ حضرت ماعر کو ہٹا
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ چار مرتبہ اقرار ہو تو اچھا ہے ورنہ ایک مرتبہ اقرار کر لے تب بھی زنا کا ثبوت ہو جائے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک عورت نے ایک مرتبہ زنا کا اقرار کیا تو اس کو رجم کیا گیا۔ عن ابى هريرة وزيد بن خالد قالا ... واعد يا انيس على امرأة هذا فان اعترفت فارجمها فغدا عليها فاعترفت فرجمها (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الاعتراف بالزناص حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابو ہریرہ فرماتے ہیں کہ لوگوں میں سے ایک آدمی حضور کے پاس آیا۔ آپ مسجد میں تھے۔ آپ کو پکارا یا رسول اللہ ! میں نے زنا کیا ہے۔ آپ نے اعراض کیا تو وہ دوسری جانب سے آئے پھر کہا یا رسول اللہ ! میں نے زنا کیا۔ آپ نے اعراض کیا۔ آپ نے جدھر چہرہ گھمایا تھا وہ اسی جانب آئے ۔ پس چار مرتبہ شہادت دی تو آپ نے ان کو بلایا اور پوچھا کیا تم کو جنون تو نہیں ہے؟ (ب) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت ماعز بن مالک محضور کے پاس آئے اور زنا کا دو مرتبہ اعتراف کیا تو آپ نے ان کو ٹال دیا (ج) یزید بن خالد فرماتے ہیں کہ ... اے انہیں اس عورت کے پاس جاؤ اگر وہ زنا کا اقرار کرے تو اس کو رجم کر دینا۔ حضرت انس ان کے پاس گئے عورت نے اقرار کیا تو حضرت انس نے ان کور تم کیا۔
[2449] (6) And confession is that a mature, sane person confesses to zina upon himself four times in four sessions of the sessions of the confessor. Whenever he confesses, the judge rejects him. 'Tadeel': to declare upright, to inquire about witnesses whether they are good people or not. [2449] (6) And the form of confession is that a mature, sane person confesses to zina upon himself four times in four sessions of the confessor's sessions. Whenever he confesses, the judge rejects him. Above was the method of proving zina through four witnesses. Now this method is being explained: the confessor himself is confessing to zina upon himself. So for him too it is necessary to confess four times, and each time the confessor's session changes. That is, four times in four separate sessions. And the judge each time rejects his confession, saying perhaps you saw or touched? It is in the hadith that Hadrat Ma'iz confessed four times and in four sessions. Narrated Abu Huraira: A man from among the people came to the Messenger of Allah while he was in the mosque, and called out, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina,' referring to himself. The Prophet turned away from him. He went to the side of his face to which he turned away and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina.' He turned away from him. He came to the side of the Prophet's face to which he turned away, and when he had testified against himself four times, the Prophet called him and said, 'Are you insane?' (a) (Bukhari, Bab su'al al-imam al-muqirr hal ahsanta, p.1008 no.6825; Muslim, Bab man i'tarafa 'ala nafsihi bi al-zina, p.66 no.1695/1692). In this hadith, Hadrat Ma'iz came four times from four directions, meaning he confessed four times in four sessions, then they would decide. (2) This confession is like witnessing. And the verse above stated that four witnesses are required. Similarly, for confession of zina, confessing four times is required. And the evidence for rejection each time also passed in the hadith. In Abu Dawud's hadith, there are these words: From Ibn Abbas: Ma'iz ibn Malik came to the Prophet and confessed to zina twice, and he turned him away. (b) (Abu Dawud, Bab rajm Ma'iz ibn Malik, p.260 no.4426). In this hadith, the Prophet turned away Hadrat Ma'iz twice. Imam al-Shafi'i says that four confessions are good, otherwise one confession is sufficient; zina is proven. It is in the hadith that a woman confessed once to zina and was stoned. From Abu Huraira and Zaid ibn Khalid: '... O Unais, go to this woman, and if she confesses, stone her.' So he went to her in the morning, she confessed, and he stoned her. (c) (Bukhari, Bab al-i'tiraf bi al-zina). Footnote: (a) Hadrat Abu Huraira says: A man from the people came to the Prophet; he was in the mosque. He called out, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina.' He turned away, so he came from the other side and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina.' He turned away, and he came to the side the Prophet had turned, and when he had testified against himself four times, he called him and asked, 'Are you insane?' (b) Hadrat Ibn 'Abbas says: Hadrat Ma'iz ibn Malik came to the Prophet and confessed to zina twice, so he turned him away. (c) Zaid ibn Khalid says: '... O Unais, go to this woman; if she confesses to zina, stone her.' Hadrat Anas went to her; the woman confessed, so Hadrat Anas stoned her.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the confession of zina, specifically the requirement of four confessions in four separate sessions. The author begins by defining the form of confession: a mature, sane person confesses to zina upon himself four times in four different sessions. Each time he confesses, the judge must reject him, possibly suggesting he saw or touched (i.e., he may be mistaken about the act). The author then provides the evidence from the hadith of Ma'iz, who confessed four times in four sessions, and the Prophet initially turned away from him. The second hadith from Abu Dawud shows the Prophet turned away Ma'iz after two confessions, indicating that less than four is not accepted. The author then notes the opposition of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that a single confession is sufficient, citing the hadith of the woman who confessed once and was stoned. This is a classic inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafi school requires four confessions analogous to four witnesses, while the Shafi'i school considers one confession sufficient based on the practice of the Prophet. The Hanafi rationale is that confession is akin to testimony (shahadah), which requires four witnesses for zina; thus four confessions are needed. The judge's rejection each time serves as a deterrent and to ensure the confessor is not coerced or insane.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession; a person's admission of guilt regarding a hadd offense, specifically zina.
مجلس (majlis): A session; a distinct gathering or occasion where the confession is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Accept the confession immediately and execute the hadd.
B) Reject the confession and warn the confessor that he might be mistaken.
C) Imprison the confessor until he has confessed four times.
D) Record the confession and wait for four witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four confessions in four separate sessions for a zina confession to establish the hadd, reflecting an analogy to the four witnesses and driven by caution in capital punishment.

The Judge's Duty to Interrogate After Confession of Zina
Ruling after four confessions of zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge must interrogate a confessor of zina and explain why each question is necessary to avoid wrongful punishment.

Core Idea
A confession alone does not trigger hadd; the judge must verify the act legally constitutes zina.

In Hanafi law, a confession of zina must be made four times in separate sessions before the judge interrogates. The judge then asks about the nature, method, location, and partner of the act to ensure it is punishable zina and not something ambiguous. This lesson unpacks the rationale behind each question and the condition for imposing the hadd penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger for interrogation
The confession must be completed four times; only then does the judge have the duty to question.
Four separate sessions, not necessarily four utterances in one sitting.
2
List the mandatory questions
The judge asks: what is zina, how was it done, where, and with whom.
Each question targets a potential source of shubha.
3
Explain the rationale for each question
The answers must confirm the act is zina in the confessor's understanding, was actual intercourse, within the jurisdiction, and with a partner incurring hadd.
For example, with a mahram or a son's slave-girl may drop hadd.
4
Determine the legal consequence
Only if all answers are correctly given and consistent does the hadd become wajib.
Any inconsistency or shubha drops the hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۵۰] (۷) فاذا تم اقراره اربع مرات سأله القاضى عن الزنا ماهو وكيف هو واين زنی و بمن زنى فاذا بين ذلك لزمه الحد [۲۴۵۰] (۷) پس جب اس کا اقرار چار مرتبہ پورا ہو جائے تو قاضی اس کو زنا کے بارے میں پوچھے کہ زنا کیا ہوتا ہے، وہ کیسے ہوتا ہے اور کہاں ہوا ، کس کے ساتھ کیا۔ پس جب اس کو بیان کر دے تو اس کو حد لازم ہوگی۔ اقرار کرنے والا چار مرتبہ اقرار کر لے تو قاضی اقرار کرنے والے کو زنا کی حقیقت پوچھے۔ یہ بھی پوچھے کہ وہ کیسے ہوتا ہے؟ یہ بھی پوچھے کہ وہ کہاں ہوا، کیونکہ اس کے اختلاف سے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ کس کے ساتھ کیا، کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ اقرار کرنے والا یہ سمجھے کہ فلاں کے ساتھ زنا کرنے سے حد لازم ہوگی حالانکہ بیٹے کی باندی سے زنا کرے تو حد لازم نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ ان ساری باتوں کا جواب صحیح صحیح دے دے تو قاضی زنا کا فیصلہ کرے گا۔
[2450] (7) So when his confession is completed four times, the judge asks him about zina: what is it, how is it, where did he commit zina, and with whom did he commit zina. So when he explains that, hadd becomes obligatory upon him. [2450] (7) So when his confession is completed four times, the judge should ask him about zina: what is zina, how is it done, where did it happen, and with whom did he do it. So when he explains that, hadd becomes obligatory upon him. The confessor, after confessing four times, the judge asks the confessor about the reality of zina. He also asks how it is done, and where it happened, because with difference (in answers) the hadd will be dropped. He also asks with whom he did it, because it is possible that the confessor thinks that with so-and-so doing zina will necessitate hadd, whereas if he does zina with his son's slave-girl, hadd is not obligatory. So when he gives correct answers to all these matters, the judge will decide on zina.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the procedure after a valid confession of zina. After the confessor has confessed four times in four sessions, the judge must interrogate him about the details: what is zina (in his understanding), how he performed it, where it occurred, and with whom. The purpose is to verify that the act actually constitutes punishable zina and not something else (e.g., a mistaken belief about the partner). The author explains that the details matter because if he claims it was with a mahram or a slave-girl of his son (where zina may not incur hadd due to shubha), the hadd may be dropped. Only if the confessor correctly explains all these details does the judge impose the hadd. This ruling is based on the need to avoid applying the punishment where there is doubt (shubha).

Key Terms
حد (hadd): The fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Sharia for certain crimes, such as zina.
شبهة (shubha): Legal doubt or ambiguity that can prevent the application of hadd punishment.
زنا (zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other and not in a valid relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) To know if the partner is a minor
D) To determine if it was consensual

Key Takeaway
A valid confession of zina requires the judge's interrogation to confirm the act legally constitutes punishable zina; otherwise, hadd is not obligatory.

Stoning for the Muhsan Zani: Conditions and Evidence
Ruling that the muhsan zani is stoned to death, with definition of muhsan and evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five Hanafi conditions for ihsan and explain why the muhsan zani is stoned rather than flogged, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Zina is punished by stoning for the muhsan but flogging for the non-muhsan, based on the Prophet's explicit command.

In the Hanafi school, the punishment for zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) depends on whether the offender is muhsan. This lesson examines the ruling that a muhsan zani must be stoned to death, defines the five conditions of ihsan, and presents the primary hadith evidence. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the hadd punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on zina committed by a muhsan person. The ruling is that he is stoned with stones until death. This is the prescribed hadd (fixed punishment).
2
List the five conditions of ihsan
The passage defines muhsan by five qualities: sanity, adulthood, valid marriage (with consummation), freedom, and Islam. A person possessing all these is muhsan.
These conditions are specific to the Hanafi school.
3
Locate the hadith evidence
The author cites the hadith of Abu Huraira where a man confessed to zina, the Prophet asked if he was muhsan, and upon confirmation ordered his stoning.
The hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim, indicating it is sound (sahih).
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference between muhsan and non-muhsan is the punishment: stoning versus one hundred lashes. This distinction is consistent across the Hanafi school.
There is no ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۵۱] (۸) فان كان الزاني محصنا رجمه بالحجارة حتى يموت آدمي (1) عاقل ہو (۲) بالغ ہو (۳) شادی شدہ ہو (۴) آزاد ہو (۵) مسلمان ہو تو اس کو حسن کہتے ہیں۔ پس اگر محصن آدمی زنا کرے تو اس کو سو کوڑے نہیں لگیں گے بلکہ پتھر سے مار مار کے ہلاک کر دیا جائے گا۔ حضرت ما عزا اور حضرت غامد یہ حسن تھے اس لئے ان کو پتھر مار کر ہلاک کیا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابا هريرة قال اتــی رســول الله رجل من الناس ... فقال احصنت ؟ قال نعم يا رسول الله ! قال اذهبوه فارجموه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب سوال الامام المترهل انت ؟ ص ۱۰۰۸ نمبر ۶۸۲۵ ر مسلم شریف ، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ج ثانی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۶۹۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زانی محصن ہو تو رجم کیا جائے گاور نہ تو زنا کے ثبوت کے بعد سو کوڑے لگیں گے۔
[2451] (8) So if the zani is muhsan, he is stoned with stones until he dies. A human (1) sane, (2) adult, (3) married, (4) free, (5) Muslim, then he is called muhsan. So if a muhsan person commits zina, he will not be given one hundred lashes, but rather will be killed by throwing stones. Hadrat Ma'iz and Hadrat Ghamidiyya were muhsan, so they were stoned to death. In the hadith: Narrated Abu Huraira: A man came to the Messenger of Allah... He said, 'Are you muhsan?' The man said 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah!' He said, 'Take him away and stone him.' (a) (Bukhari, Bab su'al al-imam al-muqirr hal inta? p.1008 no.6825; Muslim, Bab man i'tarafa 'ala nafsihi bi al-zina, p.66 no.1692) From this hadith it is understood that if the zani is muhsan, he will be stoned; otherwise, after proof of zina, one hundred lashes will be administered.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the punishment for a muhsan zani. The author first states the ruling: if the one who committed zina is muhsan, he is stoned with stones until death. He then defines the conditions for being muhsan: sane, adult, married (having validly consummated a marriage), free, and Muslim. These five conditions are the Hanafi criteria for ihsan. The author contrasts this with the punishment for a non-muhsan: one hundred lashes, as per the Quran. The evidence provided is the hadith of the man who came to the Prophet, confessed to zina, and when asked if he was muhsan and confirmed, the Prophet ordered his stoning. The author notes that the stoning of Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyya woman were based on their muhsan status. This is a well-established ruling in the Hanafi school, resting on the Sunnah and consensus.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who has all five qualities: sanity, adulthood, valid marriage, freedom, Islam; the punishment for zina is stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Having children

Key Takeaway
The muhsan zani is stoned to death; the muhsan conditions are sanity, adulthood, marriage, freedom, and Islam.

Procedure for Stoning: Order of Throwers and Effect of Witnesses Stopping
Ruling on the order of stoning and the condition of witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for stoning (rajm) and explain why the hadd is dropped if the witnesses stop stoning.

Core Idea
If witnesses stop stoning, their testimony is doubted, so the hadd is dropped.

This lesson covers the physical procedure of stoning as prescribed in the Hanafi school. You will learn the required sequence of throwers and the critical condition that the witnesses must follow through. The ruling emphasizes that the witnesses' actions reflect the certainty of their testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the required actions
Note that the condemned is taken to open ground, then the witnesses begin stoning, then the imam, then the general public. This sequence is prescribed.
The open ground is for practical reasons: ease of stoning and avoiding impurity in populated areas.
2
Evaluate the witnesses' role
Understand that the witnesses start the stoning because their testimony established the guilt. If they stop after beginning, it casts doubt on their certainty, so the hadd is dropped.
This is a key condition unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the rationale
The rule protects against executing an innocent person if the witnesses later recant or show hesitation.

[۲۴۵۲] (۹) يخرجه الى ارض ثم يبدا الشهود بالرجم ثم الامام ثم الناس وان بدا الشهود ورجموا ثم وقفوا سقط الحد عنه يخرجه الى ارض ثم يبدأ الشهود بالرجم ثم الامام ثم الناس۔ پس اگر گواہ شروع کرنے سے رک جائیں تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اگر گواہ کی گواہی کی وجہ سے زنا کا ثبوت ہوا ہو تو پہلے گواہ پتھر مارنا شروع کرے۔ پھر امام پتھر مارے۔ پھر لوگ پتھر مار کر ہلاک کرے۔ اور اگر گواہ پتھر نہ مارے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ گواہی دینے میں خامی ہے اس لئے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ میدان کی طرف لے جانے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لوگوں کو پتھر مارنے میں آسانی ہو اور لوگوں کو خون نہ لگے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔
[2452] (9) He takes him out to open ground, then the witnesses begin with stoning, then the imam, then the people. And if the witnesses begin and stone, then stop, the hadd is dropped from him. He takes him out to open ground, then the witnesses begin with stoning, then the imam, then the people. So if the witnesses stop from beginning, then hadd will be dropped. If zina was proven through the testimony of witnesses, then first the witnesses should start throwing stones. Then the imam throws stones. Then the people throw stones and kill him. And if the witnesses do not throw stones, it means there is a defect in the testimony, so the hadd is dropped. The reason for taking him to open ground is so that it is easy for people to throw stones and that people's blood is not splattered (2) There is evidence for this in hadith.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the physical procedure of stoning. The author states that the condemned is taken to open ground (outside the city to avoid impurity). Then the witnesses who testified against him begin the stoning, followed by the imam (the ruler or judge), and then the general public. The author adds a crucial condition: if the witnesses, after beginning to stone, stop, the hadd is dropped entirely. This is because their reluctance to participate casts doubt on their testimony. The Hanafi school places great emphasis on the witnesses' certainty and commitment. If the witnesses refuse to stone, it indicates they might not be fully confident, so the punishment is set aside. The reason for open ground is practical: to allow easy participation and avoid bloodshed in populated areas. The hadith evidence for this procedure is mentioned but not quoted explicitly here.

Key Terms
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as a punishment for zina committed by a married person.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes.
شهود (shuhud): Witnesses; in this context, the four witnesses who testified to the act of zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The hadd is dropped
C) The stoning continues with the imam
D) The witnesses are punished for their hesitation

Key Takeaway
The witnesses must initiate stoning and follow through; their reluctance voids the punishment.

Confession and Conditions for Muhsan in Zina
States the ruling on accepting confession and conditions for muhsan leading to rajm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for accepting a confession of zina and identify the five conditions that make a person muhsan, leading to the penalty of stoning.

Core Idea
A single confession is not enough; four consistent confessions and detailed questioning ensure the penalty is justly applied.

This passage from a Hanafi manual on hudud explains the careful procedure for accepting a confession of zina. The judge must reject the first three confessions to test the confessor's sincerity, and only after the fourth does he investigate the details. This thoroughness aims to prevent wrongful punishment and to distinguish between cases that require stoning versus flogging. The passage also defines muhsan — a free, adult, sane Muslim who has been married and consummated — for whom the penalty is stoning to death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is confessing to zina. The ruling is that the confession must be made four times, and the judge must question the confessor about the details before applying hadd.
The ruling is derived from the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ).
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the Sunnah of the Prophet (ﷺ) in the cases of Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyyah woman, where he ordered stoning after confession and asked about marital status.
This is a hadith ahad, so it is zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for establishing the ruling in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet (ﷺ) turned Ma'iz away multiple times before accepting his confession, indicating that a single confession is not sufficient. The Hanafi school derives the requirement of four separate confessions from this practice.
The judge's questioning about the nature, place, and partner of zina further confirms the need for clarity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While most schools also require four confessions, the Hanafi school uniquely requires the judge to reject the first three and to conduct a detailed investigation. Other schools may accept a single comprehensive confession after four utterances.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of caution (ihtiyat) in hudud.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi in the school, based on the clear precedent from the Prophet (ﷺ) and the aim of avoiding false convictions.
The judge must ensure all conditions of ihsan are met before ordering stoning.

(۷) پس جب اس کا اقرار چار مرتبہ پورا ہو جائے تو قاضی اس کو زنا کے بارے میں پوچھے کہ زنا کیا ہوتا ہے، وہ کیسے ہوتا ہے اور کہاں ہوا ، کس کے ساتھ کیا۔ پس جب اس کو بیان کر دے تو اس کو حد لازم ہوگی۔
اقرار کرنے والا چار مرتبہ اقرار کر لے تو قاضی اقرار کرنے والے کو زنا کی حقیقت پوچھے۔ یہ بھی پوچھے کہ وہ کیسے ہوتا ہے؟ یہ بھی پوچھے کہ وہ کہاں ہوا، کیونکہ اس کے اختلاف سے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ کس کے ساتھ کیا، کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ اقرار کرنے والا یہ سمجھے کہ فلاں کے ساتھ زنا کرنے سے حد لازم ہوگی حالانکہ بیٹے کی باندی سے زنا کرے تو حد لازم نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ ان ساری باتوں کا جواب صحیح صحیح دے دے تو قاضی زنا کا فیصلہ کرے گا۔
(۸) اگر زنا کرنے والا محصن ہے تو اس کو پتھر سے رجم کریں گے یہاں تک کہ وہ مر جائے۔ آدمی (1) عاقل ہو (۲) بالغ ہو (۳) شادی شدہ ہو (۴) آزاد ہو (۵) مسلمان ہو تو اس کو محسن کہتے ہیں۔ پس اگر محصن آدمی زنا کرے تو اس کو سو کوڑے نہیں لگیں گے بلکہ پتھر سے مار مار کے ہلاک کر دیا جائے گا۔ حضرت ما عزا اور حضرت غامدی یہ محصن تھے اس لئے ان کو پتھر مار کر ہلاک کیا۔
The Book of Hudud. From the sessions of the confessor: whenever he confesses, the judge rejects him. When his confession is completed four times, the judge asks him about zina: what it is, how it is, where he committed it, and with whom. When he explains that, the hadd becomes binding upon him. If the fornicator is muhsan, he is stoned with stones until he dies. (7) So when his confession is completed four times, the judge asks him about zina: what zina is, how it happens, where it happened, and with whom. Then when he explains it, the hadd becomes binding. The confessor confesses four times, then the judge asks the confessor about the reality of zina. He also asks how it happens, where it happened (because variation in that would drop the hadd), and with whom (because it is possible that the confessor thinks that committing zina with a certain person makes the hadd necessary, whereas if he commits zina with his son's slave-girl, the hadd is not necessary). If he answers all these matters correctly, the judge will decide the zina. (8) If the fornicator is muhsan, he is stoned, until he dies. A person is called muhsan if he is (1) sane, (2) adult, (3) married, (4) free, (5) Muslim. So if a muhsan man commits zina, he will not be given one hundred lashes, but will be killed by stoning. Hadhrat Ma'iz and Hadhrat Ghamidiyyah were muhsan, therefore they were killed by stoning.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi fiqh manual on the penal procedure for zina (fornication/adultery) when proven by confession. It specifies that a single confession is not sufficient; the judge must reject the first confession to ensure the confessor understands the consequences. Only after four consistent confessions does the judge investigate the details: the nature of zina, the manner, the place, and the partner. This thoroughness aims to eliminate any ambiguity that might nullify the hadd penalty, such as confusion about what constitutes zina or cases where the partner is a mahram or slave of a close relative, which change the ruling. The passage then defines muhsan: a free, adult, sane Muslim who has had valid marital intercourse. For a muhsan, the penalty is stoning to death (rajm), not flogging. This is based on the sunnah of the Prophet (ﷺ) with Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyyah woman. The Hanafi school holds that the judge's detailed questioning is obligatory (wajib) and that any variance in the confessor's answers can drop the hadd.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, adult, sane, Muslim, and has had valid marital intercourse; such a person is subject to stoning for zina.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession made by the accused; in hudud, it must be repeated four times and consistent.
حد (hadd): The fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific offenses, here stoning (rajm) for muhsan or lashing for non-muhsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
Four confessions and detailed questioning are required before the hadd penalty can be applied; a muhsan is stoned to death.

Procedure for Stoning and Order of Execution with Shafi'i Dispute
Details the order of stoning and discusses disagreement with Imam Shafi'i on whether witnesses must start.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of stoning for zina, explain the disagreement with Imam Shafi'i, and apply the rule to determine when hadd drops.

Core Idea
Hanafi law requires witnesses to initiate stoning; their refusal creates doubt that drops the penalty.

This lesson examines a key procedural disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the execution of rajm. The Hanafi school mandates that the witnesses who testified must cast the first stones; if they refuse, the penalty is dropped due to suspicion about their testimony. Imam Shafi'i holds that this order is only recommended, not obligatory. We'll explore the proofs and reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences of the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Begin by clearly stating what the Hanafi school requires regarding who starts the stoning. Note the consequence if witnesses refuse.
The text says: 'يبتدئ الشهود برجمه ثم الامام ثم الناس فان امتنع الشهود من الابتداء سقط'
2
Identify the Opposing View
Recognize that Imam Shafi'i disagrees: witnesses are not required to start; it is only mustahabb.
The text quotes the Shafi'i argument from the hadith of Ma'iz.
3
Follow the Opposing Proof
Examine the hadith of Ma'iz, where the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered stoning but did not stone first. Understand why the Shafi'i school sees this as evidence against obligation.
The Prophet's command was sufficient; his personal involvement was not necessary.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Understand how the Hanafi school distinguishes the Prophet's role as imam from that of ordinary witnesses. The witnesses' participation validates their testimony; hesitation indicates a defect.
The Hanafi school gives more weight to doubt (shubhah) in hudud cases.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: in Hanafi law, if witnesses refuse to stone, the hadd is completely dropped. In Shafi'i law, the stoning proceeds regardless.
This difference significantly affects the implementation of the penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يخرجه الى ارض فضاء يبتدئ الشهود برجمه ثم الامام ثم الناس فان امتنع الشهود من الابتداء سقط
(۹) زنا کرنے والے کو میدان کی طرف نکالے اور پہلے گواہ رحم کرنا شروع کرے پھر امام پھر لوگ۔ پس اگر گواہ شروع کرنے سے رک جائیں تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
اگر گواہ کی گواہی کی وجہ سے زنا کا ثبوت ہوا ہو تو پہلے گواہ پتھر مارنا شروع کرے۔ پھر امام پتھر مارے۔ پھر لوگ پتھر مار کر ہلاک کرے۔
اور اگر گواہ پتھر نہ مارے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ گواہی دینے میں خامی ہے اس لئے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ گواہوں کا پہلے مارنا ضروری نہیں ہے مارے تو اچھا ہے اور نہ مارے تو حد ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔ (۱) حضرت ما عر والی حدیث میں حضور نے دوسروں کو مارنے کے لئے فرمایا خود امام نے نہیں مارا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ قال نعم یا رسول الله إقال اذهبوا فارجموه اس حدیث مین حضور نے رجم کی ابتدا نہیں کی اس کے باوجود رجم کیا گیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہ کو مارنا ضروری نہیں ہے، البتہ مارے تو اچھا ہے
He takes him out to an open ground; the witnesses begin stoning him, then the imam, then the people. If the witnesses refrain from beginning, the hadd drops. (9) He takes the fornicator to a field, and first the witnesses start stoning, then the imam, then the people. So if the witnesses stop from starting, the hadd will drop. If the zina is proven by witness testimony, then the witnesses start stoning, then the imam, then the people stone until he dies. If the witnesses do not stone, it means there is a defect in the testimony, so the hadd drops. Imam Shafi'i says that it is not obligatory for the witnesses to stone first; if they do, it is good, and if they do not, the hadd will not drop. (1) In the hadith of Ma'iz, the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered others to stone, but he himself did not stone first. The hadith says: He said 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah.' He said 'Go and stone him.' In this hadith, the Prophet (ﷺ) did not begin the stoning, yet stoning was carried out, which shows that it is not obligatory for the witnesses to stone; it is good if they do.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the order of execution during stoning (rajm) for zina. The judge takes the convict to an open, level ground to facilitate stoning and avoid bloodshed in the city. The order is: first the witnesses (if the crime was proven by their testimony), then the imam (or judge), then the general public. According to the Hanafi school, if the witnesses refuse to cast the first stones, this indicates a possible flaw in their testimony (such as lack of certainty or a hidden doubt), and therefore the hadd penalty is dropped entirely. This is based on the idea that witnesses must be fully committed; hesitation nullifies their evidence. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the stoning order is not a condition for the validity of the penalty. He cites the hadith of Ma'iz, where the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered others to stone but did not stone first himself, and yet the stoning was valid. The Hanafi response (implied in the text) is that the Prophet's role as imam is unique; in his case, his command was sufficient, and he may have refrained to avoid personal involvement. For ordinary judges and witnesses, the order is obligatory. The Shafi'i school considers the witnesses' stoning as commendable (mustahabb) but not obligatory; if they refrain, the hadd is still carried out by the imam and the people.

Key Terms
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as a punishment for a muhsan fornicator.
شهود (shuhud): Witnesses who testified against the accused for zina.
سقوط الحد (suqut al-hadd): The dropping of the hadd penalty due to a doubt or procedural flaw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The imam stones first and the penalty is carried out
B) The penalty is dropped because doubt exists
C) The witnesses are punished for refusal
D) The penalty is converted to lashes

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates that witnesses initiate stoning; their refusal drops the hadd due to doubt, reflecting the principle that hudud are averted by ambiguities.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Order of Stoning: Witnesses Must Initiate or Not? Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Explains the order of stoning and the effect of witnesses' refusal with Shafi'i disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on who initiates stoning in a case of proven adultery, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the distinction between testimony and confession.

Core Idea
Witnesses must start stoning; if they refuse, the hadd falls—doubt repels the punishment.

Stoning (rajm) is a fixed punishment for a muhsan adulterer. An important procedural question arises: who begins the stoning? The answer depends on how the crime was proven—through the testimony of four witnesses or through the perpetrator's confession. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that witnesses must initiate the stoning, the Shafi'i objection, and the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi rule: In a case of adultery proven by the testimony of four witnesses, the witnesses must begin the stoning. If they refuse, the hadd is dropped because their refusal indicates possible doubt.
This obligation is based on the effect (athar) of ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and the principle that doubt repels the hadd.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the Shafi'i position: Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that witnesses beginning the stoning is not obligatory; it is only recommended (mandub). If they do not begin, the hadd is not dropped.
The Shafi'i school relies on hadiths where the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not initiate stoning himself.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: The hadith of Ma‘iz where the Prophet ordered others to stone but did not start, and the hadith of Anas where the Prophet did not participate in stoning after a confession.
These hadiths are cited to argue that initiation is not obligatory.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: Those hadiths involve confession, not testimony. In cases of confession, the imam starts. In cases of testimony, witnesses must start to remove any doubt about the reliability of their testimony.
The Hanafi school distinguishes the two modes of proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafi: if witnesses refuse to start, the hadd is dropped. Shafi'i: the hadd is still enforced.
This has direct implications for how courts proceed.

Source Text

فضاء يبتدئ الشهود برجمه ثم الامام ثم الناس فان امتنع الشهود من الابتداء سقط
اخبرني من سمع جابرا قال كنت فيمن رجمه فرجمناه بالمصلى فلما اذ لقته الحجارة جمز حتى ادركناه بالحرة فرجمناه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب سوال الامام المقر هل احصنت ؟ ص ۱۰۰۸ نمبر ۶۸۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ماعز کو عید گاہ کی طرف لے گئے جو مدینے سے باہر تھی اور مقام حرہ میں پتھر مارا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ میدان کی طرف لے جائے۔ پہلے گواہ پتھر مارے پھر امام مارے پھر لوگ مارے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ فقال له على... يا ايها الناس ان اول الناس يرجم الزاني الامام اذا كان الاعتراف. واذا شهد اربعة شهداء على الزنا اول الناس يرجم الشهود بشهادتهم عليه ثم الامام ثم الناس ثم رماها بحجر وكبر (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرحم والا حصان ج سابع ص ۳۲۶ نمبر ۱۳۳۵۰ سفن البیہقی ، باب من اعتبر حضور الامام والشهود و بداية الامام بالرحم الخرج ثامن، ص ۱۳۸۳ نمبر ۶۱۹۶۲ ر مصنف ابن ابی هیته نمبر ۲۸۸۰۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہی سے زنا ثابت ہوا ہو تو پہلے گواہ سنگسار کریں گے پھر امام پھر لوگ ۔ اور زانی کے اعتراف سے ثابت ہوا ہوتو پہلے امام پھر لوگ (۲) ابوداؤد میں اس کا ذکر ہے۔ حدثنا زکریا بن سلیم باسناده نحوه زاد ثم رماها بحصاة مثل الحمصة ثم قال ارموا والتقوا الوجه (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في المرأة التي امر النبي من الله بر جمعا من جمی یہ ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۴۴۴۴ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور جو امام وقت تھے پہلے انہوں نے حضرت غامدیہ کو کنکری ماری پھر باقی لوگوں کو کنکری مارنے کا حکم دیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعتراف کی شکل میں پہلے امام کنکری
مارے۔
اگر گواہ پہلے پتھر مارنے سے رک جائے تو یہ ممکن ہے کہ گواہی دینے میں کوئی شبہ ہو اور شبہ سے حد ساقط ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے حد ساقط ہو جائے
گی۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ گواہوں کا پہلے مارنا ضروری نہیں ہے مارے تو اچھا ہے اور نہ مارے تو حد ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔ (۱) حضرت ما عر والی حدیث میں حضور نے دوسروں کو مارنے کے لئے فرمایا خود امام نے نہیں مارا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ قال نعم یا رسول الله إقال اذهبوا فارجموه (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب سوال الامام المقر حل احصنت ؟ ص ۱۰۰۸ نمبر ۶۸۲۵ مسلم شریف ، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۹۹۲) اس حدیث مین حضور نے رجم کی ابتدا نہیں کی اس کے باوجود رجم کیا گیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہ کو مارنا ضروری نہیں ہے، البتہ مارے تو اچھا ہے (۳) خادم کے مسئلے میں بھی حضور نے حضرت انس کو فرمایا کہ جاؤ عورت اعتراف کرے تو رحم کر دینا۔ اور عورت نے اعتراف کیا تو رجم کر دیا جس میں حضور شامل نہیں ہوئے ۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے ۔ واغــد يـا انیس علی
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ میں رجم کرنے والوں میں سے تھا تو ہم نے عید گاہ کے قریب رجم کیا۔ پس جب ان کو پتھر لگا تو وہ بھاگے یہاں تک کہ ان کو مقام حرہ پر پایا پھر ہم نے ان کو رجم کیا (ب) حضرت علی نے ان سے کہا اے لوگو! زانی کو سب سے پہلے امام رحم کرے اگر اقرار کیا ہو۔ اور اگر چار آدمیوں نے زنا پر گواہی دی ہو تو لوگوں میں سب سے پہلے گواہ رجم کریں ان پر گواہی دینے کی وجہ سے، پھر امام ، پھر لوگ رجم کریں یہ کہ کر عورت کو پتھر مارا اور تکبیر کہی ( ج ) پھر عورت کو حضرت علی نے چنے کے برابر کنکری ماری پھر کہا تم لوگ پتھر مارو، ہاں ! چہرے پر نہ مارنا ( د ) حضرت ما عڑ نے فرمایا ہاں یارسول اللہ! کہا جاؤ ان کو رجم کرو۔
اس حدیث میں حضرت انس نے رجم کیا اور خو د حضور نے پتھر مارنا شروع نہیں کیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہ یا امام پہلے پتھر نہ مارے تو حد ساقی نہیں ہوگی۔
Chapter on Punishments. In the case (of stoning), the witnesses begin with stoning, then the imam, then the people. If the witnesses refuse to begin, it (the punishment) falls. (Narrated by one who heard Jabir: I was among those who stoned him; we stoned him at the musalla, and when the stones hit him, he ran until we caught him at al-Harrah and stoned him.) (a) This hadith indicates that... (the rest is Urdu commentary)
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage addresses the order of stoning in a case of proved adultery. The author begins by stating that when the penalty is established through the testimony of witnesses, the witnesses must initiate the stoning, followed by the imam (leader) and then the people. If the witnesses refuse to start, the penalty is dropped because their refusal may indicate doubt in the testimony, and doubt prevents the application of hadd. The author then presents the view of Imam al-Shafi‘i, who argues that it is not obligatory for witnesses to begin; rather, it is recommended. If they do not start, the hadd is not dropped. The Hanafi response relies on the action of ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and another hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not start the stoning himself, but ordered others to do so. However, the Hanafi school maintains that when proven by witnesses, they must start; when proven by confession, the imam starts. The passage concludes with the hadith of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) who stoned the woman after her confession, while the Prophet did not participate, showing that the hadd is not invalidated if the imam or witnesses do not start.

Key Terms
شهود (shuhūd): Witnesses who testify to adultery.
رجم (rajm): Stoning as a punishment for a muhsan (married) adulterer.
حد (hadd): The fixed punishment for certain crimes, here stoning for adultery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if witnesses testify to adultery but refuse to start stoning, what is the consequence?
A) The imam starts instead.
B) The hadd is dropped.
C) The witnesses are punished for false testimony.
D) The case is referred to another judge.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, for adultery proven by witnesses, the witnesses must initiate stoning; their refusal drops the punishment entirely.

The Imam Initiates Stoning Upon Confession
Ruling with proof on the order of stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who throws the first stone when the adulterer confesses, and apply the distinction between confession and testimony.

Core Idea
When adultery is proven by confession, the imam throws first, following the Prophet's example.

In hudud punishments, the procedure matters. This lesson specifies the correct order of stoning when the offender confesses. Unlike cases proven by witnesses, here the imam leads the stoning, not the witnesses. This ruling is based on the Prophet's own action with Ghamidiyyah and the practice of 'Ali.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mode of proof
Determine whether the adultery was proven by testimony or confession. The ruling differs: with testimony, witnesses start; with confession, the imam starts.
This distinction is key to understanding the rule.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
When the offender confesses, the imam throws the first stone, then the people follow.
This is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommendation), not wajib.
3
Trace the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of the Prophet stoning Ghamidiyyah first and then commanding others. Also, the athar of 'Ali supports this order.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that the imam starting is merely recommended, not a distinct rule. They do not differentiate between confession and testimony in this regard.
The practical effect is minimal, but the underlying usul differs.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Imagine a married man confesses to zina in court. The judge (imam) should pick up a small pebble and throw first, then the attendees throw. This follows the sunnah.
If the imam does not start, the stoning is still valid, but the sunnah act is missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۵۳] (۱۰) وان كان الزانى مقرا ابتدأ الامام ثم الناس [۲۴۵۳] (۱۰) پس اگر زنا کرنے والے نے اقرار کیا ہو تو امام شروع کرے پھر لوگ۔
زنا کرنے والے نے زنا کا اقرار کیا ہو اور اس کی وجہ سے زنا کا ثبوت ہوا ہو تو امام پہلے پتھر مارے پھر لوگ ماریں گے۔ او پر حدیث گزری کہ پہلے حضور نے غامدیہ کو کنکری ماری پھر لوگوں کو مارنے کا حکم دیا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ زاد ثـم رمـاهـا بحصاة مثل الحمصة ثم قال ارموا واتقوا الوجه (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف - باب في المرآة التي امرالنبی والے برجمها من جبیر یہ ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۴۴۴۴ (۲) اور حضرت علی کا اثر پہلے گزر گیا۔ (سن للبیہقی نمبر ۱۶۹۶۳/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ نمبر ۲۸۸۰۸/مصنف عبدالرزاق ،نمبر۱۳۳۵۰) جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ پہلے امام پھر لوگ پتھر ماریں گے۔
[2453] (10) And if the adulterer is confessing, the imam begins then the people. [2453] (10) So if the adulterer confessed and thereby the adultery is proved, then the imam should throw the first stone, then the people. The hadith already passed that the Prophet (peace be upon him) first threw a pebble at Ghamidiyyah, then ordered the people to throw. In the hadith: 'Then he threw a pebble like a chickpea, then said: Throw and avoid the face.' (b) (Abu Dawud...) And the effect of 'Ali has passed previously, which indicates that the imam throws first then the people.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof. The author states the rule: when a person confesses to adultery (and is therefore proven guilty by confession), the imam (the leader or judge) should initiate the stoning, and then the people follow. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the woman from Ghamid (Ghamidiyyah) who confessed. The Prophet himself threw the first small pebble as an example, then commanded others to throw but to avoid the face. Additionally, the effect of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) is cited in support. This distinguishes from the earlier case where testimony was used; there, the witnesses started.

Key Terms
مقر (muqirr): A person who confesses to adultery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The imam
C) The people
D) The confessor himself

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, upon confession of zina, the imam throws the first stone, following the sunnah; the witnesses initiate only when testimony is used.

Funeral Rites for the Stoned Adulterer
Ruling with Prophetic evidence on funeral rites for stoned adulterers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a person stoned for adultery is washed, shrouded, and prayed upon, and cite the Prophetic hadith as evidence.

Core Idea
A Muslim who dies by hadd punishment is still a believer and deserves full funeral rites.

When a Muslim is executed for a hadd crime like adultery, some might wonder whether they still deserve the dignity of Islamic funeral rites. This lesson clarifies that the Shariah treats them as any other deceased Muslim: they must be washed, shrouded, and prayed over. The Prophet's own practice with Ma'iz and Ghamidiyyah provides the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the funeral rites (washing, shrouding, prayer) for a person executed by stoning for adultery. The ruling is that these rites are obligatory (wajib).
Note: Ghusl and salat al-janazah are fard kifayah, while takfin is wajib, but all are required.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who ordered the prayer for Ma'iz and the Ghamidiyyah woman after stoning, and then had them buried.
The hadith is cited from Muslim, Bukhari, and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit command to perform the funeral prayer indicates that it is prescribed. By logical extension, washing and shrouding are also required as they are necessary prerequisites for the prayer.
The imperative 'amara' (he commanded) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the consensus
All four madhhabs agree that a Muslim executed for a hadd crime receives full funeral rites. There is no legitimate ikhtilaf on this point.
This strengthens the ruling's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۵۴] (۱۱) ويغسل ويكفن ويصلى عليه
[۲۴۵۴ (۱) اور غسل دیا جائے گا اور کفن دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی۔
زنا کے گناہ کی سزا پا چکا ہے تاہم وہ مومن ہو کر مرا ہے اس لئے عام مسلمانوں کی طرح اس کو نسل دیا جائے گا، کفن بھی دیا جائے گا اور اس پر نماز بھی پڑھی جائے گی اور دفن بھی کیا جائے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ غامد یہ اور حضرت ماعز پر نماز پڑھی گئی۔ ثم امر بها فصلى عليها و دفنت (ج) (مسلم شریف، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۴۴۳۲/۱۶۹۵ / بخاری شریف ، باب الرحم بالمصلی ص ۱۰۰۷ نمبر ۶۸۲۰ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی المرأة التي امر النبي برجمها من جبینیه ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۴۴۴۲ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رجم کے بعد اس پر نماز پڑھی جائے گی اور دفن کیا جائے گا۔ تو غسل اور کفن بھی دیئے جائیں گے۔ ابو داؤد شریف میں غامدیہ کے بارے میں ہے فاعناه على غسله وتكفينه و دفنه ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب رجم ما عز بن مالک ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۴۴۳۵)
[2454] (11) And he is washed, shrouded, and prayed upon. [2454] (1) And he will be given a bath, wrapped in a shroud, and funeral prayer will be performed for him. He has already received the punishment for the sin of adultery, but he died as a believer, so like other Muslims, he will be bathed, shrouded, prayed upon, and buried. Hadith: The Prophet ordered that the funeral prayer be performed for Ghamidiyyah and Ma'iz, and they were buried. This indicates that after stoning, funeral prayer is performed and burial occurs, so washing and shrouding also apply.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with evidence. The author states that a person who has been stoned for adultery (i.e., a married adulterer) should be given the same funeral rites as any other Muslim: washing, shrouding, funeral prayer, and burial. Even though the person died as a result of a criminal punishment, he or she died as a Muslim and has paid for the sin through the hadd. The proof is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with Ma'iz and the woman from Ghamid, both of whom were stoned and then had funeral prayers performed over them and were buried. The text cites hadiths from Muslim, Bukhari, and Abu Dawud to support this.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the deceased Muslim body before burial.
تكفين (takfīn): Shrouding the deceased in a burial cloth.
صلاة الجنازة (salāt al-janāzah): Funeral prayer performed over the deceased Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim who dies as a result of a hadd punishment remains a believer and is entitled to full Islamic funeral rites.

Punishment for Non-Muhsan Free Adulterer: 100 Lashes
Ruling that a non-muhsan free adulterer receives 100 lashes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the punishment of an unmarried free adulterer and identify the Quranic and Hadith proofs that establish it.

Core Idea
The Quran commands 100 lashes; the Sunnah specifies it for the unmarried, while the married are stoned.

This passage presents the foundational ruling for the hadd punishment of zina for a person who is not muhsan. The Quranic verse provides the general command, and the Prophet's Sunnah distinguishes between married and unmarried offenders, limiting lashes to the non-muhsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the act (zina by a non-muhsan free adult) and the prescribed punishment (100 lashes).
The ruling is a fixed hadd punishment, not a discretionary ta'zir.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
Read Surah al-Nur 24:2, which commands 100 lashes for the fornicator and fornicatress. Recognize that this is a clear, general command.
The verse uses the imperative 'فاجلدوا', indicating obligation.
3
Understand the specification via Hadith
The hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid shows the Prophet ordering flogging for the non-muhsan. This specifies that the Quranic verse applies to the unmarried, while the muhsan is stoned based on other hadiths.
The hadith is evidence of takhsis (specification) of the general Quranic command.
4
Note the distinction from muhsan
The punishment for a muhsan (free, married, consummated) is stoning, not lashes. This distinction is established by the Sunnah.
The definition of muhsan differs slightly between schools; Hanafi includes both spouses having had consummated marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۵۵] (۱۲) وان لم يكن محصنا وكان حرا فحده مائة جلدة
[۲۴۵۵] (۱۲) ۲۴۵۵ (۱۲) محسن نہ ہو اور آزاد ہو اس کی حد سو کوڑے ہیں۔
آیت میں ہے۔ الزانية والزانى فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة ( آيت ٢ سورة النور ۲۴) اس آیت میں زانی مرد اور زانیہ عورت کو سو کوڑے مارنے کا حکم ہے۔ لیکن حدیث کی بنا پر محسن اس سے الگ ہو گیا۔ اس لئے غیر محصن کو سوکوڑے ہی لگیں گے(۱) حدیث میں ہے کہ غیر محصن کو سو کوڑے لگیں گے۔ عن زيد بن خالد الجهني قال سمعت النبي الله يأمر فيمن زنى ولم يحصن جلد
حاشیہ : (الف) اے انہیں اس عورت کے پاس جاؤ اگر وہ اعتراف کرے تو اس کو رحم کر دینا۔ وہ ان کے پاس گئے میں انہوں نے اعتراف کیا تو حضرت انس نے
عورت کو رجم کیا (ب) پھر عورت کو چنے کے برابر کنکری سے مارا پھر فرمایا لوگو امار ولیکن چہرے پر نہ مارنا (ج) پھر حکم دیا تو حضرت غامد یہ پر نماز پڑھی اور دفن کیا۔
[2455] (12) And if he is not muhsan (free and not married) and is free, his punishment is one hundred lashes. [2455] (12) If he is not muhsan and is free, his hadd is 100 lashes. The verse says: 'The adulteress and the adulterer, flog each of them one hundred lashes' (Surah al-Nur, verse 2). This verse commands flogging for both male and female adulterers. But based on the hadith, the muhsan is excluded from this verse. So the non-muhsan receives 100 lashes. In the hadith: Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani said: I heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordering that those who commit adultery and are not muhsan be flogged. Footnote: (a) 'O Unays, go to this woman, if she confesses, then stone her.' He went, and she confessed, so Anas stoned the woman. (b) Then he threw a pebble like a chickpea at the woman, then said: 'People, throw, but avoid the face.' (c) Then he ordered, and the funeral prayer was performed for Ghamidiyyah and she was buried.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof. The author states that if an adulterer is not muhsan (i.e., unmarried or not in a valid marriage), and is free (as opposed to a slave), then the fixed punishment is 100 lashes. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Nur, 24:2) prescribes 100 lashes for both male and female adulterers in general. However, the Prophet's Sunnah specified that the muhsan (married person) is punished with stoning, not lashes. Therefore, the verse applies to the non-muhsan. The hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani is cited as evidence: the Prophet ordered flogging for those who commit adultery and are not muhsan. This establishes the distinction: stoning for the married, 100 lashes for the unmarried free person.

Key Terms
محصن (muḥṣan): A free person who has entered a valid marriage (even if not currently cohabiting).
جلد (jald): Flogging or lashing as a punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 100 lashes
C) 80 lashes
D) Imprisonment for one year

Key Takeaway
The Quranic command of 100 lashes applies to non-muhsan free adulterers, as specified by the Sunnah.

Order of Stoning When the Adulterer Confesses
Ruling on who initiates stoning upon confession of adultery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who initiates stoning upon the adulterer's confession and explain why it is sunnah not wajib based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The imam should start the stoning, but if he doesn't, the hadd remains valid — it is sunnah, not wajib.

This passage addresses the practical implementation of the hadd of stoning when the offense is proven by confession. The Hanafi school, drawing on Prophetic practice, establishes that the imam casts the first stone. However, the author clarifies that this is not a condition for the punishment's validity; it is a recommended sunnah. We will examine the evidence and the legal reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the stoning of an adulterer who confessed. The ruling: the imam should start, then the people.
2
Extract the hukm level
Is the imam's initiation wajib or sunnah? The text indicates sunnah because the hadd remains valid even if he does not start.
Hanafi principle: if an act is required for validity, it is rukn or shart; otherwise, it is sunnah.
3
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one where the Prophet threw the first stone at al-Ghamidiyyah, and another where Anas stoned without the Prophet starting. Also an athar from Ali.
The first hadith shows recommendation; the second shows non-obligation.
4
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet starting indicates it is good to do; his not starting (in Anas's hadith) shows that it is not a condition. Combined, they prove sunnah.
The athar of Ali reinforces the order but does not change the hukm level.
5
State the mufta bihi
The imam should start, but if he does not, the hadd is still valid. This is the operative position for fatwa.

الحد [۲۴۵۳] (۱۰) وان كان الزانى مقرا ابتدأ الامام ثم الناس (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الا اعتراف بالز ناص۱۰۰۸ نمبر ۶۸۲۷ مسلم شریف ، من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۲۹۸) اس حدیث میں حضرت انس نے رجم کیا اور خو د حضور نے پتھر مارنا شروع نہیں کیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہ یا امام پہلے پتھر نہ مارے تو حد ساقی نہیں ہوگی۔

And if the adulterer is confessing, the imam starts then the people. (الف) (Bukhari, chapter on confession of zinā, 1008 no. 6827; Muslim, chapter on one who confesses to zinā, p. 66 no. 1298) In this hadith, Anas stoned and the Prophet himself did not start throwing stones. From this it is known that if the witness or imam does not throw the first stone, the hadd is not invalid. [2453] (10) So if the adulterer has confessed, the imam should start then the people. The adulterer confessed adultery and due to that adultery is proven, so the imam should throw the first stone then the people will throw. The hadith passed that the Prophet first threw a pebble at al-Ghamidiyyah then commanded the people. In the hadith: 'Then he threw her a pebble like a chickpea, then said: Throw and avoid the face.' (ب) (Abu Dawud, chapter on the woman whom the Prophet commanded to be stoned from Jabiriyyah, p. 261 no. 4444) And the effect of Ali passed before. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi no. 16963, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah no. 28808, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq no. 13350) From this it is known that first the imam then the people throw stones.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding the implementation of the hadd of stoning (rajm) when the offender has confessed. According to the Hanafi school, the imam (judge or leader) should cast the first stone, followed by the general populace. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the case of al-Ghamidiyyah, where he threw the first stone and then instructed others. However, the text also clarifies that if the imam does not start, the hadd is not invalidated; it remains valid. This is derived from the hadith where Anas ibn Malik stoned without the Prophet starting. Thus, the imam's initiation is a recommended practice (sunnah) but not a condition for the validity of the punishment. The passage also cites an effect from Ali (may Allah honor him) to reinforce this order. The author uses the proof that if the imam does not start, the hadd still stands, which is a characteristic of recommended actions in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مقر (muqirr): One who confesses to a crime, here specifically to zina
حد (hadd): Prescribed punishment determined by divine law

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the imam's initiation of stoning upon confession is a sunnah; the hadd remains valid even if he does not start.

Washing, Shrouding, and Praying over the Stoned Offender
Ruling on funeral rites for a person executed by stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the funeral rites for a person executed by stoning and identify the Hadith evidence that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
A person stoned for a hadd crime remains a Muslim; he is washed, shrouded, and the funeral prayer is prayed over him.

This lesson addresses a specific case: a person executed by stoning for adultery. Some might think that such a person loses their Muslim status or is denied proper burial rites. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, affirms that the deceased is entitled to full Islamic funeral rites. We will examine the ruling and the evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the washing, shrouding, and funeral prayer over a person executed by stoning for adultery. The ruling is that these rites are obligatory (fard kifayah) upon the Muslim community.
The ruling aligns with the general obligation of janazah for all Muslims.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The author cites hadith reports from Muslim, Bukhari, and Abu Dawud regarding the Ghamidiyyah woman and Ma'iz ibn Malik, where the Prophet ﷺ commanded these rites after stoning.
The specific hadith in Abu Dawud explicitly says: 'He commanded us to wash her, shroud her, and bury her.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The Prophet's ﷺ command to perform ghusl, kafan, and burial after stoning indicates that the deceased remains a Muslim entitled to funeral rites. The hadd punishment does not remove Islamic identity.
This is a direct textual indication that the ruling applies universally to stoned offenders.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
There is no significant disagreement among the madhahib on this point. The ruling is mutually agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
All major schools affirm that a stoned person receives full Muslim funeral rites.
5
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
The practical effect is that the community must carry out the full janazah rites for a stoned offender, reinforcing that the hadd does not expel from Islam.
This contrasts with martyrs of battle who are not washed; the stoned person is washed like any other Muslim.

Source Text

This is based on the hadith of al-Ghamidiyyah and Ma'iz where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered these rites. The author notes that although the person died due to a prescribed punishment, they remain believers and deserve proper Islamic burial. This ruling emphasizes that the hadd does not remove the deceased's status as a Muslim.

Hadd for Non-Muhsan Free Person: 100 Lashes
Ruling on the fixed punishment for a free non-muhsan adulterer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadd for a free non-muhsan adulterer and identify the Quranic and hadith evidence for it.

Core Idea
The Quran commands 100 lashes for the non-muhsan free adulterer, and this is confirmed by mutawatir Sunnah.

This lesson examines a clear ruling from the Quran and Sunnah: the fixed punishment (hadd) for a free person who commits zina but is not muhsan (i.e., unmarried or never consummated a valid marriage). The Hanafi school applies the text literally, establishing the punishment as 100 lashes, with stoning reserved exclusively for the muhsan. We will explore the primary texts and the legal reasoning behind distinguishing between the two categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zina committed by a free person who is not muhsan. The ruling (hukm) for such a person is 100 lashes.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 24:2, which explicitly commands flogging with 100 lashes for both the male and female adulterer. The passage also cites a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim that affirms this punishment for the non-muhsan.
The hadith is from the chapter 'If a virgin commits zina, flog him and exile him'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fajlidu' (فاجلدوا) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The number '100' is explicit and unqualified for the non-muhsan. The distinction between muhsan and non-muhsan is established by the mutawatir Sunnah, which specifies stoning for the muhsan and lashes for the non-muhsan.
The dalala is considered zanni because the text applies generally, but the Sunnah specifies the category.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant ikhtilaf among the major schools on this ruling. All agree that the non-muhsan free person receives 100 lashes. The Hanafi school also includes the option of ta'zir (discretionary punishment) for exile, but the Quranic hadd remains 100 lashes.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Since there is no substantial disagreement, the ruling is taken as mufta bihi directly from the Quran and authentic hadith. The authority weight is zahir riwayah.
