Commentary
This passage states the punishment for a free person (i.e., not a slave) who commits zina but is not muhsan (i.e., not married or previously married and free). The hadd is one hundred lashes, as explicitly stated in the Quran (Surah al-Nur, verse 2). The text also cites a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim that confirms this ruling. The mention of 'free' excludes slaves, whose punishment is half (50 lashes). The condition of being muhsan is what differentiates between 100 lashes and stoning. Thus, the Hanafi school applies 100 lashes with possible exile for the non-muhsan free person.

Manner of Flogging: Medium Whip without Knots
Ruling on the type of whip and intensity of flogging for hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the type of whip and intensity of flogging for hadd, and identify the evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
A hadd flogging must be medium — neither harsh nor soft — using a whip without knots.

In this lesson, we examine the precise manner in which the hadd punishment of flogging is to be administered. The Hanafi school emphasizes moderation, ensuring the punishment fulfills its purpose without causing excessive harm. The passage draws on prophetic practice and companion action to define the proper whip and stroke intensity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its hukm
State the act (flogging for hadd) and its obligatory nature as per the Hanafi school.
The hukm is wajib based on the sunnah.
2
Recognize the conditions for the whip
The whip must be of medium thickness and without knots (thamarah).
A knot makes the whip severe; a broken whip is too soft.
3
Recognize the conditions for the strokes
The strokes must be of medium intensity—neither too hard nor too gentle.
Moderation avoids injury and ensures the punishment is effective.
4
Examine the evidence
Analyze the mursal hadith and the athar from Abu Barzah that the author cites.
Both narrations show the Prophet and a companion choosing a medium whip.
5
Understand the rationale
The goal is to implement the hadd without causing excessive harm, reflecting the Hanafi principle of avoiding harm (la darar).
The tip may be softened to prevent severe injury.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage details the manner of administering the flogging for hadd punishments. The whip should be of medium thickness, without knots (i.e., not severe). The strokes should be of medium intensity—neither too hard (which could kill or injure severely) nor too light (which would not fulfill the punishment). The text provides evidence from a mursal hadith and an athar from Abu Barzah. Additionally, there is a recommendation to soften the tip of the whip by crushing it between stones to avoid severe injury. The Hanafi school emphasizes moderation in execution of hadd, reflecting the principle of avoiding harm while implementing the divine command.

Removing Clothes for Flogging in Zina: A Specific Rule
Ruling on removing the offender's clothes before flogging for zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on removing clothes during flogging for zina and distinguish it from other hudud punishments.

Core Idea
For zina, clothes are removed to the waist-wrapper; for other hadd, clothes remain on.

The administration of hadd punishments in Islam is precise, with each crime having its own procedure. This passage from a Hanafi text clarifies a specific detail: how the offender should be dressed during flogging. The ruling distinguishes zina (adultery) from qadhf (false accusation) and shurb (drinking), relying on an athar (tradition) from the Tabi'i Qatada. Understanding this distinction ensures the punishment is carried out correctly and effectively.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon. Here, it is the removal of the offender's clothes prior to flogging for zina. The ruling is that clothes are removed down to the waist-wrapper (izar), while for qadhf and shurb, the clothes remain on.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The proof is an athar from Qatada, a Tabi'i, transmitted in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. This is considered reliable in Hanafi usul as reflecting the practice of the Companions. The text directly quotes the distinction.
The athar is: 'The slanderer and the drinker are flogged while their clothes are on them, and from the adulterer his clothes are removed until he is in his waist-wrapper.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The explicit differentiation between crimes shows that the ruling is specific to zina. The imperative ('are removed') indicates obligation (wujub) in the Hanafi understanding. The phrase 'until he is in his waist-wrapper' establishes the minimum covering (awrah) that must remain.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and thamarah al-khilaf
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih – other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may keep clothes on for all floggings, citing general covering of awrah. The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, the lashes strike bare skin for zina, increasing the deterrent effect; in other schools, the clothes absorb some force.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2457] (14) تنزع مائة وتغريب عام (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب وضع الرداء ج سابع ص 370 نمبر 13517) عن قتادة قال يجلد القاذف والشارب وعليهما ثيابهما وينزع عن الزاني ثيابه حتى يكون فى ازاره
His clothes are removed, and exile for one year. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on placing the cloak, vol. 7 p. 370 no. 13517) From Qatada: 'The slanderer and the drinker are flogged while their clothes are on them, and from the adulterer his clothes are removed until he is in his waist-wrapper.'
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage establishes that when administering the flogging for zina (adultery), the offender's clothes are to be removed except for the awrah (satr area). This is because the lashes should strike the skin directly for proper effect. However, for other hadd punishments such as qadhf (false accusation of zina) and shurb (drinking alcohol), the clothes are kept on. The athar from Qatada distinguishes between these punishments. The exile (taghrib) for one year is also mentioned as an additional punishment for the non-muhsan, though the text focuses on the clothing ruling. The Hanafi school holds that for zina, the clothes are removed down to the waist-wrapper (izar), while the awrah remains covered.

Key Terms
ازار (izar): Waist-wrapper covering from navel to knees
تغريب (taghrib): Exile for a period of one year as an additional punishment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Whip and Moderate Striking in Hadd Punishments
Ruling on the type of whip and moderate force for flogging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid whip in hadd flogging and explain why moderate striking is wajib according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The whip for hadd must be without knots and striking must be moderate – neither harsh nor soft.

In hadd punishments involving flogging, the Hanafi school prescribes specific rules for the whip and the manner of striking to ensure justice and mercy. This lesson examines the textual evidence from the Prophet's practice and the Sahaba, establishing that the whip must be free of knots and the striking must be moderate. Understanding these conditions prevents excessive harm while upholding the prescribed penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The ruling concerns the physical implementation of hadd flogging. The Hanafi school holds that using a whip without knots and striking moderately is wajib (obligatory). Determine the act being regulated and the legal classification.
The ruling is part of the sunnah method for executing hadd.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is a mursal hadith where the Prophet rejected both a knotted whip and a broken whip, choosing a middle one. Also, an athar from Abu Barzah demonstrates moderate flogging. Identify these sources.
Mursal hadith and athar are zanni in transmission but accepted in ahkam.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the Prophet's rejection of extreme whips and command to use the middle whip indicates the desired whip characteristics. Also, the athar explicitly states moderate flogging. Derive the legal implication.
The term 'sawt la thamara lahu' (whip without knots) and 'darban mutawassitan' (moderate striking) are directly derived.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi school holds this as wajib, other schools may allow some flexibility. Identify the cross-madhhab status.
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih; Hanafi emphasizes strict adherence to the sunnah method.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is from the zahir al-riwayah and is the mufta bihi. Confirm that no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists.
The ruling is clear and relied upon without significant dispute among Hanafis.

مرسل حدیث میں ہے۔ عـن یحیی بن ابی کثیر ان رجلا جاء الى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا رسول الله اني اصبت حدا فاقمه على فدعا رسول الله الله بسوط جديد عليه ثمرته فقال لا سوط دون هذا فاتي بسوط مكسور العجز فقال لا، سوط فوق هذا فاتى بسوط بين السوطين فامر به فجلد (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب ضرب الحدود وهل ضرب النبي بالسوط؟ ج سابع ص ۳۶۹ نمبر ۱۳۵۱۵/ مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ١٠٠، ما جاء في الضرب في الحدج خامس ص ۵۲۴ نمبر ۲۸۶۶۴) اس حدیث مرسل سے معلوم ہوا کہ درمیانہ کوڑے سے مارے۔ بہت طاقت سے نہ مارے اور نہ بہت آہستہ مارے۔
اثر میں ہے۔ شهدت ابا برزة اقام الحد على امة له في دهليزه وعنده نفر من اصحابه فقال اجلدها جلدا بين الجـلـدين وليس بالممطى ولا بالتخفيف (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۱۰ اما جاء فی الضرب في الحدج خامس ص ۵۲۴ نمبر ۲۸۶۶۷ / مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب ضرب الحدود وصل ضرب النبی ریا له بالسوط ؟ ج سابع ص ۳۷۰ نمبر ۱۳۵۱۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ درمیانہ مار. مارے۔ ایک روایت میں ہے کہ کوڑے کا اگلا حصہ پتھر سے چور کر دے۔ ثم يدق بين حجرين حتى يلين ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۱۰۰، فی السوط من یا مر به ان يدق ج خامس ص ۵۲۵ نمبر ۲۸۶۷۴)
[2456] (13) The imam orders him to be struck with a whip that has no knot, a moderate strike. [2456) (13) The imam will give permission to strike with a whip that has no knot, moderate strike. The hadd of zina, hadd of wine, hadd of qadhf, etc. in which the criminal is struck with a whip, such a whip is used that is not very hard and not very soft, but of a medium type so that it is a warning and the person is not severely wounded. In a mursal hadith: From Yahya ibn Abi Kathir: A man came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have committed an offense requiring a hadd penalty, so apply it to me.' The Messenger of Allah called for a new whip that had a knot. He said, 'No, a whip less than this.' Then a whip with a broken end was brought. He said, 'No, a whip above this.' Then a whip between the two was brought, and he ordered him to be flogged. (b) From this mursal hadith it is known that he should be struck with a medium whip. He should not strike with great force nor very gently. In an athar: I witnessed Abu Barzah carrying out the hadd on a slave girl of his in his vestibule, and with him were a number of his companions. He said, 'Flog her with a flogging between the two floggings, neither stretched nor light.' (c) From this athar it is known that moderate flogging should be done. In one narration: The front part of the whip should be crushed with a stone, then it is beaten between two stones until it becomes soft.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the type of whip and the manner of striking in hadd punishments. The text begins with the matn stating that the imam orders flogging with a whip that has no knots (i.e., not braided with knots) and that the striking should be moderate. The sharh expands by explaining that this applies to all hadd punishments involving flogging, such as for zina, drinking alcohol, and false accusation (qadhf). The whip must be neither very harsh nor very soft, but of a medium quality so that it serves as a deterrent without causing severe injury. The proof is a mursal hadith from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir in which the Prophet (ﷺ) rejected a new whip with a knot and a broken whip, settling for one in between. This indicates the ideal whip is without knots and of moderate condition. Another athar from Abu Barzah reports that he flogged a slave girl with a flogging that was 'between the two floggings'—neither stretched (i.e., too hard) nor light. Furthermore, it is mentioned that the tip of the whip should be crushed between stones to soften it, ensuring it is not too harsh. Thus, the Hanafi position is clear: the whip must be free of knots, and the flogging must be moderate, not excessive.

Key Terms
سوط لا ثمرة له (sawt la thamara lahu): A whip without knots; thamara refers to the knots or braiding on the whip.
ضربا متوسطا (darban mutawassitan): Moderate striking, neither too harsh nor too light.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Any whip available at the time

Ruling on Removing Clothes During Flogging
Ruling with proof on clothing during flogging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the removal of clothes during flogging for men and women, and identify the proofs from athar and hadith.

Core Idea
Men's clothes are removed except the izar; women's clothes stay on – because her whole body is 'awrah.

This lesson examines the proper procedure for executing the hadd of flogging. The Hanafi school distinguishes between male and female offenders: for a man, excess clothing is removed to ensure the lash lands effectively, but his 'awrah must remain covered. For a woman, her clothes are not removed because her entire body is 'awrah. We will explore the proofs from the athar of Qatada and the hadith of Ghamidiyyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is flogging as a hadd punishment. The ruling: for a man, remove all clothes except the izar; for a woman, keep her clothes on and make them tight.
The ruling is part of the proper execution of the hadd.
2
Locate the dalil for men
The athar from Qatada in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: the qadhif and wine drinker are flogged with clothes on, but the adulterer's clothes are removed until he is only in his izar.
This shows a distinction based on the type of crime.
3
Locate the dalil for women
The hadith of Ghamidiyyah: the Prophet ordered her clothes to be tied tightly before stoning. Also an athar from Ma'mar that a woman is flogged sitting with clothes on.
Women's clothes remain due to their entire body being 'awrah.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
For men, the 'awrah must remain covered (haram to uncover), but other clothes are removed for effective striking. For women, her whole body is 'awrah, so clothes remain.
The difference is based on modesty and the definition of 'awrah.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may not differentiate between men and women in this ruling, but the Hanafi position is based on the specific proofs.
Ikhtilaf is a legitimate area of scholarly difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(2457) (14) Remove the clothes from his body. If he is a man, keep a cloth on his private parts and remove the rest of the clothes, then flog him. Do not uncover the private parts because uncovering the private parts is haram. The clothes are removed so that the flogging lands appropriately. Especially thick clothes should be removed. (2) In an athar: Qatada said, 'The one accused of false accusation (qadhif) and the wine drinker are flogged while their clothes are on, but the adulterer's clothes are removed until he is only in his izar.' (w) From this athar it is known that the extra clothes of a man are removed. However, a woman's clothes are not removed because her entire body is 'awrah. In the hadith of Ghamidiyyah: 'The Prophet ordered that her clothes be tied tightly on her, then he ordered that she be stoned.' (a) (Abu Dawud) In this hadith, the woman's clothes were wrapped and then she was stoned. (2) From Ma'mar: 'I was informed that a woman is flogged sitting, with her clothes on, in the hadd.' (b) From this athar it is known that a woman is flogged with her clothes bound on her.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the removal of the criminal's clothes during flogging. The matn states that the clothes are removed from his body. The sharh explains the details: for a man, a cloth covering the 'awrah (private parts) must remain, but other clothes are removed to ensure the striking lands properly. It is haram to uncover the 'awrah. For a woman, her clothes are not removed because her entire body is 'awrah; rather, they are tied tightly on her. The proof for men is an athar from Qatada: the qadhif (false accuser) and the wine drinker are flogged with their clothes on, but the adulterer's clothes are removed until he is only in his izar. The proof for women is the hadith of Ghamidiyyah, where the Prophet ordered her clothes to be tied tightly before stoning, showing that a woman's clothes remain. Also, an athar from Ma'mar states that a woman is flogged sitting with her clothes on. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between men and women: men's excess clothing is removed, women's clothing remains.

Key Terms
ستر (sitr): The private parts that must be covered; here it refers to the izar worn during flogging.
ازار (izar): A waist-wrapper covering the lower body from navel to knees.

Distribution of Flogging Strokes Over the Body
Ruling on flogging distribution with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on distributing flogging strokes and explain the evidence from the practice of Ali (RA).

Core Idea
Strikes in hadd flogging are wajib to distribute, avoiding head, face, and private parts.

This lesson covers the physical method of administering flogging in hudud punishments. The Hanafi school requires that strokes be spread over the limbs and not concentrated on one area, and that the head, face, and private parts be avoided entirely. This ruling is based on a directive from Ali (RA) and is considered obligatory to prevent excessive harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the matn: the strokes are distributed over the limbs except the head, face, and private parts. Also note the differentiation for slaves: fifty lashes.
The ruling applies to both free and slave offenders, with the number of lashes adjusted for slaves.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The proof cited is a statement from Ali (RA): 'Give each limb its right and avoid his face and genitals.' This is recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi (statement of a Companion), which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
Ali's command to 'give each limb its right' implies that strokes must be distributed across the body, not concentrated. The explicit prohibition of the face and genitals establishes the exempted areas.
The imperative 'give' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the epistemological weight
The evidence is zanni in both transmission and meaning, so the ruling is considered wajib (obligatory) rather than fard (definitive).
This classification affects the level of bindingness.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
While most schools agree on avoiding the face and genitals, the Hanafi emphasis on distribution and the specific evidence from Ali may differ from other schools that rely on other proofs.
The practical consequence is that Hanafi flogging is more regulated to prevent injury.

Hadd Flogging for Slaves in Zina: The Ruling of Fifty Lashes
Ruling on the number of stripes for slaves in hadd flogging

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of lashes for slaves convicted of zina and identify the Quranic and sunnah proofs that support it.

Core Idea
The Quran explicitly halves the hadd for slaves — fifty instead of one hundred lashes.

This lesson examines a clear-cut ruling from the Hanafi school: the hadd punishment for zina when the offender is a slave. While the free person receives one hundred lashes, the slave receives exactly fifty. The proof is direct and unambiguous — a Quranic verse that states 'half the punishment' — and is further confirmed by the practice of the Caliph Umar. Understanding this ruling illustrates how the Shariah takes into account the reduced culpability of slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) committed by a slave. The Hanafi ruling is that the slave receives fifty lashes, half of the free person's punishment.
This applies to both male slaves (abd) and female slaves (amah).
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The primary proof is the Quranic verse 4:25, which explicitly states that for slave women (who commit zina), the punishment is half of that for free women.
The verse is: 'But if they commit immorality, then on them is half the punishment prescribed for free women.'
3
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'half the punishment'. This is a clear (zahir) textual indication that the hadd for slaves is one-half of the free person's hadd.
In Hanafi usul, such explicit wording is qat'i in dalalah (definitive in meaning).
4
Confirm with secondary evidence (athar)
The passage cites an athar (report) from the Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab, who ordered fifty lashes for slave girls belonging to the government. This is a qawl sahabi (companion's statement) that corroborates the Quranic ruling.
The athar strengthens the proof and demonstrates the early practice.
5
Note the extension by qiyas
Though the Quranic verse explicitly addresses female slaves, the ruling is extended to male slaves by qiyas (analogy). The effective cause (illa) is the state of being a slave, which diminishes legal capacity and responsibility.
This extension is unanimously accepted by the Hanafi school and is also reflected in the matn's statement 'and likewise the female slave' — showing both are treated equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۵۹] (۱۲) وان كان عبدا جلده خمسين وكذلك الامة.

تشر آزادز نا کرے تو اس کو سو کوڑے لگتے ہیں اور غلام یا باندی زنا کرے تو اس کا آدھا ہوگا یعنی پچاس کوڑے لگیں گے۔ آیت میں ہے۔ فان اتين بفاحشة فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب (و) ( آیت ۲۵ سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام باندی پر آزاد سے آدھی سزا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ امرنی عمر بن الخطاب في فتية من قريش فجلدنا ولائد من ولائد الامارة خمسين خمسين في الزنا (ه) (سن للبیہقی ۳۴ باب ماجاء فی حدالمالک ج خامس ص ۲۹۷ نمبر ۱۷۰۸۹ر مصنف ابن ابی هیبت ۴۸ فی الامته والعبد یز نیان ج خامس ص ۴۲۲، نمبر ۲۸۳۷۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ باندی اور غلام کو زنا میں پچاس کوڑے
[2459] (12) And if he is a slave, he is flogged fifty, and likewise the female slave. Shar'an: If a free person commits zina, he gets one hundred lashes, and if a male slave or female slave commits zina, it will be half, i.e., fifty lashes. In the verse: 'But if they commit immorality, then on them is half the punishment prescribed for free women.' (Quran 4:25) From this verse it is known that the punishment for a slave is half of that of a free person. (2) In an athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab ordered me, along with some youth of Quraysh, and we flogged some slave girls belonging to the government fifty lashes each for zina.' (h) From this athar it is known that a female slave and a male slave are given fifty lashes for zina.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the number of lashes for slaves in hadd flogging for zina. The matn states that if the offender is a slave (abd or amah), he is flogged fifty stripes. The sharh explains that a free person gets one hundred lashes, while a slave gets half. The proof is the Quranic verse 4:25, which explicitly says that for slave women, the punishment is half of that for free women. Qiyas extends this to male slaves as well. Additionally, an athar from Umar shows that he ordered fifty lashes for slave girls. This confirms the Hanafi ruling that the hadd for a slave is half of that for a free person, i.e., fifty lashes.

Key Terms
عبد (abid): A male slave; here, refers to an owned person who commits zina.
الأمة (al-amah): A female slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many lashes does a female slave receive for zina?
A) 20 lashes
B) 50 lashes
C) 100 lashes
D) 80 lashes

Key Takeaway
The hadd for zina for slaves is fixed at fifty lashes, half the free person's punishment, based on the explicit text of Quran 4:25 and confirmed by the practice of Umar.

Distribution of Lashes in Hadd Punishment
Ruling on distribution of lashes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how lashes are to be distributed in a hadd punishment, identify the three areas that must be avoided, and explain the dalil from the athar of Ali (ra).

Core Idea
Las-hes must be spread over the body, sparing the head, face, and private parts.

When a fixed penalty (hadd) requires lashing, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific method to prevent harm and uphold dignity. This lesson examines the ruling that lashes must be distributed across the limbs, not concentrated, and that three sensitive areas are exempt. We will trace the evidence from an athar of Sayyidina Ali (ra) and understand its legal implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the administration of lashes in a hadd punishment. The ruling is that lashes must be distributed over the limbs (not all on one spot) and must avoid the head, face, and private parts.
This is a ruling on how to execute the punishment, not on the punishment itself.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar (narration) from Sayyidina Ali (ra), recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. He instructed a man regarding a hadd: 'Strike and give each limb its due, and avoid his face and his private parts.'
This is a qawl sahabi, considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'adrib' (strike) and 'a'ti' (give) indicate obligation (wujub). The verb 'ijtanib' (avoid) indicates prohibition. Thus, distributing lashes and avoiding the face and private parts are wajib.
The head is also avoided by analogy or because it is included in 'face' context.
4
Note the exception
The three exceptions are the head, face, and private parts. The rationale is that these are sensitive areas where striking could cause severe injury or death.
Other limbs receive an equal distribution of lashes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُفرَّق الضرب على أعضائه إلا رأسه ووجهه وفرجه [۲۴۵۸] (۱۵) اور متفرق کئے جائے ضرب اس کے اعضاء پر سوائے اس کے سر اور چہرہ اور شرمگاہ کے۔ جسم کے ایک حصے پر تمام ضر ہیں نہ ماریں بلکہ الگ الگ عضو پر مارے، البتہ سر، چہرہ اور شرم گاہ پر نہ مارے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ قال اتی عليا رجل في حد فقال اضرب واعط كل عضو حقه واجتنب وجهه ومذاكيره (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ضرب الحدود وهل ضرب النبی والے بالوط؟ ج سابع ص ۳۷۰ نمبر ۱۳۵۱۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مختلف اعضاء پر کوڑا مارے، البتہ چہرہ ، شرمگاہ اور سر پر نہ مارے کیونکہ یہ نازک اعضاء ہیں۔
The lashing is distributed over his limbs except his head, face, and private parts. [Commentary:] And the lashing is made to fall on different limbs, not all on one part, but on each limb separately, except the head, face, and private parts should not be struck. There is an athar: 'A man came to Ali regarding a hadd punishment, so he said: Strike and give each limb its due, and avoid his face and his private parts.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq...) From this athar it is understood that the whip should be struck on different limbs, but not on the face, private parts, and head because they are sensitive parts.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on how the lashing of a hadd punishment should be administered. The lashing must be distributed over the various limbs of the body, not concentrated on one area. Three areas are specifically excluded: the head, the face, and the private parts. The proof comes from an athar (narration) of Sayyidina Ali (ra) who instructed to give each limb its due and to avoid the face and private parts. This indicates the obligation (wujub) of distributing the lashes and avoiding these sensitive areas. The wisdom is to prevent severe harm or death and to maintain dignity.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed corporal punishment determined by Shari'ah for specific crimes such as zina.
ضرب (darb): Lashing, the act of striking with a whip as a punishment.
عضو (udhw): Limb or part of the body; the lashes are to be distributed over different limbs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Head, face, and private parts
B) Head, face, and feet
C) Back, stomach, and legs
D) Only the face

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, hadd lashes must be distributed over the body, avoiding the head, face, and private parts, based on the authoritative instruction of Sayyidina Ali (ra).

Hadd Punishment for Slaves: Fifty Lashes
Ruling with proof for slave's hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadd punishment for slaves committing zina, cite the Quranic proof (4:25), and explain the role of qiyas in extending the ruling to male slaves.

Core Idea
A slave’s hadd for zina is half that of a free person: fifty lashes, as the Quran explicitly decrees.

This passage addresses the specific punishment for slaves and bondswomen who commit zina. While a free person receives 100 lashes, the Quran explicitly states that a slave's punishment is half, i.e., 50 lashes, and this is confirmed by the practice of Caliph Umar. We will examine the textual evidence and the logical extension to male slaves via qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the exact punishment for a male slave (abd) and a female slave (amah) who commit zina according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling is 50 lashes for both.
2
Cite the primary dalil (Quran)
Locate the Quranic verse (al-Nisa 4:25) and note that it explicitly mentions 'half of what is prescribed for free women' regarding slave women.
The verse uses the word 'nisf' (half).
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the verse proves the ruling: the text directly gives half punishment for female slaves; by qiyas (analogy), the same applies to male slaves because the common reason (illa) is servitude.
The Hanafi school applies qiyas here, though some scholars may differ on the method.
4
Confirm secondary dalil (athar)
Consider the practice of Caliph Umar who ordered 50 lashes for slave-girls, which corroborates the Quranic ruling and shows practical application.
This athar serves as supporting evidence (shahid).
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
Confirm that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is 50 lashes for all slaves (male and female) without dispute among the three imams.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon across all schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان عبدا جلده خمسين وكذلك الامة. تشریح: آزاد زنا کرے تو اس کو سو کوڑے لگتے ہیں اور غلام یا باندی زنا کرے تو اس کا آدھا ہوگا یعنی پچاس کوڑے لگیں گے۔ آیت میں ہے۔ فان اتین بفاحشة فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب (و) ( آیت ۲۵ سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام باندی پر آزاد سے آدھی سزا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ امرنی عمر بن الخطاب في فتية من قريش فجلدنا ولائد من ولائد الامارة خمسين خمسين في الزنا (ه) (سن للبیہقی ۳۴ باب ماجاء فی حدالمالک ج خامس ص ۲۹۷ نمبر ۱۷۰۸۹ر مصنف ابن ابی هیبت ۴۸ فی الامته والعبد یز نیان ج خامس ص ۴۲۲، نمبر ۲۸۳۷۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ باندی اور غلام کو زنا میں پچاس کوڑے
And if he is a slave, he is lashed fifty, and likewise a bondswoman. [Commentary:] Explanation: If a free person commits zina, he gets one hundred lashes; and if a slave or bondswoman commits zina, his punishment will be half, i.e., fifty lashes. In the Quran: 'And if they commit a shameful deed, then their punishment is half of what is prescribed for free women' (Quran 4:25). From this verse it is understood that the punishment for a slave and bondswoman is half of that for a free person. And there is an athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab ordered us, a group of youths from Quraysh, so we lashed some slave-girls of the imarah with fifty lashes each for zina.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...) From this athar, it is understood that a bondswoman and slave receive fifty lashes for zina.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage gives the distinct ruling for slaves and bondswomen in the hadd of zina. While a free person receives 100 lashes, a slave receives 50. This is based on the explicit Quranic text (Surah al-Nisa, 4:25) which states that the punishment for slave women is half of that for free women. The same applies to male slaves. The ruling is further supported by the practice of Caliph Umar, who ordered fifty lashes for slave-girls. This establishes the Hanafi position that the hadd for slaves is exactly half of the free person's punishment.

Key Terms
عبد (abd): A male slave; his hadd for zina is 50 lashes.
امة (amah): A female slave (bondswoman); her hadd is 50 lashes.
نصف (nisf): Half; the slave's penalty is half of the free person's.

Retraction Nullifies Hadd: Confession is Not Final
Ruling with proof on retraction nullifying hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of confession in hadd cases and explain the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Retraction of confession nullifies the hadd — even during its execution.

Confession (iqrar) is one of the ways to establish a hadd punishment, but Hanafi fiqh treats confession as a revocable evidence. The Prophet ﷺ regretted that the people did not leave Ma'iz when he fled during stoning, indicating that retraction would have dropped the hadd. This lesson explores the rule and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Clearly state the Hanafi rule: if the confessor retracts before or during the execution of the hadd, the hadd is dropped and the person is released.
This applies to all hadd crimes (zina, theft, qadhf, etc.) where confession is the basis.
2
Locate the Dalil
Two main proofs: (1) The hadith of Ma'iz – the Prophet's statement 'Why did you not leave him?' (2) The athar from Umar offering a woman to retract.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear (dalala qati') in the Hanafi view.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet's disapproval of executing Ma'iz when he fled shows that if he had retracted (by fleeing), the hadd should have been lifted. Umar's explicit offer to a woman confirms the same principle.
The legal principle: 'Avert hadd by doubts' (dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat) supports accepting retraction as a doubt.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., some Shafi'i jurists) do not accept retraction after the confession is confirmed by the judge. The Hanafi school accepts it even during execution.
The practical consequence (thamarah): in Hanafi law, the hadd is abandoned; in other views, the execution continues.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) and is based on the stronger textual evidence and the principle of avoiding hadd when possible.
This is the view of the majority of the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن رجع المقر عن إقراره قبل إقامة الحد عليه أو في وسطه خلي سبيله [۲۴۹۰] (۱۷) اگر اقرار کرنے والا اپنے اقرار سے رک جائے اس پر حد قائم ہونے سے پہلے یا اس کے درمیان تو اس کا رجوع کرنا قبول کیا جائے گا اور اس کو چھوڑ دیا جائے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ فذكروا ذلک لرسول الله الله انه فرحين وجد مس الحجارة ومس الموت فقال رسول الله هلا تر کنموه (الف) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی در و الحد عن المعترف اذار جمع ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۱۴۲۸) ابو داؤد شریف میں یہ بھی ہے۔ هلا تركتموه لعله ان يتوب فيتوب الله عليه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب رجم ماعزبن مالک ص ۲۵۸، نمبر ۴۴۱۹ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تم نے حضرت ماعز کو چھوڑ کیوں نہ دیا۔ اگر وہ توبہ کر لیتے اور اقرار سے رجوع کر لیتے تو اللہ ان کی توبہ قبول کر لیتا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقرر جوع کرلے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن شداد ان امرأة رفعت الى عمر اقرت بالزنا اربع مرات فقال ان رجعت لم نقم عليك فقالت لا يجتمع على امران (ب) مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۷ افی الرجل والمرأة يقران بالحد ثم ینکر انہج خامس ص ۵۴۰ نمبر (۲۸۸۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اقرار کے بعد انکار کر دے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
If the confessor retracts his confession before the establishment of the hadd upon him, or during it, he is released. [Commentary:] If the confessor retracts his confession before the hadd is carried out or during it, his retraction will be accepted and he will be let go. There is a hadith: 'They mentioned to the Messenger of Allah that when he felt the stones and felt death, he fled. So the Messenger of Allah said: Why did you not leave him?' (Tirmidhi...) And in Abu Dawud: 'Why did you not leave him? Perhaps he would repent and Allah would forgive him.' From this hadith it is understood that if the confessor retracts, the hadd is dropped. And there is an athar: 'A woman was brought to Umar who confessed to zina four times. He said: If you retract, we will not carry out the hadd upon you. She said: Two matters cannot be combined upon me.' From this athar it is understood that after confession, if he denies, the hadd is dropped.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage presents a key procedural rule in Hanafi hadd law: the confession that initiates the hadd punishment can be retracted before or even during the execution of the punishment. The retraction is accepted, and the punishment is dropped. The proof is from the famous incident of Ma'iz ibn Malik, where the Prophet (SAW) regretted that the people did not leave him when he fled, indicating that retraction would have nullified the hadd. Additionally, Caliph Umar offered a woman the option to retract, showing the practical application. This ruling emphasizes the principle that confessions are suspect and that the hadd is to be avoided if possible. The Hanafi school strongly upholds this.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession; the admission of guilt by the accused.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction; withdrawing one's confession.
سقوط (suqut): Nullification/falling; the hadd becomes void upon retraction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a retraction of confession nullifies the hadd, based on the Prophet's (SAW) statement 'Why did you not leave him?'

Imam Should Suggest Retraction to Confessor
Recommendation for imam to prompt retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (mustahabb) for the imam to prompt a confessor's retraction and identify the prophetic dalil.

Core Idea
The imam should gently prompt a confessor to retract, following the Prophet's example with Ma'iz, to avert hadd.

When a person confesses to a hadd offense like zina, the imam (judge) is not required to immediately apply the punishment. Islamic law encourages averting hudud through doubts. This lesson examines the recommended act (mustahabb) for the imam to gently suggest that the confessor may have done a lesser act, thus giving an opportunity to retract. The proof comes from the Prophet's treatment of Ma'iz ibn Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam prompting the confessor to retract his confession. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
Mustahabb is synonymous with sunnah ghayr muakkadah in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the hadith of Ma'iz ibn Malik recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sunan Abi Dawud. The Prophet (SAW) asked Ma'iz: 'Perhaps you kissed, or squeezed, or looked?'
This hadith is a had (single) narration, but its meaning is supported by the general principle of averting hudud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of suggesting lesser acts indicates the permissibility and desirability of prompting retraction to avoid the hadd. If it were obligatory, the Prophet would have commanded it explicitly.
The wording 'perhaps' shows it is a suggestion, not an interrogation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
All major schools (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) agree that prompting retraction is commendable (mustahabb). There is no valid disagreement.
This is an issue of muttafaq alayh (consensus) in terms of recommendation.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the imam should prompt retraction. There is no tarjih needed as there is no conflict.
The ruling is firmly established from the prophetic practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب للامام ان يلقن المقر الرجوع ويقول له لعلك لمست او قبلت [۲۴۶۱] (۱۸) امام کے لئے مستحب ہے کہ اقرار کرنے والے کو رجوع کی تلقین کرے اور اس سے کہے شاید تم نے چھویا ہوگا یا بوسہ لیا ہوگا۔ جب حضرت ماعز زنا کا اقرار کرنے تشریف لائے تو آپ نے رجوع کی تلقین کرتے ہوئے فرمایا تھا شاید تم نے بوسہ لیا تھا، شاید تم نے بھینچا تھا ، شاید تم نے صرف دیکھا تھا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لما اتى ماعز ابن مالک النبی الله قال له لعلک قبلت او غمزت او نظرت ؟ قال لا ياسول الله (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب هل يقول الامام للمقر لعلک لمست او غمزت ؟ ( ۱۰۰۸ نمبر ۶۸۲۴ را بو داؤد شریف، باب رجم ماعز بن مالک ص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۴۴۲۷ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کے لئے مستحب ہے کہ رجوع کی تلقین کرے۔
It is recommended for the imam to prompt the confessor to retract and say to him: 'Perhaps you touched or kissed.' [Commentary:] It is mustahabb for the imam to prompt the confessor to retract and say to him: 'Perhaps you touched or kissed.' When Ma'iz came to the Prophet (SAW) and confessed, he said: 'Perhaps you kissed, perhaps you squeezed, perhaps you only looked.' The hadith: 'Ibn Abbas said: When Ma'iz ibn Malik came to the Prophet, he said to him: Perhaps you kissed, or squeezed, or looked? He said: No, O Messenger of Allah.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is understood that it is mustahabb for the imam to prompt retraction.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage outlines a sunnah (recommended) act for the imam (ruler or judge) when a person confesses to zina. The imam should gently suggest that the confessor may have done something less than full zina, such as touching or kissing, in order to give the person a chance to retract the confession and avoid the hadd. This is based on the example of the Prophet (SAW) with Ma'iz ibn Malik. The Prophet repeatedly asked Ma'iz if he had only kissed or looked, hoping he would retract. This reflects the general Hanafi principle of averting hadd punishments as much as possible. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory, but it is a commendable practice.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting or suggesting something to someone; here, suggesting retraction to the confessor.
مقر (muqirr): A person who confesses (the confessor).
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an act that is praiseworthy but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wajib
B) Mustahabb
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The imam's prompting is mustahabb, based on the Prophet's treatment of Ma'iz, reflecting the principle of averting hudud.

Retraction of Confession Before Hadd Execution
Ruling on acceptance of retraction before or during hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the acceptance of retraction of a confession to a hadd offense and apply the proof (hadith and athar) to determine when the punishment is dropped.

Core Idea
A retraction of confession before or during hadd drops the punishment in Hanafi fiqh.

In Hanafi law, when a person confesses to a hudud offense like zina, the punishment is normally carried out. However, the school places great emphasis on averting punishments through doubts (shubhat). This lesson examines the ruling that if the confessor retracts before or even during the execution, his retraction is accepted and he is set free.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Retraction of confession; it is accepted and the hadd is dropped.
The ruling applies to any hadd offense where a confession is the basis.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ma'iz (Tirmidhi) and athar of Umar (Ibn Abi Shaybah) are cited.
The hadith is a secondary proof (zanni al-thubut) but decisive in meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement 'Why did you not leave him?' implies that retraction would have been accepted; Umar's giving the option shows the same.
The use of 'perhaps he would repent' indicates retraction is a valid ground for dropping the hadd.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) restrict retraction before evidence, but Hanafi accepts it even after confession and during execution.
The Hanafi position is consistent with the principle that doubts (shubha) avert hudud.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the principle of shubha and is the mufta bihi in the school.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah upholds this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢٤٩٠] (١٧) فأن رجع المقر عن اقراره قبل اقامة الحد عليه او في وسطه قبل رجوعه خلی سبیله
لگیں گے۔ یہ آزاد کی حد زنا سو کوڑے کا آدھا ہے۔
[٢٤٩٠] (١٧) اگر اقرار کرنے والا اپنے اقرار سے رک جائے اس پر حد قائم ہونے سے پہلے یا اس کے درمیان تو اس کا رجوع کرنا قبول کیا جائے گا اور اس کو چھوڑ دیا جائے گا۔
چار مرتبہ اقرار کرنے کی وجہ سے زنا ثابت ہوا تھا۔ حد قائم کرنے سے پہلے یا حد قائم ہونے کے درمیان اپنے اقرار سے رجوع کر
جائے تو اس کا رجوع کرنا قبول کیا جائے گا اور اس کو چھوڑ دیا جائے گا۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ فذكروا ذلک لرسول الله الله انه فرحين وجد مس الحجارة ومس الموت فقال رسول الله هلا تر کنموه (الف) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی در و الحد عن المعترف اذار جمع ص ٢٦٣ نمبر ١٤٢٨) ابو داؤد شریف میں یہ بھی ہے۔ هلا تركتموه لعله ان يتوب فيتوب الله عليه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب رجم ماعزبن مالک ص ٢٥٨، نمبر ٤٤١٩ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تم نے حضرت ماعز کو چھوڑ کیوں نہ دیا۔ اگر وہ توبہ کر لیتے اور اقرار سے رجوع کر لیتے تو اللہ ان کی توبہ قبول کر لیتا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مقرر جوع کرلے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی (٢) اثر میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن شداد ان امرأة رفعت الى عمر اقرت بالزنا اربع مرات فقال ان رجعت لم نقم عليك فقالت لا يجتمع على امران (ب) مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ٢٧ افی الرجل والمرأة يقران بالحد ثم ینکر انہج خامس ص ٥٤٠ نمبر (٢٨٨٢) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اقرار کے بعد انکار کر دے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
If the confessor retracts his confession before the execution of the hadd upon him, or in the middle of it before his retraction, he is released. ... From this hadith it is known that if the confessor retracts, the hadd is dropped. Also in the athar: from Abdullah bin Shaddad that a woman was brought to Umar who confessed to zina four times; he said: 'If you retract, we will not execute the hadd on you.' She said: 'Two matters cannot be combined upon me.' From this athar it is known that if after confession he denies, the hadd is dropped.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The passage states the Hanafi position that if a person confesses to zina (or other hadd offense) and then retracts before the hadd is fully carried out, the retraction is accepted and he is released. This applies even if he retracts during the execution, as long as he hasn't completed the punishment. The proof is from the hadith of Ma'iz where the Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'Why did you not leave him? Perhaps he would repent...' Also an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab where a woman who confessed was given the option to retract, implying the hadd would be dropped. This shows the importance of avoiding punishment where possible. The Hanafi school applies this principle broadly: any doubt (shubha) can avert the hadd, and retraction is considered a shubha.

Key Terms
المقر (al-muqirr): The person who confesses (to a hadd offense)
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Retraction of the confession

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the retraction of a confession to zina accepted?
A) Only before any evidence is presented
B) Only before the hadd execution begins
C) Anytime before or during the hadd execution before it is fully completed
D) It is never accepted after confession

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a retraction of confession anytime before full execution of the hadd is accepted and the punishment is dropped.

Imam Prompting Retraction of Confession (Talqin)
Ruling on mustahabb action with prophetic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on talqin (prompting retraction) for the imam and identify the proof from the hadith of Ma'iz.

Core Idea
The imam should prompt retraction to avoid the hadd—a mercy, not an interrogation.

When someone confesses to a hadd crime like zina, the imam is not required to immediately execute the punishment. The Hanafi school teaches that it is strongly recommended (mustahabb) for the imam to give the confessor a way out by suggesting possible doubts (shubha). This lesson examines the ruling and its primary proof: the Prophet's own treatment of Ma'iz.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage's opening phrase 'ويستحب للامام ان يلقن المقر الرجوع' — what is the hukm level?
The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
2
Locate the textual proof
Find the hadith of Ma'iz cited. What did the Prophet say to him?
The Prophet asked: 'Perhaps you kissed, squeezed, or looked?'
3
Understand the wisdom
Why would the Prophet suggest these doubts? Reflect on the principle of 'averting punishments by doubts' (daf' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat).
Giving a way to retract aligns with the Quranic command to turn away from zina accusations (Quran 24:4).
4
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
The passage hints that this is a Hanafi emphasis. Other schools may not consider it recommended. Think about why.
Hanafis prioritize averting hadd; others may see confession as conclusive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢٤٦١] (١٨) ويستحب للامام ان يلقن المقر الرجوع ويقول له لعلك لمست او قبلت.
لگیں گے۔ یہ آزاد کی حد زنا سو کوڑے کا آدھا ہے۔
[٢٤٦١] (١٨) امام کے لئے مستحب ہے کہ اقرار کرنے والے کو رجوع کی تلقین کرے اور اس سے کہے شاید تم نے چھویا ہوگا یا بوسہ لیا ہوگا۔ جب حضرت ماعز زنا کا اقرار کرنے تشریف لائے تو آپ نے رجوع کی تلقین کرتے ہوئے فرمایا تھا شاید تم نے بوسہ لیا تھا، شاید تم نے بھینچا تھا ، شاید تم نے صرف دیکھا تھا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لما اتى ماعز ابن مالک النبی الله قال له لعلک قبلت او غمزت او نظرت ؟ قال لا ياسول الله (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب هل يقول الامام للمقر لعلک لمست او غمزت ؟ ( ١٠٠٨ نمبر ٦٨٢٤ را بو داؤد شریف، باب رجم ماعز بن مالک ص ٢٦٠ نمبر ٤٤٢٧ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کے لئے مستحب ہے کہ رجوع کی تلقین کرے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) لوگوں نے حضور کے سامنے تذکرہ کیا کہ جب پتھر کی مار پڑی اور موت نظر آئی تو حضرت ماعز بھاگے تو حضور نے فرمایا تم اس کو چھوڑ کیوں نہ دیئے؟ (ب) عبد اللہ بن شداد فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک عورت کا معاملہ حضرت عمر کے پاس لے گئے جس نے چار مرتبہ زنا کا اقرار کیا تو انہوں نے فرمایا اگر تم اقرار سے رجوع کر جاؤ تو تم پر حد جاری نہیں کریں گے۔ تو عورت نے کہا مجھ پر دو معاملے جمع نہیں ہو سکتے (ج) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں جب حضرت مارا حضور کے پاس آئے تو آپ نے ان کو ٹالنے کے لئے کہا شاید بوسہ لیا ہوگا یا بھینچا ہوگا یا دیکھا ہوگا۔ فرمایا نہیں یا رسول اللہ!
It is recommended for the imam to prompt the confessor to retract and say to him: 'Perhaps you touched or kissed.' ... When Ma'iz came to the Prophet, he said to him: 'Perhaps you kissed, or squeezed, or looked?' He said: 'No, O Messenger of Allah.' From this hadith it is known that it is mustahabb for the imam to prompt retraction.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This is a ruling on the recommended (mustahabb) action for the imam. The passage states that the imam should prompt the confessor to retract by suggesting possible shubha (doubt), such as 'perhaps you only touched or kissed.' This is based on the Prophet's (ﷺ) treatment of Ma'iz, where he asked if he had only kissed, squeezed, or looked. The wisdom is to give the confessor an opportunity to retract and thus avert the hadd, as the Prophet preferred to avoid punishments when possible. The Hanafi school emphasizes this as a sunnah (recommended).

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting or suggesting, specifically the imam prompting the confessor to retract
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended or desirable action

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Do you admit to zina?
D) Retract your confession.

Key Takeaway
The imam should prompt retraction of confession (talqin) as a recommended practice (mustahabb) based on the Prophet's example with Ma'iz, to avert hadd punishments.

Master Enforcing Hadd on Slave Requires Imam's Permission
A clear ruling on master's authority over slave for hadd punishments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a master cannot enforce hadd on his slave without the imam's permission and identify the underlying rationale.

Core Idea
Hadd punishments are public authority rights; even a master needs imam's permission.

In the Hanafi school, the master's authority over his slave is not absolute when it comes to criminal punishments. This lesson presents a clear ruling from the matn: the master must obtain the imam's permission before executing a hadd punishment such as flogging for zina. This ensures that punishments prescribed by Allah are carried out by the legitimate public authority, preventing abuse and maintaining justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the master enforcing a hadd punishment (like flogging or stoning) on his male or female slave. The ruling is that it is not permissible (haram) to do so without the imam's permission.
2
Identify the condition
The condition for the master to validly enforce hadd is that he must have explicit permission from the imam (the ruler or his deputy). Without this, the act is unlawful.
3
Understand the rationale
Hadd punishments are considered rights of Allah (haqq Allah) and are part of the public authority. The imam represents the community's interest in executing these punishments uniformly and justly. Allowing private enforcement would lead to chaos and potential injustice.
4
Note the consequence of violation
If a master enforces hadd without permission, his action is sinful (haram) and the punishment may be considered invalid. The slave may also have the right to seek redress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢٤٦٤] (٢١) آقا اپنے غلام اور باندی پر حد قائم نہ کرے مگر امام کی اجازت سے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) قبیلہ جمیلہ کی ایک عورت حضور کے پاس آئی حضور نے حکم دیا کہ اس پر کپڑا باندھ دیا جائے پھر حکم دیا اور رحم کر دی گئی (ب) حضرت حسن بفرماتے ہیں کہ ضمیر تین کی ایک عورت نے زنا کیا۔ پس اس کو لوہے کا لباس پہنایا اور حضرت علی کے پاس لائے تو انہوں نے اس کو کوڑے مارے اس حال میں کہ لباس عورت پر تھا (ج) حضرت غامد یہ حضور کے پاس آئیں. پھر حکم دیا اور اس کے لئے سینے تک گڑھا کھودا اور لوگوں کو حکم دیا پس ان کو رجم کر دیا گیا۔
The master should not enforce the hadd on his male or female slave except with the permission of the imam.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling statement. The master, despite having ownership over his slave, does not have the authority to execute the prescribed hadd punishments (such as flogging for zina) on his own. He must seek permission from the imam (the ruler or his deputy) who has jurisdiction over criminal punishments. The reasoning is that hadd punishments are a right of Allah (haqq Allah) and must be carried out by the public authority to ensure justice and prevent abuse. The footnote provides supporting narrations about the Prophet's and Ali's practices in executing hadd on women, but the core ruling is that the master needs authorization.

Key Terms
السيد (al-sayyid): The master of a slave
الإمام (al-imam): The ruler or his deputy authorized to enforce hadd

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing, the master has full authority
B) The slave's consent
C) The permission of the imam (ruler)
D) A witness

Key Takeaway
The master must obtain the imam's permission before enforcing any hadd punishment on his slave; otherwise the act is haram and invalid.

Equality of Men and Women in Hadd Except for Clothing
Ruling on similarity of hadd for men and women with clothing exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on clothing during hadd for men and women and explain the Hanafi position using the evidence from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Men are stripped, women are clothed: the hadd penalty is equal but the manner differs to preserve modesty.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Saghir addresses a practical aspect of executing the hadd punishment for zina: what clothing should the convict wear? While the penalty itself applies equally to men and women, the manner of execution differs to protect the woman's 'awrah and ensure the effectiveness of the lash. The Hanafi school relies on the precedent of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the practice of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) to establish that a woman must be covered with thin cloth while a man is stripped.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule of equality
The source begins with a statement of equality between men and women in the hadd penalty itself. Understand that the punishment for zina (lashes or stoning) is the same for both genders.
2
Note the exception for women's clothing
The exception states that a woman's clothes are not removed except thick items like fur or padding. This means she must be covered during the execution, unlike a man who is stripped.
3
Examine the evidence for the exception
Two pieces of evidence are cited: the hadith of the Ghamidiyah woman whom the Prophet ordered to be stoned with her clothes tied, and the athar of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib who lashed a woman while she wore an iron garment. Analyze how these proofs indicate the requirement of clothing.
4
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains that a woman's entire body is 'awrah, so must be covered. Thick garments are removed because they would absorb the blow, making the lash ineffective. This shows the balance between modesty and effective punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عورت کا پورا جسم ستر ہے اس لئے پورے جسم پر پتلا کپڑا ہوتا کہ حد لگاتے وقت ستر نہ کھلے۔ اور موٹے کپڑے پر کوڑے کی ضرب نہیں لگے گی اس لئے موٹے کپڑے اتار لئے جائیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت غامدیہ کو رجم کیا تو کپڑا اچھی طرح باندھ دیا۔ روایت ہے۔ عسن
صلى الله
عمران بن حصين ان امرأة من جهينة اتت نبي الله ... فـامـر بها نبي الله الله فشكت عليها ثيابها ثم امر بها فرجمت (الف) ( مسلم شریف، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۶۹۶ار ابو داؤد شریف، باب في المرأة التي امر النبی من برجمها من جھین ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۴۴۴۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت پر کپڑا باندھ کر حد لگائے یار جسم کرے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن الحسن ان امرأة من الضبيريين شنت فالبسها اهلها درعا من حديد فرفعت الى على فضربها وهو عليها (ب)(مصنف ابن ابى هیه ۳۸ فی الزانية والزانی تخلع عنهما شیا بھما او يضربان فيها ؟ ج خامس ص ۴۹۲ نمبر ۲۸۳۱۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کے جسم پر کپڑا ہو اسی حال میں حد لگائے ۔ نت الفرد : پوتین۔ الحشو : موٹا کپڑا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) قبیلہ جمیلہ کی ایک عورت حضور کے پاس آئی حضور نے حکم دیا کہ اس پر کپڑا باندھ دیا جائے پھر حکم دیا اور رحم کر دی گئی (ب) حضرت حسن بفرماتے ہیں کہ ضمیر تین کی ایک عورت نے زنا کیا۔ پس اس کو لوہے کا لباس پہنایا اور حضرت علی کے پاس لائے تو انہوں نے اس کو کوڑے مارے اس حال میں کہ لباس عورت پر تھا
[2422] (19) The man and the woman are equal in that, except that the woman's clothes are not removed except the fur and the padding/stuffing. [2463] (20) And if a pit is dug for her in stoning, it is permissible. [2464] (21) And the master does not execute... Commentary: Talaqin: to prompt, to indicate retraction. Qabbala: kissed. [2422] (19) Man and woman are equal regarding the hadd penalty, except that the woman's clothes will not be removed except the fur coat and thick cloth. In the attributes of hadd and in questioning the man and woman, both are equal in rulings. However, when applying the hadd, the man's body should have no cloth, and the woman's body should have cloth, but not thick cloth or coat etc. The woman's entire body is 'awrah, so thin cloth on the entire body so that the 'awrah is not exposed during hadd. And on thick cloth, the strike of the whip will not be effective, so thick clothes are removed. (2) In hadith: that the Ghamidiyah woman was stoned, and the cloth was tied properly. It is narrated from 'Imran ibn Husayn that a woman from Juhaynah came to the Prophet of Allah... and the Prophet of Allah ordered that her clothes be tightened on her, then ordered her stoning. (a) (Muslim, Bab man i'tarafa 'ala nafsihi bil-zina, p.66 no.1696; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-mar'ah allati amara al-nabi bi-rajmiha min Juhaynah, p.261 no.4440) From this hadith it is understood that the woman should have clothes tied and the hadd applied. There is an athar: from al-Hasan that a woman from the Dabbah tribe committed adultery, so her family put on her an iron coat and she was brought to 'Ali, and he whipped her while she was wearing it. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 38 fi al-zaniyah wa al-zani yukhla'u 'anhuma shay'un bihima aw yudrabana fiha? vol.5 p.492 no.28318) From this athar it is understood that the woman's body should have cloth and in this state the hadd is applied. Al-farw: fur. Al-hashw: thick cloth. Footnote: (a) A woman from the tribe of Juhaynah came to the Prophet, and the Prophet ordered that her clothes be tied, then ordered and she was stoned. (b) al-Hasan says: a woman from the Dabbah tribe committed adultery, so her people put an iron garment on her and brought her to 'Ali, and he lashed her while the garment was on her.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that in the implementation of the hadd punishment for zina, men and women are treated equally in terms of the penalty itself, but there is a difference in the manner of execution regarding clothing. For men, they are stripped of their clothes so that the lashes strike the skin directly. For women, they are not stripped completely; instead, they are required to wear thin clothing that does not prevent the effect of the lash but covers their 'awrah, which is the entire body in the Hanafi school. Thick garments such as fur coats or padded clothing are removed because they would absorb the strike. The ruling is supported by the hadith of the Ghamidiyah woman who was stoned with her clothes tied securely, and by the athar of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) who lashed a woman while she wore an iron garment. This establishes the Hanafi position that a woman must be clothed during the execution of hadd.

Key Terms
الفرو (al-farw): A fur coat or thick outer garment that would impede the effect of lashes.
الحشو (al-hashw): Padded or stuffed clothing that cushions the blow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are a woman's thick clothes (like a fur coat) removed during hadd punishment?
A) To humiliate her more
B) So that the lashes are ineffective
C) So that the lashes strike the body effectively, while still covering the 'awrah with thin cloth
D) Because the hadd is increased for women

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a woman to be clothed during hadd execution, covering her 'awrah, while men are stripped, based on prophetic practice.

Digging a Pit for Stoning a Woman: Preserving Modesty in Execution
Ruling with proof on a procedural detail of rajm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on digging a pit for a woman during rajm and explain the dalil from the Ghamidiyah hadith.

Core Idea
Digging a pit for a woman during stoning is recommended to preserve her dignity, not to punish her further.

The hadd punishment of rajm is severe, but the Prophet's ﷺ practice demonstrated that even punishment must respect human dignity. This lesson examines the ruling on digging a pit for a woman to be stoned—a procedure that shields her 'awrah and shows mercy in the midst of execution. Based on the Ghamidiyah hadith, the Hanafi school considers this a recommended (mustahab) act, not an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is digging a pit for a woman who is to be stoned. The text states it is 'ja'iz' (permissible) and then says it is 'better' (behtar). The hukm level is mustahab (recommended) in Hanafi fiqh.
Ja'iz is a broad term; the preferred interpretation here is mustahab.
2
Understand the underlying wisdom
The reason given is to prevent exposure of the woman's 'awrah during the stoning. Since stones can cause falling or struggling, a pit provides cover for her lower body.
The pit also may help contain the body, but the primary rationale is modesty.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The evidence is the hadith of the Ghamidiyah woman, where the Prophet ﷺ ordered a pit dug up to her chest before stoning. This is a specific action (fi'l) that indicates recommendation (istihbab) in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is reported by Muslim and Abu Dawud; its chain is sound (sahih).
4
Note the Hanafi application
The Hanafi school adopts this practice as mustahab for all women undergoing rajm. The pit should be deep enough to reach the chest, but not more. Digging is not a condition for validity of the punishment.
Opposing views may consider it unnecessary or even problematic, but Hanafi relies on the explicit practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۶۳] (۲۰) اور اگر عورت کے لئے رحم میں گڑھا کھودے تو جائز ہے۔
چونکہ رجم کر کے مار دینا ہے اس لئے ستر نہ کھلے اس لئے گڑھا کھودے اور رحم کرے تو بہتر ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت غامد یہ کور جم کرتے وقت سینے تک گڑھا کھودا ہے ۔ قال فجاءت الغامدية فقالت ... ثم امر بها فحفر لها الى صدرها وامر الناس فرجموها (ج) (مسلم شریف، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۹۹۵) را بو داؤد شریف باب في امرأة التي امر النبی ال برجمها من حميد ه ص ۲۶۱، نمبر ۴۴۴۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کور جم کرتے وقت سینے تک گڑھا کھودا جائے تو بہتر ہے۔
حاشیہ : (ج) حضرت غامد یہ حضور کے پاس آئیں. پھر حکم دیا اور اس کے لئے سینے تک گڑھا کھودا اور لوگوں کو حکم دیا پس ان کو رجم کر دیا گیا۔
[2463] (20) And if a pit is dug for her in stoning, it is permissible. Since stoning is to kill, therefore the 'awrah is not exposed, so digging a pit and stoning is better. In hadith that the Ghamidiyah woman, at the time of stoning, a pit was dug up to her chest. He said: then the Ghamidiyah came and said... then he ordered and a pit was dug for her up to her chest, and he ordered the people and they stoned her. (c) (Muslim, Bab man i'tarafa 'ala nafsihi bil-zina, p.66 no.1995; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-mar'ah allati amara al-nabi bi-rajmiha min Juhaynah, p.261 no.4443) From this hadith it is understood that when stoning a woman, it is better to dig a pit up to the chest. Footnote: (c) The Ghamidiyah woman came to the Prophet, then he ordered and a pit was dug for her up to the chest, and he ordered the people and she was stoned.

Commentary
This passage discusses the manner of stoning a woman. The text states that it is permissible (ja'iz) to dig a pit for the woman to stand in during the stoning, and that doing so is better. The reasoning is to preserve her modesty ('awrah) since falling or struggling might expose her. The proof is the hadith of the Ghamidiyah woman, where the Prophet ﷺ ordered a pit dug up to her chest before stoning her. This is the Hanafi position: it is recommended but not obligatory. The pit should be deep enough to cover her chest, so that her body remains covered until death.

Key Terms
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as the hadd punishment for married adulterers.
الغامدية (al-Ghamidiyyah): A woman from the Ghamid tribe who confessed to adultery and was stoned by the Prophet's ﷺ order, with a pit dug up to her chest.

Master Cannot Execute Hadd on Slave Without Imam's Permission
Inter-madhhab dispute on master's authority to execute hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master's execution of hadd on his slave and explain the proof-based dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Hudud are the ruler's domain — a master cannot punish his slave without the imam's permission.

This passage examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a master may independently execute the hadd punishment on his own slave. The Hanafi school restricts this authority, requiring the imam's permission, while the Shafi'i school allows it. Understanding the proofs and reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to evaluate how different usul principles lead to different fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core question: can a master carry out hadd on his own slave without the imam's permission?
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafi view requires imam's permission; evidence includes the athar from al-Hasan that hudud are for the ruler.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its evidence
The Shafi'i view allows it; evidence includes the hadith commanding flogging of slave women and the action of Fatimah (RA).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut? By arguing that the hadith and athar are either abrogated or restricted to contexts where authority is delegated.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: in a Hanafi jurisdiction, master cannot punish without imam; in Shafi'i, he can.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۶۴] (۲۱) آقا اپنے غلام اور باندی پر حد قائم نہ کرے مگر امام کی اجازت سے۔
غلام یا باندی نے زنا کیا تو آقا خود اس پر حد قائم نہیں کر سکتا۔ ہاں ! امام سے رابطہ کرے وہ فیصلہ کرنے کے بعد آقا کو حد جاری کرنے کا حکم دے تو وہ حد جاری کر سکتا ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ ہر آدمی حد جاری کرے گا تو زیادتی کر سکتا ہے اس لئے امام سوچ بچار کر حد جاری کرے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن عائشة عن الحسن قال اربع الى السلطان الصلوة والزكوة والحدود والقضاء (الف) (مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ۴۸ من قال تدفع الزكوة الى السلطان ج ثانی ص ۳۸۵ نمبر ۲۸۴۲۹/۱۰۱۸۹) اور سنن بیہقی میں ہے۔ حدثنا ابي الزناد عن ابيه عن الفقهاء الذين ينتهى الى قولهم من اهـل الـمـدينة كانوا يقولون لا ينبغي لاحد ان يقيم شيئا من الحدود دون السطان (ب) (سن للبیہقی ۳۶ باب حد الرجل امته اذ ازنت ج ثامن ص ۴۲۸ نمبر ۱۷۱۱۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ قاضی حد قائم کرے۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ آقا اپنے غلام اور باندی پر حد قائم کر سکتا ہے۔
اس لئے کہ وہ مالک ہے۔ اور یہ اس کا مال ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة وزيد بن خالد ان رسول الله سئل عن الامة اذا زنت ولم تحصن قال اذا زنت فاجلدوها ثم ان زنت فاجلدوها ثم ان زنت فاجلدوها ثم يبيعوها ولو بضفير (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا زنت الامته ص ۱۰۱۱ نمبر ۶۸۳۷ ، مسلم شریف، باب رجم الیہود اہل الذمۃ فی الزنا ص ۶۷ نمبر ۱۷۰۳) اس حدیث میں آپ نے آقا سے فرمایا کہ باندی پر حد قائم کرو اس لئے آقا خود حد قائم کر سکتا ہے (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ ان فاطمة بنت رسول الله حدت جارية لها زنت (د) ( من سيبقى ، باب حد الرجل امته اذ زنت ج نامن ص ۲۲۷ نمبر ۷ ۷۱۰ ار مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۳۰ فی الرجل بزنی مملوکہ یقال علیہ الحد ام لا؟ ج خامس ص ۴۸۸ نمبر ۲۸۲۶۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت فاطمہ نے خود اپنی باندی پر حد جاری کی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آقا اپنے غلام اور باندی پر حد قائم کر سکتا ہے۔
[2464] (21) The master should not establish hadd on his male slave or female slave except with the permission of the imam. If a male slave or female slave commits zina, the master himself cannot establish hadd on them. Yes, he should contact the imam; after the imam makes a decision, if he orders the master to carry out the hadd, then he can carry it out, otherwise not. If every person were to carry out hadd, there could be excess, so the imam will deliberate and carry out hadd. (2) There is an athar: from 'A'ishah from al-Hasan that he said: four things are for the ruler: prayer, zakat, hudud, and judiciary. (a) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah; Sunan al-Bayhaqi). And in Sunan al-Bayhaqi: from Abu al-Zinad from his father from the jurists of Madinah that they used to say: it is not proper for anyone to establish any of the hudud without the ruler. (b) From these athar it is understood that the judge establishes hadd. Imam al-Shafi'i says that the master can establish hadd on his male slave and female slave because he is the owner and this is his property. (2) Hadith: from Abu Hurairah and Zayd ibn Khalid that the Messenger of Allah was asked about the female slave if she commits zina and is not muhsan; he said: if she commits zina, then flog her; if she commits zina again, flog her; if she commits zina again, flog her; then sell her even for a rope. (c) (Bukhari, Bab idha zanat al-amah, p.1011 no.6837; Muslim, Bab rajm al-yahud ahl al-dhimmah fi al-zina, p.67 no.1703) In this hadith, he told the master to establish hadd on the female slave, so the master can establish hadd himself. (3) Athar: that Fatimah, daughter of the Messenger of Allah, established hadd on a female slave of hers who committed zina. (d) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) From this athar it is understood that Fatimah herself established hadd on her female slave, indicating that the master can establish hadd on his slave.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the authority to execute the hadd punishment on slaves. The Hanafi position, stated first, is that a master cannot independently execute hadd on his own slave; he must seek permission from the imam (ruler). The evidence is the general principle that hudud are the prerogative of the ruler to prevent chaos and ensure justice. The supporting athar from al-Hasan and the Madinan jurists states that four matters—prayer, zakat, hudud, and judiciary—belong to the ruler. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school. The Shafi'i position, then presented, allows the master to execute hadd directly. Their evidence includes the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ instructed masters to flog their slave women for zina, and the action of Fatimah (may Allah be pleased with her) who flogged her own slave. The passage does not provide a direct Hanafi rebuttal, but the Hanafi position is supported by the general principle that hudud are to be administered by the state to avoid private vendettas. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that the permission of the imam is required.

Key Terms
المولى (al-mawla): The master or owner of a slave.
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes like zina, theft, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The master alone
B) The master with consultation of a scholar
C) The imam (ruler)
D) The slave's family

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, hudud are exclusively the ruler's domain; a master cannot punish his slave without the imam's permission.
