Retraction of Witnesses in Hadd Cases: Before and After Execution
Rulings on retraction of witnesses in hadd cases with Quranic proof and companion practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a witness retracting testimony before and after execution of hadd, and explain the legal consequences including compensation and hadd.

Core Idea
Retraction before execution nullifies the hadd; retraction after execution triggers hadd and partial diyah for the witness.

This passage from the Sharh distinguishes two critical moments in hudud cases: retraction before the punishment is carried out and retraction after. The difference in rulings depends on whether the punishment can be undone. Let us trace the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note that the text explicitly addresses two timelines: retraction before rajm (stoning) and retraction after rajm.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
Before: stoning is dropped, witnesses receive hadd of qadhf. After: only the retracting witness receives hadd and must pay one-fourth diyah.
The hadd is 80 lashes based on Quran 24:4.
3
Trace the dalil (Quranic proof)
The Quran commands flogging for those who accuse chaste women without four witnesses. Retracting witnesses effectively become accusers without sufficient proof.
This is the basis for the hadd of qadhf.
4
Understand the basis for diyah after execution
Since the conviction relied on all four witnesses, retracting one reveals they jointly caused the death. The retractor's share is one-fourth of the full diyah (10,000 dirhams).
The principle of shared responsibility (similar to Ali's judgment in the theft case).
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Imagine four witnesses testify to zina, the convicted person is stoned, then one witness retracts. The retractor is flogged 80 lashes and must pay 2,500 dirhams. The other three witnesses face no penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۲۴۶۵ (۲۲) وان رجع احد الشهود بعد الحكم قبل الرجم ضُر بو الحد وسقط الرجم عن المشهود علیه [۲۴۶۶] (۲۳) وان رجع بعد الرجم حُدَّ الراجع وحده وضمن ربع الدية. تشریح گواہوں کی گواہی کے بعد رجم کا فیصلہ ہوا لیکن رجم کرنے سے پہلے کبھی گواہ یا ایک دو گواہ انکار کر گئے تو رحم ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور جن لوگوں نے گواہی دی تھی ان پر حد قذف لگے گی۔ آیت میں ہے۔ والذين یرمون المحصنات ثم لم يأتوا باربعة شهداء فاجلدوهم ثمانين جلدة (ه) ( آیت ۴ سورۃ النور ) اور چونکہ رجم سے پہلے چار گواہ نہ رہے اس لئے گواہوں کو حد لگے گی (۳) حضرت عمر کے سامنے حضرت ابو بکرہ اور سفیرہ کے سلسلے میں تین گواہ پیش ہوئے اور چوتھے گواہ زیاد نے گواہی دینے سے انکار کیا تو حضرت عمر نے تینوں گواہوں کو حد لگایا۔ [ ۲۴۶۶] (۲۳) اور اگر رجم کے بعد رجوع کیا تو صرف رجوع کرنے والے کو حد لگے گی اور چوتھائی دیت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ چار آدمی کی گواہی سے رجم کیا۔ رجم کے بعد ایک گواہ نے رجوع کر لیا تو جس نے رجوع کیا اس کو حد لگے گی اور اس پر چوتھائی دیت یعنی ڈھائی ہزار درہم کا ضامن ہوگا۔ حد تو اس لئے لگے گی کہ اس نے گویا کہ رجم والے پر تہمت لگائی۔ اور اگر تہمت لگائی اور چار گواہ نہ لا سکے تو اس کو اوپر کی آیت کی وجہ سے حد لگے گی۔ فاجلدوهم ثمانين جلدة (آیت ۴ سورة النور (۲۴) اور چونکہ چار آدمیوں نے مل کر رحم والے کی جان لی ہے اس لئے ایک آدمی پر چوتھائی دیت لازم ہوگی۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشعبي ان رجلين شهدا عند على على رجل بالسرقة فقطع على يده ثم جاء ا بآخر فقالا هذا هو السارق لا الاول فاغرم على الشاهدين دية يد المقطوع الاول وقال لو اعلم انكما تعمدتما لقطعت ايديكما ولم يقطع الثاني (ج)
[2465 (22)] If one of the witnesses retracts after the judgment but before the stoning, then the witnesses are punished with hadd, and the stoning falls from the one testified against. [2466] (23) And if (the witness) retracts after the stoning, then the retracting witness is punished with hadd (alone) and is liable for one-fourth of the blood-money. Explanation: After the testimony of witnesses, the judgment of stoning was issued, but before the stoning some or one or two witnesses recanted, then the stoning is dropped, and those who had given testimony are punished with the hadd of qadhf. The verse says: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes.' (Surah An-Nur, verse 4) And since before stoning there were not four witnesses, therefore the witnesses are punished with hadd. (3) In the presence of Umar, Abu Bakra and Sufira (a case) three witnesses came forward, and the fourth witness Ziyad refused to testify, so Umar punished the three witnesses with hadd. [2466] (23) And if he retracts after the stoning, then only the retracting witness is punished with hadd and is liable for one-fourth of the blood-money. (If) stoning was carried out on the testimony of four men, and after the stoning one witness retracted, then the one who retracted is punished with hadd and is liable for one-fourth of the blood-money, i.e., two thousand five hundred dirhams. The hadd is because he has, as it were, accused the stoned person. And if he accused and could not produce four witnesses, then he is punished with hadd due to the above verse: 'Flog them with eighty lashes.' (Surah An-Nur, verse 4) And since the four persons jointly took the life of the stoned person, one person is liable for one-fourth of the blood-money. There is an athar: from ash-Sha'bi that two men testified before Ali against a man for theft, so Ali cut off his hand. Then two others came and said, 'This is the thief, not the first.' So Ali imposed on the two witnesses the blood-money for the hand of the first man whose hand was cut, and said, 'If I knew that you two did it intentionally, I would cut off your hands, and he did not cut off (the hand of) the second (thief).'
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage deals with the consequences if witnesses in a hadd case (specifically stoning for zina) retract their testimony. It distinguishes between retraction before execution of the punishment and after. Before execution: if one or more witnesses retract, then the number of witnesses falls below four (the required number for stoning), so the punishment is dropped, and the original witnesses are punished with the hadd of qadhf (false accusation) because they effectively accused someone without four witnesses. The proof is the Quranic verse commanding flogging for false accusers. An example is given from the practice of Umar, who flogged three witnesses when the fourth refused to testify. After execution: if a witness retracts after the stoning has been carried out, then only the retracting witness is punished with hadd (again for false accusation), and he must also pay one-fourth of the blood-money (diyah) because he is one of four who caused the death. The reasoning is that he falsely accused, and he shares in taking the life. A supporting athar from Ali is cited: when witnesses to theft retracted after the hand was cut, Ali made them pay the blood-money for the hand, and did not cut the hand of the actual thief. This shows the principle of compensation for erroneous testimony.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction or withdrawal of testimony by a witness.
حد قذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for false accusation of zina, which is 80 lashes.
دية (diyah): Blood-money or financial compensation paid for homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a witness retracts his testimony after the convicted person has already been stoned to death, what happens to the witness according to the Hanafi school?
A) He is not punished because the punishment was already carried out
B) He is punished with hadd of qadhf and must pay one-fourth of the diyah
C) He must pay the full diyah
D) He is executed for causing death

Key Takeaway
A witness who retracts after a hadd punishment has been executed is liable to hadd for false accusation and must pay a proportional share of the diyah.

Witness Retraction in Zina Cases: Rulings Before and After Stoning
Ruling on witness retraction in zina cases with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on witness retraction in zina cases before and after stoning, and explain the Quranic and prophetic proofs that support these rulings.

Core Idea
Witness retraction before stoning drops the hadd from the accused and punishes the witnesses; after stoning, the retractor still faces hadd and must pay diyah.

This lesson examines the critical moment when witnesses in a zina case retract their testimony. The Hanafi school distinguishes between retraction before and after the punishment is carried out. You will learn the precise rulings and the Quranic and prophetic proofs that support them. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the Hanafi approach to hudud and witness accountability.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct situations: retraction before stoning and retraction after stoning. Note the different rulings for each.
2
2. State the ruling for each scenario
Before stoning: witnesses receive hadd (qadhf) and stoning is dropped. After stoning: the retractor alone gets hadd and pays 1/4 diyah.
3
3. Locate the proofs
The passage cites Quranic verses (Surah An-Nur 24:3-4) and athar from Umar and Ali. Identify these proofs.
4
4. Analyze the derivation (wajh al-dalalah)
Explain how the proofs lead to the rulings. For example, the verse requiring four witnesses for zina, and the penalty for false accusation when four are not brought.
5
5. Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Some schools may differ on diyah liability after stoning. The Hanafi position is based on joint liability among witnesses.
Al-Marghinani supports this.

نہیں کاٹا۔
The Hudud chapter. The ruling before stoning: they receive the hadd penalty and stoning falls from the one testified against. [2466] (23) And if he retracts after stoning, the retractor is punished with hadd alone and is liable for one-fourth of the diyah. In this verse: bring four witnesses. And if they do not bring four witnesses, then the witness himself gets the hadd. In the second verse: Why did they not bring four witnesses? So if they do not bring the witnesses, then they are the liars in the sight of Allah. (Surah An-Nur 24:3) This verse also made four witnesses necessary, and if they could not bring them, then the accuser is a liar. And because before stoning, four witnesses were not present, so the witnesses get the hadd. (3) In the presence of Umar, three witnesses came forward regarding Abu Bakrah and Sufayrah, and the fourth witness Ziyad refused to testify, so Umar punished the three witnesses with hadd. He said: He called the witnesses and Abu Bakrah, Shibl ibn Sa'id, and Abu Abdullah Nafi testified. Umar said about him: When these three testified, the matter became difficult for Umar. Then when Ziyad stood, he said: you testify, Allah willing, except with the truth. Ziyad said: As for zina, I do not testify to it, but I have seen an ugly matter. Umar said: Allahu Akbar, punish them with hadd. So they flogged them. (Bayhaqi) In this athar, after the witness's retraction, Umar punished the remaining three witnesses with hadd. [2466] (23) And if he retracts after stoning, then only the retractor gets the hadd and is liable for one-fourth of the diyah. Stoning was done on the testimony of four people. After stoning, one witness retracted, so the one who retracted gets the hadd and is liable for one-fourth of the diyah, i.e., 2500 dirhams. He gets the hadd because he essentially accused the stoned person. And if he accuses and cannot bring four witnesses, then he gets the hadd due to the above verse: flog them eighty lashes (Surah An-Nur 24:4). And because four people together took the life of the stoned person, so one person is liable for one-fourth of the diyah. There is an athar: from al-Sha'bi that two men testified before Ali against a man for theft, so Ali cut off his hand. Then they brought another and said: This is the thief, not the first. So Ali imposed on the two witnesses the diyah of the hand of the first amputee and said: If I knew that you did it intentionally, I would cut off your hands in retaliation, and he did not cut off the second thief's hand. (Bayhaqi) Footnote: So flog him eighty lashes. (a) Why? Because they could not bring four witnesses for the accusation. So since they did not bring witnesses, they are liars in the sight of Allah. (b) Umar called the witnesses, so Abu Bakrah, Shibl ibn Sa'id, and Abu Abdullah Nafi came. So these three came, and Umar said, and it was hard for Umar. Then when Ziyad stood, it was said: you testify, but only with the truth. Ziyad said: I will not testify to zina. However, I have seen a bad affair. So Umar said: Allahu Akbar! Punish these three with hadd. So they flogged them. (c) Ali says that two men testified before Ali against a man for theft, so Ali cut off his hand. Then two others came and said: The thief is the second man, not the first. So Ali imposed on the witnesses the diyah of the first man whose hand was cut off, and said: If I were certain that you did it intentionally, I would cut off your hands in retaliation, and he did not cut off the second thief's hand.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the retraction of witnesses in zina cases. It is a ruling with proof, presenting the Hanafi position on two scenarios: retraction before stoning and after stoning. The matn states that if witnesses retract before stoning, they receive the hadd punishment (eighty lashes for qadhf) and stoning is dropped from the accused. If retraction occurs after stoning, the retracting witness alone is flogged and must pay one-fourth of the diyah (blood money). The commentary supports this with Quranic verses (Surah An-Nur:4 and 24:3-4) and athar from Umar and Ali. The ruling is based on the principle that false accusation (qadhf) without four witnesses is punishable, and that joint liability for the death is divided equally among the witnesses. The hadd is applied to deter false testimony, and the diyah compensates the wrongfully executed person's family.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed, prescribed punishment for specific crimes like zina, qadhf, theft. Here, the hadd for qadhf (false accusation) is eighty lashes.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of testimony by a witness after giving it. In this context, it affects the validity of the punishment.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a person wrongfully killed or injured. Here, one-fourth of the full diyah for a free male (2,500 dirhams).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a witness retracts his testimony after the accused has been stoned, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) No punishment for the witness.
B) The witness is flogged eighty lashes and pays one-fourth of the diyah.
C) The witness is stoned as well.
D) The witness is only flogged forty lashes.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, witness retraction in zina cases before stoning removes the hadd from the accused and imposes it on the witnesses; after stoning, the retractor faces both hadd and diyah.

Punishment for Insufficient Witnesses in Zina Accusations
Ruling that all witnesses are flogged if fewer than four

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when fewer than four witnesses bring a zina accusation, and explain the proof from Quran and athar.

Core Idea
Fewer than four witnesses for zina triggers eighty lashes on the accuser — the same as qadhf.

In Hanafi law, proving zina requires four eyewitnesses. If someone accuses another of zina and brings only three, two, or one witness, all those who testified become liable for the hadd punishment of qadhf. This lesson explores the ruling and its evidence from the Quran and the practice of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the exact legal consequence when the number of witnesses is less than four.
The ruling applies to all witnesses, not just the accuser.
2
Locate the primary proof: Quran 24:4
Recite the verse: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes.' Note the imperative verb 'fajliduhum'.
The verse directly links insufficient witnesses to the hadd punishment.
3
Understand the athar from Qatada
The athar expands the ruling: even if the accuser brings three witnesses, they are flogged unless the fourth completes the set.
This shows the strict application — no partial acceptance.
4
Derive the wisdom (hikmah)
The ruling serves to block the means (sadd al-dhara'i) of false accusations, maintaining the high evidentiary standard for zina.
Without this, people could easily defame others with insufficient proof.

Source Text

وان نقص عدد الشهود عن اربعة حُدُّوا جميعا [۲۴۶۷] (۲۴) اگر چار سے گواہوں کی عدد کم ہو تو سب کو حد لگائی جائے گی۔ حد زنا کے لئے چار گواہ ضروری ہیں۔ لیکن اگر چار سے کم تین یا دو گواہ لا سکے اس سے زیادہ نہ لا سکا تو جن لوگوں نے گواہی دی ہے ان کو حد قذف لگ جائے گی۔ او پر آیت گزر چکی ہے کہ چار گواہ نہ لائے تو گواہوں کو حد قذف لگے گی۔ والذین یرمون المحصنات ثم لم يأتوا باربعة شهداء فاجلدوهم ثمانين جلدة (الف) (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن قتادة في الرجل يقذف الرجل ثم يؤتى بثلاثة يشهدون قال يجلدون ويجلد الا ان يأتي باربعة فان جاء باربعة فشهدوا جميعا اقيم الحد (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الرجل يقذف ويجي بثلاثه ج سابع ص ۳۳۳ نمبر ۱۳۳۷۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ چار گواہ نہ ہوں تو باقی گواہوں کو حد لگ جائے گی تا کہ تہمت لگانے کا سد باب ہو جائے ۔
And if the number of witnesses is less than four, all are punished with hadd. [2467] (24) If the number of witnesses is less than four, all will receive the hadd. For zina, four witnesses are necessary. But if he brings less than four, like three or two, and cannot bring more, then those who testified will be punished with hadd qadhf. The verse has passed that if four witnesses are not brought, then the witnesses get hadd qadhf: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes' (Surah An-Nur 24:4). (a) There is an athar from Qatada about a man who accuses a man and then brings three witnesses: he said, they are flogged and he is flogged, unless he brings four. If he brings four and they all testify together, the hadd is established. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) From this athar, it is understood that if four witnesses are not present, the remaining witnesses get the hadd, so as to block the means of accusation.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof specifying that if fewer than four witnesses testify for zina, all of them are subject to the hadd punishment for qadhf (false accusation). The commentary emphasizes that four witnesses are required for proving zina; lacking that, the testifiers become liable for eighty lashes. The Quranic verse (Surah An-Nur 24:4) is cited as the primary proof, along with an athar from Qatada explaining that even if three witnesses come, they are flogged unless the fourth completes the set. The purpose is to deter false accusations and maintain the strict evidentiary standard for zina.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina. Here, the punishment for qadhf is eighty lashes, applied to witnesses who fail to produce four others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, what happens if a person accuses another of zina and brings only three witnesses?
A) The three witnesses are praised for bringing evidence.
B) The three witnesses are punished with eighty lashes each for qadhf.
C) The accused is stoned based on three witnesses.
D) The matter is dismissed with no punishment.

Key Takeaway
Fewer than four zina witnesses face eighty lashes to uphold the strict evidentiary standard.

Conditions of Ihsan for Stoning
Definition and conditions of ihsan for stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six conditions of ihsan and state the evidence for each, and distinguish the punishment for muhsan vs. non-muhsan.

Core Idea
Stoning only applies if six conditions of ihsan are met — a slave cannot be stoned because half punishment cannot be divided in stoning.

This passage defines the legal concept of ihsan (being muhsan) which determines the hadd punishment for zina. The author enumerates six conditions, each supported by dalil from Quran and Sunnah. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly applying the severe penalty of stoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal concept being defined
Ihsan (محصن) is a technical term in hudud law. Recognize that the passage is defining who qualifies as muhsan for stoning.
Muhsan literally means 'fortified' — here, one who has been fortified against zina through marriage.
2
List each condition
Extract the six conditions: free, adult (baligh), sane (aqil), Muslim, valid marriage (nikah sahih), and consummation (wati') with both spouses being muhsan.
The condition of both spouses having ihsan means both must meet the conditions themselves at the time of intercourse.
3
Note the legal effect
If all conditions are present, the offender is stoned (رجم). If any condition is missing, the punishment is flogging — 100 lashes for free non-muhsan, 50 for slaves.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may define muhsan differently.
4
Examine the proof for freedom
The passage provides two proofs: a hadith ordering only flogging for a slave-girl, and the Quranic verse (An-Nisa 4:25) giving half punishment to slaves, which cannot apply to stoning.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim, establishing that slaves are not muhsan.
5
Understand the consequence
Because stoning is an indivisible punishment, half punishment necessarily refers to flogging. Thus freedom is a necessary condition for ihsan.
This reasoning (half punishment cannot be stoning) is an example of qiyas and textual inference.

[2468] (25) For a person to be muhsan for stoning, it is that (1) he is free, (2) adult, (3) sane, (4) Muslim, (5) he made a valid marriage with a woman, and (6) he had intercourse with her, while both possess the quality of ihsan. For stoning in zina, being muhsan is necessary. If he is not muhsan, the criminal gets one hundred lashes. And if he is a male or female slave, then fifty lashes. So the author wants to state that when six conditions exist, then a person is muhsan. And if any one of them is missing, he will not be muhsan. In that case, he will not be stoned. The proof for each condition is as follows: [1] He is free, because male and female slaves are not muhsan. In a hadith: from Abu Huraira that he heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: 'When a slave-girl commits zina and her zina becomes evident, flog her and do not taunt her; then if she commits zina, flog her and do not taunt her.' (Bukhari and Muslim) In this hadith, flogging is ordered for the slave-girl, not stoning, indicating that freedom is a condition for ihsan. (2) In the verse: 'And if they commit lewdness, then for them is half the punishment of chaste women' (Surah An-Nisa 4:25). This verse states that the slave-girl gets half the punishment, and half cannot be in stoning but can be in flogging. Therefore, Footnote: (a) Those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes. (b) Qatada said: If a man accuses a man and then brings three witnesses, then these three are flogged and he is flogged, unless he brings a fourth. If he brings four and they all testify together, then the hadd is established. (c) The Prophet said: If a slave-girl commits zina and her zina becomes evident, flog her and do not taunt her; then if she commits zina, flog her and do not taunt her. (1) So if a slave-girl commits zina, her punishment is half that of a free chaste woman.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of ihsan (being muhsan) which is a prerequisite for the punishment of stoning in zina. It is a definition-ruling, listing six conditions: free, adult, sane, Muslim, valid marriage, and consummation. The commentary explains that if these conditions are met, the offender is stoned; otherwise, he/she receives flogging (100 lashes for free non-muhsan, 50 for slaves). The proof for freedom includes a hadith that commands only flogging for slave-girls, indicating they are not muhsan. The Quranic verse (An-Nisa 4:25) confirms half punishment for slaves, which is impossible in stoning (since stoning is a single, whole punishment). Thus, the conditions highlight the strictness of the stoning penalty, applicable only to those with high moral and legal status.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who has fulfilled the six conditions making them eligible for stoning punishment for zina.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as a punishment for zina committed by a muhsan person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for ihsan according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Being free.
B) Being male.
C) Being Muslim.
D) Having consummated a valid marriage.

Key Takeaway
Ihsan has six precise conditions; missing any one removes the stoning penalty.

Punishment of Witnesses When Fewer Than Four for Zina
States ruling that witnesses of zina are punished if less than four

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that witnesses of zina are punished with hadd al-qadhf if they are fewer than four, and cite the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
To accuse of zina without four witnesses is qadhf—even the witnesses themselves are lashed eighty times.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle in Islamic criminal law: the requirement of four witnesses for zina. The Quranic verse and a companion tradition (athar) establish that anyone who brings less than four witnesses—including the witnesses themselves—incurs the hadd of false accusation (qadhf). This ruling protects honor and prevents frivolous accusations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of bringing fewer than four witnesses to a zina accusation. The ruling is that all such witnesses are subject to hadd al-qadhf (eighty lashes).
This ruling applies to both the accuser and the witnesses who testify.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse: Surah An-Nur:4. It commands lashing those who accuse chaste women without bringing four witnesses.
The verse is explicit and qat'i al-thubut.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'then do not bring four witnesses' includes cases where some witnesses are brought but not the full four. Thus, even partial testimony triggers the hadd.
The linguistic implication is that the absence of all four witnesses invokes the punishment.
4
Note the supporting athar
Qatada's statement confirms that if a man brings three witnesses, all are flogged unless a fourth is produced. This reinforces the Quranic ruling.
The athar is from Musannaf Abdurrazzaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان نقص عدد الشهود عن اربعة حُدُّوا جميعا (۲۴۶۷) (۲۴) اگر چار سے گواہوں کی عدد کم ہو تو سب کو حد لگائی جائے گی۔ حد زنا کے لئے چار گواہ ضروری ہیں۔ لیکن اگر چار سے کم تین یا دو گواہ لا سکے اس سے زیادہ نہ لا سکا تو جن لوگوں نے گواہی دی ہے ان کو حد قذف لگ جائے گی۔ او پر آیت گزر چکی ہے کہ چار گواہ نہ لائے تو گواہوں کو حد قذف لگے گی۔ والذين یرمون المحصنات ثم لم يأتوا باربعة شهداء فاجلدوهم ثمانين جلدة (الف) (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن قتادة في الرجل يقذف الرجل ثم يؤتى بثلاثة يشهدون قال يجلدون ويجلد الا ان يأتي باربعة فان جاء باربعة فشهدوا جميعا اقيم الحد (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الرجل يقذف ويجي بثلاثه ج سابع ص ۳۳۳ نمبر ۱۳۳۷۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ چار گواہ نہ ہوں تو باقی گواہوں کو حد لگ جائے گی تا کہ تہمت لگانے کا سد باب ہو جائے ۔
And if the number of witnesses is less than four, they are all punished. (2467) (24) If the number of witnesses is less than four, then all are given hadd. For the hadd of zina, four witnesses are necessary. But if he brings less than four, three or two, and cannot bring more, then those who testified are given the hadd of qadhf. The verse has already passed: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses - lash them eighty lashes.' (Surah An-Nur:4). And an athar: from Qatada concerning a man who accuses another man of zina and then brings three witnesses - he said: they are flogged, and he is flogged, unless he brings a fourth. If he brings four and they all testify together, the hadd is established. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, bab al-rajul yaqdhif wa yaji' bi thalathah, vol.7, p.333, no.13376). From this athar it is understood that if there are not four witnesses, the remaining witnesses are given hadd to block the way of accusation.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that if the number of witnesses in a zina case is less than four, then all of those witnesses are punished with the hadd of qadhf (false accusation). The author explains that four witnesses are required for zina. If someone brings only three or two, they cannot bring more, they are guilty of qadhf and receive eighty lashes. The proof is the Quranic verse (Surah An-Nur:4) and an athar from Qatada confirming that if three witnesses come, they are all flogged unless they bring a fourth. This discourages false accusations.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina, punishable by eighty lashes.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes.
شهود (shuhud): Witnesses, specifically for zina cases requiring four male witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) They are ignored.
D) They are punished with tazir.

Key Takeaway
In zina cases, if the required four witnesses are not brought, all those who testified are liable to the hadd of qadhf, eighty lashes.

Conditions of Ihsan and the Dispute over Islam as a Condition
Defines conditions of ihsan and debates condition of Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six Hanafi conditions of ihsan and explain why the Hanafi school requires Islam as a condition for stoning, using proofs from both sides.

Core Idea
Ihsan requires Islam: a non-Muslim adulterer is lashed, not stoned, in Hanafi law.

The punishment for zina depends on whether the offender is muhsan. The Hanafi school defines six conditions for ihsan, including Islam. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing the Prophet's stoning of Jews. This lesson unpacks the conditions and the key dispute.

Guided Path
1
List the six Hanafi conditions of ihsan
Identify all six: free, adult, sane, Muslim, valid marriage, and consummation. Each is required for the offender to be subject to stoning.
The source text lists them at the beginning: 'free, adult, sane, Muslim, has married validly, and has consummated.'
2
Identify the disputed condition
The condition of being Muslim is contested. The Hanafi school insists on it; the Shafi'i school does not.
3
Present the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school cites the hadith: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' This shows that a non-Muslim cannot be muhsan.
The source text quotes this hadith from Ibn Umar via Darqutni.
4
Present the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues from the incident where the Prophet stoned a Jewish man and woman for zina. This indicates that non-Muslims can be stoned, so Islam is not a condition.
The source text cites Bukhari and Muslim on this incident.
5
Explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference affects the punishment of a non-Muslim fornicator: Hanafi says lashes, Shafi'i says stoning if other conditions are met.

Stoning (rajm) is for one who is free, adult, sane, Muslim, has married a woman in a valid marriage, and has consummated with her while both are in the state of ihsan. (Commentary...) It became known that slave men and women are not muhsan, rather being free is a condition of ihsan. [2] The proof for being adult and sane has been mentioned several times: from Ali from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he regains sanity.' (Abu Dawud). Also the hadith of Ma'iz: the Prophet asked him, 'Do you have insanity?' He said no. This shows that sanity and puberty are necessary for ihsan. (4) Being Muslim is a condition for ihsan. A hadith: from Ibn Umar from the Prophet: 'Whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan.' (Darqutni). This shows that a non-Muslim is not muhsan, so if he commits zina, he is lashed, not stoned. Benefit: Imam al-Shafi'i says that being Muslim is not a condition for ihsan. The Jews were stoned. From Ibn Umar: The Prophet brought a Jewish man and woman who had committed zina and stoned them at al-Balat. (Bukhari, Muslim). This shows that a Jew can be stoned, indicating that Islam is not a condition. (5) One has made a valid marriage with a woman and then had intercourse with her; that person becomes muhsan. If he did not have intercourse, even if he married, he is not muhsan. (1) Hadith from Abdullah: The Prophet said: 'It is not permissible to shed the blood of a Muslim who testifies that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah except in one of three cases: the married adulterer, life for life, and the one who leaves his religion and separates from the community.' (Muslim, chapter on...)
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the conditions of ihsan (being muhsan) required for the punishment of stoning (rajm) for zina. The author first lists six conditions: free, adult, sane, Muslim, valid marriage with consummation. Then proofs are given for each. For the condition of being Muslim, the Hanafi school holds that a non-Muslim cannot be muhsan, so if a non-Muslim commits zina, he/she is lashed, not stoned. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the Prophet stoned Jews who committed zina, proving that Islam is not a condition for ihsan. The Hanafi response is not explicitly given here but the text presents the Shafi'i argument. The author then continues with other conditions and proofs.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who has the protection of valid marriage and meets the conditions of freedom, adulthood, sanity, Islam, and consummation, thus subject to stoning for zina.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death, the punishment for a muhsan adulterer.
احصان (ihsan): The state of being muhsan, i.e., having the conditions that make one subject to stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Conditions for Ihsan in the Punishment of Stoning (Rajm)
Explains the five conditions for ihsan and stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for ihsan according to the Hanafi school and explain why each is required, including the evidence and the dispute with Imam Shafi'i.

Core Idea
To be muhsan requires freedom, adulthood, sanity, Islam, a valid marriage, consummation, and a similarly qualified spouse.

In the Hanafi school, stoning (rajm) is only applied to a muhsan person—one who meets a set of strict conditions. This lesson walks through each condition, the textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and the key disagreement with the Shafi'i school over the requirement of Islam. Understanding these conditions determines whether the punishment for zina is stoning or flogging.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five conditions for ihsan
From the passage, list the five conditions: freedom, adulthood and sanity, Islam, valid marriage with consummation, and both parties being muhsan at the time of marriage and intercourse.
2
Examine the proof for each condition
For each condition, locate the hadith or athar cited in the passage. Note which hadith is used for adulthood/sanity (ref al-qalam, hadith of Ma'iz), for Islam (Ibn Umar hadith), for marriage/consummation (hadith of the three who may be killed, case of the slave boy).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah of each proof
Explain how each hadith directly proves the condition. For example, the hadith of Ma'iz shows that sanity is a prerequisite for stoning; the hadith on marriage shows that only a married person can be muhsan.
4
Focus on the dispute over the Islam condition
Identify the Hanafi position (Islam required) and the Shafi'i position (Islam not required). Read the Hanafi response: the stoning of Jews was not because they were muhsan but because of their crime plus altering scripture.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical outcome: a non-Muslim (dhimmī) who commits zina is flogged under Hanafi but stoned under Shafi'i if he is muhsan. This affects how a judge applies the hadd punishment.

بھی پتا چلا کہ باندی اور غلام حصن نہیں ہیں بلکہ آزاد ہونا محصن کی شرط ہے۔ [۲] بالغ اور عاقل ہونے کی دلیل کئی مرتبہ حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ عن علی عن النبی الا الله قال رفع القلم عن ثلاثة عن النائم حتى يستيقظ وعن الصبى حتى يحتلم وعن المجنون حتى يعقل (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی المجون ليسرق او یصیب ص ۲۵۶ نمبر ۴۴۰۳) (۲) حضرت ماعر کی حدیث میں آپ نے با ضابطہ پوچھا ہے کہ کیا ماعز کو جنون تو نہیں ہے؟ لوگوں نے فرمایا نہیں ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ محصن ہونے کے لئے عاقل اور بالغ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ دعاہ النبی اللہ ایک جنون؟ قال لا (ب) ( بخاری شریف باب لا يرجم المجون والجو بیص ۱۰۰۶ نمبر ۶۸۱۵ر مسلم شریف ، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالز نی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۹۹۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا
کہ محصن ہونے کے لئے عاقل بالغ ہونا ضروری ہے۔
(۴) محصن ہونے کے لئے مسلمان ہونا شرط ہے۔

سرح الثميرى الجزء الثالث)
۳۸۰
كتاب الحدود
على صفة الاحصان .
يباح به دم المسلم ص ۵۹ نمبر ۱۶۷۶) اس حدیث میں کہ وہ نکاح شدہ جو زنا کرنے والا ہو وہ قتل کا مستحق ہے۔ جس سے پتا چلا کہ محسن کے لئے نکاح ہونا ضروری ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ ملازم لڑ کا نکاح شدہ نہیں تھا تو اس کو رحم نہیں کیا بلکہ سوکوڑے لگائے ۔حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ انہ سمع أبا هريرة ... وعلى ابنك جلد مائة وتغريب عام (الف ) ( مسلم شریف ، باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنی ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۹۹۷) اس حدیث میں لڑکا غیر شادی شدہ تھا اس لئے اس کو سو کوڑے لگائے رجم نہیں کیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ محصن ہونے کے لئے شادی شدہ ہونا ضروری ہے (۳) اور نکاح صحیح ہو نکاح فاسد سے محسن نہیں ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن عطاء في رجل تزوج بامرأة ثم دخل بها فاذا هي اخته من الرضاعة قال ليس باحصان وقاله معمر عن ف ن قتادة (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب بل یکون النكاح الفاسد احصاناج سابع ص ۳۰۹ نمبر ۱۳۳۰۵) اس اثر میں رضاعی بہن سے شادی کی اور صحبت کی چونکہ یہ نکاح فاسد ہے اس لئے اس شادی اور صحبت سے آدمی محسن نہیں ہوا۔ [1] دونوں کے احسان کی صفت پر صحبت کی ہو۔
اثر میں ہے۔ عن عطاء قال الاحصان ان يجامعها ليس دون ذلك احصان ولا يرجم حتى يشهدوا لرأيناه يغيب في ذلك منها (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب بل تحصن الرجل ولم یدخل ج سامع ص ۳۰۴ نمبر ۱۳۲۷۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ صحبت کرے تب محصن ہو گا صرف شادی کرنے سے محصن نہیں ہوگا۔
[۷] دونوں احصان کی صفت پر ہوں اس حال میں شادی کرے اور صحبت کرے اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہودیہ، نصرانیہ اور باندی سے شادی کرے تو محسن نہیں ہوگا۔ آزاد مسلمان عورت سے شادی کرے تب محصن ہوگا۔
حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن کعب بن مالک انه اراد ان يتزوج يهودية او نصرانية فسأل رسول الله فنهاه عنها وقال انها لا تحصنك (ر)(دار قطنی، کتاب الحدود والدیات ج ثالث ص ۰۸ انمبر ۳۲۶۸ سفن للبیہقی ، باب من قال من اشرک باللہ فلیس محسن ج ثامن ص ۳۷۶ نمبر ۱۶۹۴۱) اس حدیث میں یہودیہ محصنہ نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے شادی کرنے سے آدمی محصن نہیں ہو گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن عطاء قال ليس نكاح الامة باحصان (ه) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب نکاح الامتہ لیس با حصان ج سابع ص ۳۰۶ نمبر ۱۳۲۸۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ باندی سے شادی کرے تو آدمی محسن نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ وہ محصنہ نہیں ہے۔
حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) پر جان کے بدلے جان اور دین کو چھوڑنے والا جو جماعت سے جدا ہونے والا ہو (الف) آپ نے فرمایا تمہارے بیٹے پر سو کوڑے اور ایک سال قید ہے (ب) حضرت عطا فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی آدمی نے کسی عورت سے شادی کی پھر اس سے دہلی کی بعد میں پتا چلا کہ وہ اس کی رضاعی بہن ہے تو اس سے محسن نہیں ہو گا۔ حضرت معمر نے حضرت قتادہ سے بھی یہی بات بیان کی ہے (ج) حضرت عطاء فرماتے ہیں کہ محسن اس وقت بنے گا کہ بیوی سے صحبت کرے اس کے بغیر محصن نہیں ہوگا اور رحم نہیں کیا جائے یہاں تک کہ گواہی دیں کہ ہم نے اس کو دیکھا ہے کہ اس کی شرمگاہ عورت کی شرم گاہ میں غائب ہو گئی ( د ) حضرت کعب بن مالک نے سوچا کہ یہودیہ یا نصرانیہ عورت سے شادی کرے تو حضور سے پوچھا تو آپ نے اس سے منع فرمایا اور فرمایا کہ یہ عورتیں تمہیں محصن نہیں بنا ئیں گی (ہ) حضرت عطانے فرمایا باندی سے نکاح کرنے سے آدمی محصن نہیں ہوتا۔
Book of Hudud. Stoning is for one who is free, adult, sane, Muslim, who married a woman with a valid marriage and had intercourse with her while both [are muhsan]. It became known that slave women and slave men are not muhsan; rather being free is a condition for ihsan. [2] Proof for being adult and sane has been mentioned many times in hadith[...]
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage from Al Sharh Ul Sameri on the conditions of ihsan (being a muhsan) for the punishment of stoning (rajm) in zina. The author explains the five conditions: (1) freedom – a slave is not muhsan; (2) adulthood and sanity – supported by the hadith of raising the pen from three persons (sleeping child, minor, insane) and the hadith of Ma'iz where the Prophet asked if he was insane; (3) Islam – with a Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute; (4) valid marriage and consummation – using hadith that only marriage makes blood halal, and the case of the unmarried slave boy who received lashes; (5) both parties being muhsan at the time of marriage and intercourse – a free Muslim woman is required, not a Jewish, Christian, or slave woman. The passage includes proofs from hadith and athar, and responds to Imam Shafi'i who does not require Islam for ihsan.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, adult, sane, Muslim, married validly, and has consummated the marriage with a similarly qualified spouse.
إحصان (ihsan): The quality of being muhsan; the conditions that make a person liable for stoning if they commit zina.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as punishment for zina committed by a muhsan person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for a person to be considered muhsan for the punishment of stoning?
A) Being free
B) Being a Muslim
C) Being married for the first time with no previous divorce
D) Having consummated the marriage

Key Takeaway
Ihsan (being muhsan) requires five conditions: freedom, adulthood, sanity, Islam, and a valid marriage with consummation where both spouses are muhsan at the time.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Conditions of Ihsan for Hadd Zina
Defines ihsan and lists its conditions with textual evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions of ihsan and apply them to determine whether a person is muhsan in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Ihsan requires valid marriage, consummation, and a free Muslim spouse – all conditions are proven by explicit texts.

The punishment for zina in Islamic law depends on whether the offender is muhsan (married and fulfilling certain conditions) or ghayr muhsan. This passage from Sharh al-Thamiri systematically defines ihsan and lists its conditions using hadith and athar. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the hadd punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal term and its significance
The term ihsan is being defined; it determines whether the punishment for zina is stoning or flogging. First, understand that ihsan is a legal status, not a moral quality.
2
Extract the conditions from the text
Read the passage carefully and list every condition mentioned explicitly. The text states: marriage, valid marriage, consummation, both spouses being free, both spouses being Muslim.
The text uses both hadith (Prophetic) and athar (Companion/Successor) as evidence.
3
Match each condition to its proof
For each condition, identify the specific hadith or athar cited. For example, the need for marriage is proven by the hadith of the slave boy; the need for a valid marriage is proven by the athar of foster-sister marriage; etc.
Note the type of evidence: hadith (Sunna) and athar (qawl sahabi).
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school requires both spouses to be free and Muslim. The Shafi'i school does not require the spouse to be free or Muslim; any valid marriage suffices. This ikhtilaf affects who is considered muhsan.
This ikhtilaf is mentioned in the analytical toolbox and is relevant for comparative fiqh.
5
Apply the conditions to a new scenario
Take a hypothetical case (e.g., a man married to a Kitabiyya, consummated) and determine if he is muhsan. Use the conditions step by step: marriage? valid? consummation? spouse free Muslim? If any condition fails, he is not muhsan.
Practice applying the conditions to real or imagined cases to internalize them.

[۷] دونوں احصان کی صفت پر ہوں اس حال میں شادی کرے اور صحبت کرے اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہودیہ، نصرانیہ اور باندی سے شادی کرے تو محسن نہیں ہوگا۔ آزاد مسلمان عورت سے شادی کرے تب محصن ہوگا۔
حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن کعب بن مالک انه اراد ان يتزوج يهودية او نصرانية فسأل رسول الله فنهاه عنها وقال انها لا تحصنك (ر)(دار قطنی، کتاب الحدود والدیات ج ثالث ص ۰۸ انمبر ۳۲۶۸ سفن للبیہقی ، باب من قال من اشرک باللہ فلیس محسن ج ثامن ص ۳۷۶ نمبر ۱۶۹۴۱) اس حدیث میں یہودیہ محصنہ نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے شادی کرنے سے آدمی محصن نہیں ہو گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن عطاء قال ليس نكاح الامة باحصان (ه) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب نکاح الامتہ لیس با حصان ج سابع ص ۳۰۶ نمبر ۱۳۲۸۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ باندی سے شادی کرے تو آدمی محسن نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ وہ محصنہ نہیں ہے۔
حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) پر جان کے بدلے جان اور دین کو چھوڑنے والا جو جماعت سے جدا ہونے والا ہو (الف) آپ نے فرمایا تمہارے بیٹے پر سو کوڑے اور ایک سال قید ہے (ب) حضرت عطا فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی آدمی نے کسی عورت سے شادی کی پھر اس سے دہلی کی بعد میں پتا چلا کہ وہ اس کی رضاعی بہن ہے تو اس سے محسن نہیں ہو گا۔ حضرت معمر نے حضرت قتادہ سے بھی یہی بات بیان کی ہے (ج) حضرت عطاء فرماتے ہیں کہ محسن اس وقت بنے گا کہ بیوی سے صحبت کرے اس کے بغیر محصن نہیں ہوگا اور رحم نہیں کیا جائے یہاں تک کہ گواہی دیں کہ ہم نے اس کو دیکھا ہے کہ اس کی شرمگاہ عورت کی شرم گاہ میں غائب ہو گئی ( د ) حضرت کعب بن مالک نے سوچا کہ یہودیہ یا نصرانیہ عورت سے شادی کرے تو حضور سے پوچھا تو آپ نے اس سے منع فرمایا اور فرمایا کہ یہ عورتیں تمہیں محصن نہیں بنا ئیں گی (ہ) حضرت عطانے فرمایا باندی سے نکاح کرنے سے آدمی محصن نہیں ہوتا۔
The Third Part of Sharh al-Thamiri
Page 380
Book of Hudud
On the description of ihsan.
The hadith: 'His blood is permissible' (no. 1676) indicates that the married person who commits zina deserves death. From this it is learned that marriage is necessary for ihsan. (2) The hadith that the slave boy was not married, so he was not stoned but flogged one hundred lashes. The hadith portion: 'He heard Abu Huraira... and upon your son one hundred lashes and exile for a year' (Muslim, chapter on confession of zina, p. 66 no. 1997). This hadith shows that the boy was unmarried, so he was flogged one hundred lashes and not stoned, thus marriage is necessary for ihsan. (3) And the marriage must be valid; an invalid marriage does not make one muhsan. The evidence is this athar: 'From Ata regarding a man who married a woman, then had intercourse with her, and she turned out to be his foster sister. He said: This is not ihsan.' And Ma'mar related similarly from Qatada (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on invalid marriage being ihsan, vol. 7, p. 309 no. 13305). In this athar, he married a foster sister and had intercourse; because the marriage was invalid, he did not become muhsan. [1] Both must have had intercourse while in the state of ihsan.
There is an athar: 'From Ata who said: Ihsan is that he has intercourse with her; without that there is no ihsan, and he is not stoned until they testify that they saw him insert [his penis] into her' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on ihsan of a man without entry, vol. 7, p. 304 no. 13276). From this athar it is learned that he becomes muhsan only through intercourse, not merely by marriage.
[7] Both must be in the state of ihsan. That is, one marries and has intercourse. This means that if he marries a Jewish, Christian, or slave woman, he will not become muhsan. He becomes muhsan only if he marries a free Muslim woman.
There is proof in the hadith: 'From Ka'b ibn Malik that he wanted to marry a Jewish or Christian woman, so he asked Allah's Messenger, and he forbade him and said: She will not make you muhsan' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hudud wa al-Diyat, vol. 3, p. 98 no. 3268, and Bayhaqi, chapter on whoever associates partners with Allah is not muhsan, vol. 8, p. 376 no. 16941). This hadith shows that a Jewish woman is not muhsana, so marrying her will not make one muhsan. (2) There is an athar: 'From Ata who said: Marriage to a slave woman is not ihsan' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on marriage to a slave woman not being ihsan, vol. 7, p. 306 no. 13283). From this athar it is learned that if one marries a slave woman, he will not become muhsan, because she is not muhsana.
Footnote: (Continued from previous page) ... (a) He said: Upon your son one hundred lashes and one year of exile. (b) Hadrat Ata says: A man married a woman then had intercourse; later it was found that she was his foster sister, so he does not become muhsan. Hadrat Ma'mar also narrated the same from Hadrat Qatada. (c) Hadrat Ata says: A person becomes muhsan only when he has intercourse with his wife; without it he is not muhsan and is not stoned until they testify that they saw his penis disappear into her vagina. (d) Hadrat Ka'b ibn Malik thought of marrying a Jewish or Christian woman, so he asked the Prophet, and he forbade him and said: These women will not make you muhsan. (e) Hadrat Ata said: Marrying a slave woman does not make one muhsan.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and proof of the conditions for ihsan in the context of hadd zina. The author begins by stating that ihsan is a prerequisite for the punishment of stoning. Using a hadith, he establishes that marriage is necessary: a married adulterer is executed (i.e., stoned), while an unmarried one is flogged. The narration of the slave boy confirms that without marriage, there is no stoning. Next, the marriage must be valid (nikah sahih); an invalid marriage (nikah fasid), like marrying one's foster sister by mistake, does not confer ihsan. This is proven by the athar of Ata. Then, consummation (intercourse) is essential—mere marriage without intercourse does not make one muhsan, as per another athar. Finally, both spouses must enjoy the quality of ihsan: they must be free Muslims. Marrying a Jewish, Christian, or slave woman does not make a man muhsan, supported by the hadith of Ka'b ibn Malik and the athar of Ata. The footnotes reiterate these points. In the Hanafi school, ihsan is defined as being a free, adult, Muslim who has had valid consummated marriage with a free Muslim spouse. These conditions are all derived from the explicit text.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): Here it means the legal status of a married, free, adult Muslim who has consummated the marriage, making stoning the prescribed punishment for zina.
محصن (muhsan): A person who has the quality of ihsan, i.e., meets all conditions for stoning in zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for ihsan?
A) Valid marriage contract
B) Consummation of marriage
C) Spouse must be a free Muslim
D) Spouse must be a virgin

Key Takeaway
Ihsan is a legal status requiring valid marriage, consummation, and a free Muslim spouse, elevating the punishment for zina to stoning.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
The Muhsan is Stoned Only: Hanafi View on Hadd Punishment
states the Hanafi ruling and rebuts a contrary hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school punishes a muhsan with stoning only, identify the primary evidence (Prophetic practice), and evaluate the contrary hadith of Ubadah.

Core Idea
A muhsan is stoned only; flogging is not added. The Prophet's practice overrides a seemingly explicit hadith.

This passage from the chapter on hudud clarifies a key point of Hanafi penal law: for the muhsan (married, free, Muslim adult who has consummated marriage and commits zina), the only fixed punishment is stoning (rajm). The text rejects the combination of flogging (jald) before stoning, a view held by some other schools. It presents both rational and empirical evidence, and confronts a strong counter-hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Start by noting the explicit ruling: 'Flogging and stoning shall not be combined for the muhsan.' This is the central thesis.
The Arabic phrase: ولا يجمع فى المحصن بين الجلد والرجم
2
Examine the rational proof
The text gives a rational argument: since stoning aims at death, flogging beforehand serves no purpose.
This is an istihsan-based reasoning (can be overridden by stronger evidence).
3
Analyze the practical proof
It cites the Prophet's treatment of Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyya, who were only stoned, not flogged.
This is a sunna fi'liyya (practice of the Prophet) that is considered decisive.
4
Address the contrary hadith
The hadith of Ubadah says 'the thayyib (muhsan): one hundred lashes then stoning.' Note the wording 'then' (thumma).
The Hanafi response: this hadith is either abrogated (mansukh) by the practice, or the 'then' indicates sequence of legislation, not obligation to combine.
5
Recognize the practical difference
Hanafis: stoning only; Shafi'is: flogging then stoning. This difference in punishment is the thamarah al-khilaf.
Understanding this ikhtilaf helps in evaluating evidence and tarjih (preference).

Source Text

آدمی محصن ہو تو اس پر رحم ہے اب رجم سے پہلے کوڑا لگایا جائے یا نہیں ؟ تو اس بارے میں یہ ہے کہ صرف رجم کیا جائے گا کوڑا نہیں لگایا جائے گا۔

The Third Part of Sharh al-Thamiri
Page 381
Book of Hudud
2469 (26) And flogging and stoning shall not be combined for the muhsan.
[2470] (27) And flogging and exile shall not be combined for the bikr, unless the imam sees a maslahah in it, then he may exile him as he sees fit.
[2469] (26) Flogging and stoning shall not be combined for the muhsan.
If a person is muhsan, he is to be stoned. Should he be flogged before stoning? In this regard, the ruling is that only stoning will be carried out, not flogging.
Since the purpose is to kill by stoning, what benefit is there in flogging before? (2) Hadrat Ma'iz and Hadrat al-Ghamidiyya were only stoned, not flogged before. Therefore, only stoning will be done.
But Hadrat Ishaq says that the muhsan should be flogged and also stoned.
From Ubadah ibn al-Samit: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Learn from me. Allah has made a way for them. The thayyib (married) with the thayyib: one hundred lashes then stoning. The bikr (virgin) with the bikr: one hundred lashes and exile for a year.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on stoning the married, p. 264 no. 1434). This hadith indicates that the muhsan receives both flogging and stoning.
Footnote: (a) He said: Learn from me. Allah has made a way for them. A married man who commits zina with a married woman: one hundred lashes then stoning. And a virgin man with a virgin woman: one hundred lashes and one year of exile.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its proof. The ruling (numbered 26) clearly states that for a muhsan (a married person who has committed zina), the punishments of flogging and stoning are not combined; only stoning is applied. The commentary provides a rational argument: since stoning is meant to kill, flogging beforehand serves no purpose. It also cites the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with Ma'iz and al-Ghamidiyya, who were only stoned. However, it mentions a contrary view from Hadrat Ishaq, who holds that both should be combined, citing a hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit. This hadith says 'the thayyib (muhsan): one hundred lashes then stoning.' The Hanafi response, implicit in the text, is that this hadith is either abrogated (mansukh) or interpreted differently, and the practice of the Prophet and the Caliphs supports only stoning. The footnote elaborates on the hadith. In Hanafi fiqh, the mufta bihi position is that the muhsan is stoned without prior flogging.

Key Terms
جلد (jald): Here it means flogging as a hadd punishment, specifically 100 lashes.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as punishment for zina when the offender is muhsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for a muhsan in zina?
A) 100 lashes followed by stoning
B) Stoning only
C) Imprisonment for one year
D) Flogging only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a muhsan who commits zina is to be stoned only; flogging is not added because the Prophet's established practice takes precedence over a general hadith.
